The Unity of the Term: Refuting Multiple-Term Theories
Affirming the single term and refuting alternate views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic position that each person has only one fixed term, refuting the views of al-Ka'bi and the philosophers who propose multiple terms.

Core Idea
Every creature has a single, fixed term from God, not multiple terms.

Having established that death is a non-existent decree, the author now addresses the nature of the term (ajal). He firmly states that the term is one, rejecting two alternative views that propose multiple terms: al-Ka'bi's two-term theory for the killed, and the philosophers' distinction between natural and interceptive terms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the unity of the term
Read the Arabic passage that asserts the term is one and refutes al-Ka'bi and the philosophers. Pay attention to the specific claims being rejected.
This is the second half of the source text.
2
Identify al-Ka'bi's view
Al-Ka'bi claimed that a killed person has two terms: one for killing and one for natural death. Understand why this is problematic.
This implies a person could have died naturally if not killed, contradicting divine decree.
3
Identify the philosophers' view
The philosophers claimed a natural term and interceptive terms due to accidents. Understand the rejection of multiple terms.
The Islamic view is that all deaths occur by God's decree at the appointed time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومبنى هذا على أن الموت وجودى، بدليل قوله تعالى : خلق الموت والحياة [الملك: ٢] والأكثرون على أنه عدمى ومعنى خلق الموت : قدره . والأجل واحد لا كما زعم الكعبي ، أن للمقتول أجلين : القتل والموت . وأنه لو لم يقتل لعاش إلى أجله الذي هو الموت. ولا كما زعمت ( الفلاسفة ) أن للحيوان أجلا طبيعيا. وهو وقت موته بتحلل رطوبته وانطفاء حرارته الغريزيتين وآجالا اخترامية - على خلاف مقتضى طبيعته - بحسب الآفات والأمراض.
And the basis of this is that death is existent, as evidenced by His saying, the Most High: 'He created death and life' [Quran 67:2]. And the majority hold that it is non-existent, and the meaning of 'created death' is He decreed it. And the term is one, not as al-Ka'bi claimed: that the killed has two terms: killing and death, and that if he were not killed he would live to his term which is death. And not as the philosophers claimed: that animals have a natural term, which is the time of their death by the dissolution of their moisture and extinguishing of their innate heat, and interceptive terms, contrary to the requirement of their nature, according to afflictions and diseases.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage discusses the metaphysical nature of death and the unity of the term. It begins by stating the basis of the previous discussion (about the killed dying by his term) is whether death is existent (wujudi) or non-existent ('adami). The author notes that some argue death is existent, citing the Quranic verse 'He created death and life' (Surah al-Mulk, 67:2) as evidence that death is created, hence existent. However, the majority (al-aktharun) hold that death is non-existent, and they interpret 'created death' to mean 'decreed it' (qaddarahu), not that it is a created entity.

The author then affirms that the term (ajal) for everyone is one and the same, refuting two alternative views. First, al-Ka'bi (a Mu'tazilite) claimed that the killed person has two terms: the term of killing (i.e., the time he is killed) and the term of death (i.e., the time he would have died naturally). According to him, if he were not killed, he would live until the second term which is death. The author rejects this, insisting the term is one.

Second, the philosophers (al-falasifa) are refuted. They claim that animals have a natural term (ajal tabi'i), which is the time of death caused by the dissolution of their two moistures and extinguishing of their two innate heats (i.e., natural aging). Additionally, they posit 'interceptive terms' (ajal ikhtirami) that occur contrary to the natural requirement, due to accidents and diseases. The author rejects both multiplicity of terms and the philosophical distinction between natural and accidental terms.

Key Terms
الأجل
الكعبي
الأجل الطبيعي
الأجل الاخترامي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that a person can have more than one term, e.g., a natural term and an accidental term.
Correction: Islamic theology teaches that every person has exactly one fixed term known to God, which is when death actually occurs.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Ka'bi claim about a killed person?
A) That the killed person has only one term.
B) That the killed person has two terms: killing and death.
C) That the killed person has no term.
D) That the killed person's term is the same as the natural term.

Key Takeaway
Every creature has a single, divinely determined term, contrary to theories that propose multiple terms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does knowing that your death has a single, unalterable term from God change how you view the risks and dangers in your life? Do you still fear accidents and diseases as if they could cut your life short contrary to God's decree? What would it mean for you to truly internalize that nothing can hasten or delay your appointed term? This week, choose one fear you have about your health or safety and consciously entrust it to God, repeating the truth that your term is one.
?
When you hear of someone dying young or in a tragic accident, do you feel a sense of injustice or randomness? Does this lesson's refutation of multiple terms affect that feeling? How can you use this truth to cultivate greater trust in God's wisdom and decree? Write down one situation in your life where you struggled with accepting God's timing, and commit to surrendering that to Him.
?
If every being has a single, fixed term, then how should that impact your sense of urgency in calling to good and forbidding evil? Does the certainty of your own death motivate or paralyze you? This lesson teaches that no external cause can change your term. How can you live today with the freedom that comes from knowing your time is solely in God's hands, not in the hands of circumstances? Identify one way you will act boldly this week because you believe your term is already determined by God.

The Reality of Grave Torment and Bliss
Taftazani affirms the reality of grave torment and bliss, specifying who experiences each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that grave torment and bliss are real, who experiences each, and why the author emphasises including bliss in the discussion.

Core Idea
Grave torment is for disbelievers and some sinners; bliss is for the obedient, by God's will.

Taftazani affirms both torment and bliss in the grave, correcting the common tendency to only mention torment. He explains that torment is for disbelievers and some disobedient believers, while bliss is for those who obeyed, according to God's knowledge and will. This lesson explores this affirmation and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Read the affirmation
Start with the opening statement that both torment and bliss are true. Notice that the author immediately specifies who experiences each.
The word 'حق' indicates certainty.
2
Distinguish the recipients
Identify that torment is for disbelievers and some sinful believers, but not all. Bliss is for the obedient, as God knows and wills.
This shows God's justice and mercy.
3
Understand the author's preference
The author notes that most books only mention torment because texts about it are more numerous and most grave inhabitants are disbelievers, but including bliss is more complete.
This shows scholarly thoroughness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عذاب القبر ونعيمه حق
وعذاب القبر للكافرين، ولبعض عصاة المؤمنين خص
الله البعض لأن منهم من لا يريد تعالى تعذيبه، فلا يعذب. وتنعيم أهل الطاعة في القبر بما يعلمه الله تعالى، ويريده) وهذا أولى مما وقع فى عامة الكتب من الاقتصار على إثبات عذاب القبر دون تنعيمه، بناء على أن النصوص الواردة فيه أكثر، وعلى أن عامة أهل القبور كفار ،وعصاة، فالتعذيب بالذكر أجدر .

The torment of the grave and its bliss are true. The torment of the grave is for the disbelievers and for some of the disobedient believers; God singled out some because among them are those whom He does not will to torment, so He does not torment them. And the bliss of the obedient in the grave is with what God Most High knows and wills. And this is more appropriate than what occurs in most books of confining [the discussion] to affirming the torment of the grave without its bliss, based on the fact that the texts about it are more numerous, and that most inhabitants of graves are disbelievers and disobedient, so mentioning torment is more worthy. And the questioning of Munkar and Nakir — they are two angels who enter the grave and ask the servant about his Lord, his religion, and his prophet. Al-Sayyid Abu Shuja' said: Indeed, there is questioning for children, and likewise for prophets according to some. (Established) Each of these matters is established by transmitted proofs (1) because they are possible matters about which the truthful one informed, according to what the texts have stated. God Most High said: "The fire, they are exposed to it..." (1) Because it is from the unseen or from metaphysics or what the ancient philosophers say (metaphysics), and this is verified by what God or His Messenger says.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage affirms the reality of grave torment and bliss. The author specifies that torment is for disbelievers and some sinful believers, while bliss is for the obedient, according to God's knowledge and will. He notes that most books only mention torment due to more texts and the majority of graves being disbelievers, but including bliss is more complete. Then he discusses the questioning by the two angels Munkar and Nakir, who ask about Lord, religion, and prophet. He adds a view that children and prophets also undergo questioning. Finally, he states that all these matters are established by transmitted proofs (samʿiyyāt), as they are possible and reported by the truthful one (the Prophet), supported by Quranic texts, citing an incomplete verse about exposure to the fire.

عذاب القبر
نعيم القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think only grave torment is proven, and bliss is not mentioned.
Correction: The author explicitly affirms bliss for the obedient, based on God's knowledge and will, and considers it more complete to include both.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who experiences torment in the grave?
A) All believers
B) All disbelievers and some sinful believers
C) Only disbelievers
D) Only sinful believers

Key Takeaway
Grave torment and bliss are real; torment is for disbelievers and some sinful believers, while bliss is for the obedient, as God wills.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die tonight, based on your current state of obedience, do you honestly believe you would experience grave torment or bliss? What does your answer reveal about your relationship with God?
?
The author says that God may exempt some sinful believers from torment. Does this make you feel complacent or more hopeful? Why, and what does that say about your intentions?
?
Knowing that bliss in the grave is known only to God, does your obedience stem more from love of His reward or fear of punishment? How can you transform your motivation?

The Questioning by Munkar and Nakir and the Proof from Transmitted Evidence
Taftazani describes the questioning by Munkar and Nakir and asserts that it is proven by transmitted evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reality of the questioning by the two angels Munkar and Nakir, the differing views on children and prophets, and that these matters are established by transmitted proofs.

Core Idea
Munkar and Nakir question every soul about Lord, religion, and prophet; it is proven by scripture.

After affirming grave torment and bliss, Taftazani discusses the questioning by the two angels Munkar and Nakir. He mentions that children are also questioned, and some say prophets are as well. He then concludes that all these matters are established by transmitted proofs (samʿiyyāt), being possible events reported by the truthful Prophet and supported by the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read about Munkar and Nakir
Learn that they are two angels who enter the grave and ask the deceased about three things: Lord, religion, and prophet.
This is a core Islamic belief about the afterlife.
2
Consider the exceptions
Notice the additional views: that children are questioned, and according to some, prophets as well. This shows scholarly discussion.
Not all agree on these extensions.
3
Understand the proof category
The author states that these matters are established by 'transmitted proofs' (samʿiyyāt), meaning they are based on revelation, not reason. They are possible and reported by the truthful Prophet.
This categorizes them as matters of faith, not rational deduction.

Punishment and Bliss of the Grave
Affirmation of punishment and bliss in the grave with scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand who experiences punishment and bliss in the grave according to Sunni doctrine.

Core Idea
Grave punishment is for disbelievers and some sinful believers; bliss is for the obedient.

The text affirms that both punishment and bliss in the grave are real. It clarifies that punishment applies not only to disbelievers but also to some sinful believers, while the obedient experience bliss. The author also notes why most books emphasize punishment over bliss.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the categories
The passage presents three categories: punishment for disbelievers, punishment for some sinful believers, and bliss for the obedient. Find each one.
Notice that the author says punishment is 'for the disbelievers, and for some sinful believers'.
3
Reflect on the reason
Ask yourself why the author mentions that most books focus only on punishment. The commentary will help explain the rationale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عذاب القبر ونعيمه حق. وعذاب القبر للكافرين، ولبعض عصاة المؤمنين خص الله البعض لأن منهم من لا يريد تعالى تعذيبه، فلا يعذب. وتنعيم أهل الطاعة في القبر بما يعلمه الله تعالى، ويريده. وهذا أولى مما وقع في عامة الكتب من الاقتصار على إثبات عذاب القبر دون تنعيمه، بناء على أن النصوص الواردة فيه أكثر، وعلى أن عامة أهل القبور كفار وعصاة، فالتعذيب بالذكر أجدر. وسؤال منكر ونكير وهما ملكان يدخلان القبر فيسألان العبد عن ربه وعن دينه وعن نبيه. قال السيد أبو شجاع: إن للصبيان سؤالا، وكذا للأنبياء عند البعض. (ثابت) كل من هذه الأمور ثابت بالدلائل السمعية لأنها أمور ممكنة أخبر بها الصادق على ما نطقت به النصوص. قال الله تعالى: {النار يعرضون عليها غدوا وعشيا ويوم تقوم الساعة أدخلوا آل فرعون أشد العذاب} [غافر: 46] وقال الله تعالى: {أغرقوا فأدخلوا نارا} [نوح: 25] وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: "استنزهوا من البول، فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه". وقال عليه السلام: {يثبت الله الذين آمنوا بالقول الثابت في الحياة الدنيا وفي الآخرة} [إبراهيم: 27] نزلت في عذاب القبر إذا قيل له: من ربك؟ وما دينك؟ ومن نبيك؟ فيقول: ربي الله وديني الإسلام ونبيي محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم. وقال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: "إذا قبر الميت أتاه ملكان أسودان أزرقان عيناهما، يقال لأحدهما منكر والآخر نكير" إلى آخر الحديث. وقال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: "القبر روضة من رياض الجنة أو حفرة من حفر النيران". وبالجملة: الأحاديث الواردة في هذا المعنى، وفي كثير من أحوال الآخرة: متواترة المعنى. وإن لم يبلغ أحادها حد التواتر.
Punishment of the grave and its bliss are true. And the punishment of the grave is for the disbelievers, and for some sinful believers—Allah has specified some because among them are those whom He, exalted, does not will to punish, so He does not punish them. And the bliss of the obedient in the grave is with that which Allah knows and wills. And this is more appropriate than what occurs in most books of limiting [the discussion] to affirming punishment of the grave without its bliss, based on the fact that the texts concerning it are more numerous, and that most inhabitants of graves are disbelievers and sinners, so mentioning punishment is more befitting. And the questioning of Munkar and Nakir—they are two angels who enter the grave and ask the servant about his Lord, his religion, and his prophet. Al-Sayyid Abu Shuja' said: Indeed, for children there is questioning, and likewise for prophets according to some. (It is established) All of these matters are established by transmitted proofs because they are possible matters informed of by the truthful one, as articulated by the texts. Allah Most High said: {The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening, and on the Day the Hour will be established: 'Admit the family of Pharaoh to the severest punishment'} [Ghafir: 46]. And Allah Most High said: {They were drowned and then admitted into a Fire} [Nuh: 25]. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Clean yourselves from urine, for indeed the general punishment of the grave is from it.' And he (peace be upon him) said: {Allah will keep firm those who have believed with the word that stands firm in this world and in the Hereafter} [Ibrahim: 27] was revealed concerning the punishment of the grave when it is said to him: 'Who is your Lord? What is your religion? Who is your prophet?' So he says: 'My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, and my prophet is Muhammad (peace be upon him).' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When the dead is buried, two angels come to him, black with blue eyes, one is called Munkar and the other Nakir' to the end of the hadith. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The grave is either a garden from the gardens of Paradise or a pit from the pits of Hellfire.' In summary: the hadiths narrated on this meaning, and on many conditions of the Hereafter, are mutawatir in meaning, even if each individual hadith does not reach the level of tawatur.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage affirms the reality of punishment and bliss in the grave and the questioning by Munkar and Nakir. It begins by stating that punishment of the grave is true and applies to disbelievers and some sinful believers, while some believers are spared because Allah does not will their punishment. The bliss of the obedient is also affirmed, and the author notes that most books focus only on punishment, but mentioning bliss is more appropriate because most people in graves are disbelievers or sinners. The passage then describes the questioning by the two angels, Munkar and Nakir, who ask about the Lord, religion, and prophet. A marginal note from al-Sayyid Abu Shuja' mentions that children and, according to some, prophets are also questioned. The author emphasizes that all these matters are established by transmitted proofs (dalā'il sam'iyya) because they are possible matters reported by the truthful one (Allah and His messenger). Several Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths are cited as evidence: the verse about Pharaoh's family being exposed to the fire morning and evening, the verse about the drowned being entered into fire, the hadith about cleansing from urine, the verse about Allah keeping the believers firm, the hadith about the two angels, and the hadith that the grave is either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hellfire. The passage concludes by noting that the hadiths on this topic and on many affairs of the Hereafter are mutawatir in meaning, even if individual narrations are not mutawatir. The overall argument is that these eschatological realities are known through revelation, not reason.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
نعيم القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think only disbelievers experience grave punishment.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that punishment is for disbelievers and for some sinful believers.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who experiences punishment in the grave?
A) Only disbelievers
B) Disbelievers and all sinful believers
C) Disbelievers and some sinful believers
D) Only sinful believers

Key Takeaway
Punishment in the grave is for disbelievers and some sinful believers; bliss is for the obedient.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own life, do you see yourself among the obedient who will receive bliss, or among the sinful believers who may face punishment? What does this passage reveal about where you truly stand, and what will you change today to seek Allah's mercy?
?
The passage warns that not all sinful believers escape punishment—Allah wills it for some. Do you take His forgiveness for granted while persisting in sin? How does this specific teaching press you to repent sincerely and not delay?
?
Most books only mention punishment because most graves are sinners. Have you assumed you are safe based on generic teachings? This lesson insists on mentioning bliss for the obedient. Are you living in obedience that gives you hope of bliss, or are you relying on vague hope? Commit: what specific act of obedience will you start today to make sure you are counted among the obedient?

عذاب القبر ونعيمه حق. وعذاب القبر للكافرين، ولبعض عصاة المؤمنين خص الله البعض لأن منهم من لا يريد تعالى تعذيبه، فلا يعذب. وتنعيم أهل الطاعة في القبر بما يعلمه الله تعالى، ويريده. وهذا أولى مما وقع في عامة الكتب من الاقتصار على إثبات عذاب القبر دون تنعيمه، بناء على أن النصوص الواردة فيه أكثر، وعلى أن عامة أهل القبور كفار وعصاة، فالتعذيب بالذكر أجدر. وسؤال منكر ونكير وهما ملكان يدخلان القبر فيسألان العبد عن ربه وعن دينه وعن نبيه. قال السيد أبو شجاع: إن للصبيان سؤالا، وكذا للأنبياء عند البعض. (ثابت) كل من هذه الأمور ثابت بالدلائل السمعية لأنها أمور ممكنة أخبر بها الصادق على ما نطقت به النصوص. قال الله تعالى: {النار يعرضون عليها غدوا وعشيا ويوم تقوم الساعة أدخلوا آل فرعون أشد العذاب} [غافر: 46] وقال الله تعالى: {أغرقوا فأدخلوا نارا} [نوح: 25] وقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: "استنزهوا من البول، فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه". وقال عليه السلام: {يثبت الله الذين آمنوا بالقول الثابت في الحياة الدنيا وفي الآخرة} [إبراهيم: 27] نزلت في عذاب القبر إذا قيل له: من ربك؟ وما دينك؟ ومن نبيك؟ فيقول: ربي الله وديني الإسلام ونبيي محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم. وقال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: "إذا قبر الميت أتاه ملكان أسودان أزرقان عيناهما، يقال لأحدهما منكر والآخر نكير" إلى آخر الحديث. وقال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: "القبر روضة من رياض الجنة أو حفرة من حفر النيران". وبالجملة: الأحاديث الواردة في هذا المعنى، وفي كثير من أحوال الآخرة: متواترة المعنى. وإن لم يبلغ أحادها حد التواتر.
Punishment of the grave and its bliss are true. And the punishment of the grave is for the disbelievers, and for some sinful believers—Allah has specified some because among them are those whom He, exalted, does not will to punish, so He does not punish them. And the bliss of the obedient in the grave is with that which Allah knows and wills. And this is more appropriate than what occurs in most books of limiting [the discussion] to affirming punishment of the grave without its bliss, based on the fact that the texts concerning it are more numerous, and that most inhabitants of graves are disbelievers and sinners, so mentioning punishment is more befitting. And the questioning of Munkar and Nakir—they are two angels who enter the grave and ask the servant about his Lord, his religion, and his prophet. Al-Sayyid Abu Shuja' said: Indeed, for children there is questioning, and likewise for prophets according to some. (It is established) All of these matters are established by transmitted proofs because they are possible matters informed of by the truthful one, as articulated by the texts. Allah Most High said: {The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening, and on the Day the Hour will be established: 'Admit the family of Pharaoh to the severest punishment'} [Ghafir: 46]. And Allah Most High said: {They were drowned and then admitted into a Fire} [Nuh: 25]. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Clean yourselves from urine, for indeed the general punishment of the grave is from it.' And he (peace be upon him) said: {Allah will keep firm those who have believed with the word that stands firm in this world and in the Hereafter} [Ibrahim: 27] was revealed concerning the punishment of the grave when it is said to him: 'Who is your Lord? What is your religion? Who is your prophet?' So he says: 'My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, and my prophet is Muhammad (peace be upon him).' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When the dead is buried, two angels come to him, black with blue eyes, one is called Munkar and the other Nakir' to the end of the hadith. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The grave is either a garden from the gardens of Paradise or a pit from the pits of Hellfire.' In summary: the hadiths narrated on this meaning, and on many conditions of the Hereafter, are mutawatir in meaning, even if each individual hadith does not reach the level of tawatur.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage affirms the reality of punishment and bliss in the grave and the questioning by Munkar and Nakir. It begins by stating that punishment of the grave is true and applies to disbelievers and some sinful believers, while some believers are spared because Allah does not will their punishment. The bliss of the obedient is also affirmed, and the author notes that most books focus only on punishment, but mentioning bliss is more appropriate because most people in graves are disbelievers or sinners. The passage then describes the questioning by the two angels, Munkar and Nakir, who ask about the Lord, religion, and prophet. A marginal note from al-Sayyid Abu Shuja' mentions that children and, according to some, prophets are also questioned. The author emphasizes that all these matters are established by transmitted proofs (dalā'il sam'iyya) because they are possible matters reported by the truthful one (Allah and His messenger). Several Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths are cited as evidence: the verse about Pharaoh's family being exposed to the fire morning and evening, the verse about the drowned being entered into fire, the hadith about cleansing from urine, the verse about Allah keeping the believers firm, the hadith about the two angels, and the hadith that the grave is either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hellfire. The passage concludes by noting that the hadiths on this topic and on many affairs of the Hereafter are mutawatir in meaning, even if individual narrations are not mutawatir. The overall argument is that these eschatological realities are known through revelation, not reason.

Key Terms
منكر ونكير
سؤال القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think children are not questioned in the grave.
Correction: Al-Sayyid Abu Shuja' explicitly states that children are questioned.

Checkpoint
What do the angels Munkar and Nakir ask about?
A) The deceased's age and wealth
B) Their Lord, religion, and prophet
C) Their good and bad deeds
D) The reasons for their death

Key Takeaway
Munkar and Nakir question every deceased person about their Lord, religion, and prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were asked by Munkar and Nakir right now about your Lord, your religion, and your prophet, would your answers come from deep certainty or mere information? What is one thing today that proves you truly live by your answers?
?
The passage teaches that even children are questioned. If you have children or influence young ones, are you preparing them for this reality with the same urgency as you prepare them for school or worldly success? What specific step will you take this week to teach them about their Lord, religion, and prophet?
?
Knowing that prophets are also questioned, how does that affect your view of accountability? If the best of creation are not exempt, what excuse do you have to delay preparing for that moment?

Transmitted Proofs for the Grave's Realities
Citing transmitted proofs and asserting mutawatir meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the realities of the grave are known through transmitted proofs and that the hadiths on this topic are mutawatir in meaning.

Core Idea
The grave's realities are proven by revelation, not reason, and the hadiths on the subject are collectively authentic.

This passage presents the scriptural evidence for the doctrine of the grave, including Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths. It concludes by explaining that the many hadiths on this topic are mutawatir in meaning, providing a strong basis for belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify each proof
The passage cites two Quranic verses and several hadiths. List them and note what each proves.
3
Understand mutawatir meaning
The passage ends by stating that these hadiths are mutawatir in meaning. Ask yourself what that means and why it is important.

Refuting the Denial of Grave Punishment
Objection and answer regarding grave punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Mu'tazila and Rawafid objection that punishing a dead body is impossible by appealing to Allah's ability to create partial life for perception.

Core Idea
Allah can create partial life in the dead body to enable perception of punishment.

Some groups deny punishment of the grave, arguing that a dead body is inanimate and cannot feel. The answer is rooted in Allah's omnipotence: He can create life in parts of the body sufficient for experiencing pain or pleasure. This refutation does not require the soul's return or visible effects, and it is supported by examples of unseen punishment.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection from the Mu'tazila and Rawafid: they argue that a dead body is inanimate (jamād) with no life or perception, so punishing it is impossible. Identify the logical premise and conclusion.
The objection is based on a physicalist assumption about death.
2
Study the answer
The author answers that Allah can create a type of life in some or all parts of the body, enough to perceive pain or pleasure. Note that this does not require full resurrection or visible effects.
The answer relies on Allah's omnipotence (qudra) to do what is rationally possible.
3
Examine the examples
The author gives three cases: drowned, eaten by animals, crucified. In each, punishment can occur even if we do not see it. Reflect on how these strengthen the argument.
These examples show that punishment is not bound by normal physical laws.
4
Reflect on the theological principle
The author concludes by inviting reflection on Allah's wonders and power, implying that such matters are not far-fetched. Appreciate how this refutation upholds the unseen realities of the afterlife.
This connects to the broader Islamic belief in the sam'iyyāt (things known by revelation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنكر عذاب القبر بعض المعتزلة والروافض، لأن الميت جماد لا حياة له ولا إدراك، فتعذيبه محال. والجواب: أنه يجوز أن يخلق الله تعالى في جميع الأجزاء أو في بعضها نوعا من الحياة قدر ما يدرك ألم العذاب أو لذة التنعيم. وهذا لا يستلزم إعادة الروح إلى بدنه ولا أن يتحرك ويضطرب، أو يرى أثر العذاب عليه حتى إن الغريق في الماء أو المأكول في بطون الحيوانات، أو المصلوب في الهواء، يعذب وإن لم نطلع عليه. ومن تأمل في عجائب ملكه تعالى وملكوته وغرائب قدرته وجبروته لم يستبعد أمثال ذلك فضلا عن الاستحالة.
And some of the Mu'tazila and Rawafid denied the punishment of the grave because the dead is an inanimate object with no life or perception, so punishing it is impossible. The answer: It is permissible that Allah Most High creates in all the parts or in some of them a type of life to the extent of perceiving the pain of punishment or the pleasure of bliss. And this does not necessitate the return of the soul to his body, nor that he moves or becomes agitated, or that the effect of punishment is seen upon him, such that even the one drowned in water, or eaten in the bellies of animals, or crucified in the air, is punished even if we do not see it. And whoever reflects on the wonders of His dominion and sovereignty, and the wonders of His power and omnipotence, does not deem such things remote, let alone impossible.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (i'tirāḍ wa jawāb) regarding the punishment of the grave. The objection comes from some Mu'tazila and Rawafid who argue that punishing a dead body is impossible because the dead body is inanimate (jamād), lacking life and perception. The answer is that Allah can create a partial life in some or all parts of the body, sufficient to perceive the pain or pleasure of punishment or bliss. This does not require the full return of the soul or bodily movement or visible effects. Examples are given: a person drowned in water, eaten by animals, or crucified in the air can still be punished even if we do not perceive it. The author then calls the reader to reflect on the wonders of Allah's dominion and power, concluding that such things are not even far-fetched, let alone impossible. The refutation relies on the principle that Allah is omnipotent and can create life anywhere, which is a key kalam argument against the deniers.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الروافض
جزء
حياة
إدراك
ألم
لذة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that punishment of the grave requires the full bodily resurrection and visible signs, such as movement or external effects.
Correction: The author clarifies that Allah can create partial life in the body, enough for perception, without needing the soul's return or visible agitation.

Checkpoint
How does the author answer the objection that a dead body cannot be punished because it has no life or perception?
A) By asserting that the soul remains in the body after death
B) By stating that Allah can create life in some parts of the body to enable perception
C) By arguing that punishment is only spiritual, not physical
D) By denying that the dead are truly dead

Key Takeaway
Grave punishment is possible because Allah can create partial life in the dead body for perception, without requiring full resurrection or visible effects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the grave is real and near, or do you live as if it is a distant theory? What would change in your daily choices if you felt the weight of its reality tonight?
?
The author says that even if your body is scattered or consumed, Allah can still make you perceive punishment. Does this challenge your hidden assumption that death is an end? How does it make you reconsider your current state of heedlessness?
?
Are you among those who reflect on Allah's power until impossible things become possible, or do you let your limited senses dictate what you accept of the unseen? What will you do today to cultivate that reflection?

The Grave as Intermediate State and General Proof
Summarizes the intermediate state of the grave and the general proof for the Hereafter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the general proof for eschatological matters as formulated in classical kalam: they are rationally possible and confirmed by revelation.

Core Idea
Eschatological matters are rationally possible and confirmed by revelation.

This passage from the Sharh al-Aqaid al-Nasafiyyah marks a transition from discussing the grave as an intermediate state to the broader eschatological events. It also provides the foundational proof for all such matters, grounding them in both rational possibility and divine testimony.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once to get a sense of its flow, then read the literal translation. Notice the two parts: the statement about the grave and the proof.
The passage begins with 'واعلم' (and know), signaling an important point.
2
Identify the two parts of the passage
The first part explains why the grave's conditions are treated separately (they are intermediate). The second part gives the proof for all eschatological matters.
3
Understand the proof
The proof is that these matters are rationally possible (mumkināt) and have been reported by the truthful one (Allah). Reflect on why this is sufficient in kalam.
This is a common argument for sam'iyyāt: rational possibility + reliable report.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم: أنه لما كان أحوال القبر مما هو متوسط بين أمر الدنيا والآخرة، أفردها بالذكر، ثم اشتغل ببيان حقيقة الحشر، وتفاصيل ما يتعلق بأمور الآخرة. ودليل الكل: إنها أمور ممكنة أخبر بها الصادق.
And know: Since the conditions of the grave are among what is intermediate between the matter of this world and the Hereafter, he singled them out for mention, then engaged in explaining the reality of the Resurrection and the details of what pertains to the matters of the Hereafter. And the proof for all of it: They are possible matters informed of by the truthful one.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage serves as a transition and summary. The author notes that the conditions of the grave are intermediate between this world and the Hereafter, which is why they were treated separately before moving to the Resurrection and details of the Hereafter. Then the author provides the general proof for all these eschatological matters: they are possible (mumkināt) and have been reported by the truthful one (i.e., Allah through revelation). This is the standard kalam argument for accepting sam'iyyāt: if a matter is rationally possible and comes from a reliable source (revelation), it must be believed. The phrase 'دليل الكل' (the proof for all) encapsulates the methodological principle that underpins belief in all transmitted eschatological doctrines.

Key Terms
أحوال القبر
متوسط
الحشر
أمور الآخرة
ممكنة
الصادق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the proof for eschatological matters is purely rational or empirical.
Correction: The author clarifies that the proof is that these matters are rationally possible and reported by the truthful one (revelation), not that they are necessary or observable.

Checkpoint
What is the general proof given for all eschatological matters, including the grave and the Hereafter?
A) They are necessary truths known by reason
B) They are possible matters informed of by the truthful one
C) They are empirically observed
D) They are unanimously agreed upon by all scholars

Key Takeaway
The belief in all eschatological events is founded on their rational possibility and their being conveyed by truthful revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the grave and the Hereafter are not just theoretical possibilities but certain realities because Allah, the Truthful, has informed you? How does that certainty shape what you did today?
?
The grave is an intermediate state between this world and the next. Have you ever stopped to consider that your life right now is preparing you not for this world alone, but for that waiting chamber? What are you stockpiling for it?
?
If the proof for all eschatological matters rests on their possibility and on the word of the Truthful One, then every time you act as if this world is permanent, you are effectively denying that you believe that report. What one action today can you change to prove that you take that report seriously?

Scriptural Evidence for the Punishment of the Grave
Sanusi cites Qur'anic verses and prophetic hadiths proving the punishment of the grave, noting their collective certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural basis for the punishment of the grave from the Quran and hadith, and the concept of tawatur in meaning.

Core Idea
Multiple revealed proofs collectively establish the reality of grave punishment.

Before addressing those who deny the punishment of the grave, Sanusi first lays out the overwhelming scriptural evidence. He cites explicit Quranic verses and authentic hadiths, then highlights that these reports are mutawatir in meaning—conveying certainty even if individually they are not. Let's examine these proofs as presented by the author.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses
Start by reading the two verses cited: Ghafir 40:46 and Nuh 71:25. Notice how they mention punishment after death but before the Day of Resurrection.
These verses establish that punishment occurs immediately after death, not just on Judgment Day.
2
Examine the hadith proofs
Read the four hadiths: the warning about urine, the interpretation of the 'firm word' verse, the hadith of Munkar and Nakir, and the hadith about the grave being a garden or pit. Each reinforces the reality of grave punishment.
The hadiths cover multiple aspects: causes, the questioning, and the nature of the grave itself.
3
Understand tawatur in meaning
Sanusi states that these hadiths, though individually not mutawatir, are mutawatir in meaning because they all point to the same reality from different angles. Reflect on how this strengthens certainty.
Tawatur in meaning is a key concept in hadith methodology—mass transmission of core content even if wording varies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غُدُوا وَعَشِيًّا وَيَوْمَ تَقُومُ السَّاعَةُ أَدْخِلُوا آلَ فِرْعَونَ أَشَدَّ الْعَذَاب [غافر: ٤٦] وقال الله تعالى: ﴿أُغْرِقُوا فَأُدْخِلُوا نَارًا ﴾ [نوح: ٢٥] وقال النبي استنزهوا من البول، فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه، وقال عليه السلام: قوله تعالى: ﴿يُثَبِّتُ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِالْقَوْلِ الثَّابِتِ فِي الْحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيَا وَفِي الْآخِرَةِ﴾ [إبراهيم: ٢٧] نزلت في عذاب القبر إذا قيل له: من ربك؟ وما دينك؟ ومن نبيك؟ فيقول: ربي الله وديني الإسلام ونبيي محمد عليه السلام. وقال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: «إذا قبر الميت أتاه ملكان أسودان أزرقان عيناهما، يقال لأحدهما منكر والآخر نكير» إلى آخر الحديث. وقال النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: «القبر روضة من رياض الجنة أو حفرة من حفر النيران». وبالجملة: الأحاديث الواردة في هذا المعنى، وفي كثير من أحوال الآخرة: متواترة المعنى، وإن لم يبلغ آحادها حد التواتر. وأنكر عذاب القبر بعض المعتزلة والروافض، لأن الميت جماد لا حياة له ولا إدراك، فتعذيبه محال. والجواب: أنه يجوز أن يخلق الله تعالى في جميع الأجزاء أو في بعضها نوعا من الحياة قدر ما يدرك ألم العذاب أو لذة التنعيم. وهذا لا يستلزم إعادة الروح إلى بدنه ولا أن يتحرك ويضطرب، أو يرى أثر العذاب عليه حتى إن الغريق في الماء أو المأكول في بطون الحيوانات، أو المصلوب في الهواء، يعذب وإن لم نطلع عليه. ومن تأمل في عجائب ملكه تعالى وملكوته وغرائب قدرته وجبروته لم يستبعد أمثال ذلك فضلا عن الاستحالة.
('They are exposed to the Fire morning and evening, and on the Day the Hour will be established: 'Admit the people of Pharaoh to the severest punishment.' [40:46]) And Allah Almighty said: 'They were drowned and then made to enter a Fire.' [71:25] And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Beware of urine, for most of the punishment of the grave is from it.' And he (peace be upon him) said concerning the saying of Allah Almighty: 'Allah confirms those who believe with the firm word in the worldly life and in the Hereafter' [14:27] – it was revealed concerning the punishment of the grave, when it is said to him: 'Who is your Lord? What is your religion? Who is your Prophet?' He says: 'My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, and my Prophet is Muhammad (peace be upon him).' And the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'When the deceased is buried, two black angels with blue eyes come to him; one is called Munkar and the other Nakir' – to the end of the hadith. And the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) said: 'The grave is either a garden from the gardens of Paradise or a pit from the pits of Hell.' In summary: the hadiths reported on this meaning, and on many matters of the Hereafter, are mutawatir in meaning, even if individual hadiths do not reach the level of tawatur. Some Mu'tazila and Rawafid denied the punishment of the grave, because the deceased is an inanimate object with no life or perception, so punishing him is impossible. The answer: It is permissible that Allah Almighty creates in all the parts or in some of them a type of life sufficient to perceive the pain of punishment or the pleasure of bliss. This does not necessitate the return of the soul to his body, nor that he moves and stirs, nor that the effect of punishment is seen upon him; even the drowned in water, the eaten in the stomachs of animals, or the crucified in the air is punished even if we do not perceive it. And whoever reflects on the wonders of His dominion and sovereignty and the marvels of His power and might does not deem such things unlikely, let alone impossible.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the reality of the punishment of the grave and a refutation of those who deny it. The author begins by citing Qur'anic verses: the first from Surah Ghafir (40:46) showing that the people of Pharaoh are exposed to the Fire morning and evening, and the second from Surah Nuh (71:25) indicating that after drowning they were made to enter a Fire. These establish punishment after death before the Day of Resurrection. Then he cites hadiths: the Prophet's warning about urine being a cause of grave punishment, the interpretation of 'firm word' verse as referring to the questioning in the grave, the hadith of Munkar and Nakir, and the hadith that the grave is either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hell. He then states that the hadiths on this topic are mutawatir in meaning, meaning they convey certainty even if each individual hadith is not mutawatir. Next, he mentions that some Mu'tazila and Rawafid deny grave punishment because the dead is insentient. The answer is that Allah can create a partial life in some or all parts of the body sufficient to feel pain or pleasure, without requiring full restoration of the soul or bodily movement. He gives examples: the drowned, the eaten, the crucified – they are punished without apparent signs. Anyone who contemplates Allah's power finds nothing improbable in this.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
متواتر المعنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are the hadiths on the punishment of the grave considered 'mutawatir in meaning'?
A) Each hadith is narrated by so many companions that it is impossible to have agreed upon a lie.
B) Although individual hadiths are not mutawatir, the large number of hadiths on the same meaning collectively conveys certainty.
C) The Quran confirms them, so they are automatically mutawatir.
D) The hadiths have strong chains of narration that reach tawatur individually.

Key Takeaway
The punishment of the grave is firmly established by multiple scriptural proofs that together yield certainty, even though each individual report may not be mass-transmitted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die right now and face Munkar and Nakir, what would your answer be to 'Who is your Lord?' and 'What is your religion?' and 'Who is your Prophet?' Are you truly certain of those answers, or are they just words you repeat?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) warned that neglecting purification from urine is a major cause of grave punishment. What 'small' sin or negligence in your daily worship do you excuse, knowing it could lead to severe consequences in the grave?
?
Sanusi shows that multiple proofs together create certainty. Do you actually live with the certainty (yaqin) that you will be questioned in the grave? If not, what change in your routine will you make today to prepare for that moment?

Refuting Deniers: The Divine Power to Create Partial Life
Sanusi presents the denial of grave punishment by Mu'tazila and Rawafid and refutes it by affirming Allah's ability to create partial life for perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection raised by those who deny the punishment of the grave and the rational response that affirms Allah's power to create perception without full revival.

Core Idea
Allah can create a limited life in the dead to perceive pain, without needing full resurrection.

After presenting the scriptural evidence, Sanusi addresses a theological objection. Some groups deny grave punishment because the dead are insentient. The response is a powerful affirmation of divine omnipotence: Allah can create partial life in the body to experience pain. This lesson unpacks that rebuttal and its implications for understanding God's power.

Guided Path
1
Understand the deniers' argument
Read the passage presenting the Mu'tazila and Rawafid objection. They argue that since the dead are inanimate (جماد) with no life or perception, punishment is impossible.
This is a rationalistic objection based on the apparent insentience of corpses.
2
Learn the counter-argument
Sanusi responds by stating that Allah can create a type of life in all or some parts of the body, sufficient to feel pain or pleasure. Carefully note this: the soul does not need to return fully.
The response relies on Allah's absolute power—nothing is impossible for Him.
3
Reflect on the examples
The passage gives examples: the drowned, the eaten, and the crucified. These are punished without external signs. Consider how these illustrate unseen divine action.
These examples show that punishment can occur without our perception, reinforcing the point.
4
Contemplate divine power
Sanusi concludes that anyone who reflects on Allah's wonders will not find such things improbable. Internalize this as a general principle of kalam.
This is a call to trust in God's omnipotence as a foundation for accepting revealed truths.

Source Text

Definition and Proof of Bodily Resurrection
Sanusi defines resurrection and proves it from Qur'anic texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of resurrection as reassembling original parts and returning souls, and its scriptural proof.

Core Idea
Resurrection is the reassembly of original parts, not a numerical duplicate of the body.

Sanusi begins by defining what resurrection means in Islamic theology. He clarifies that it is not the creation of a new body but the gathering of the original parts that persist throughout life. He then cites decisive Qur'anic verses to affirm its truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of resurrection
Read the Arabic definition of al-ba'th. Note that it involves gathering original parts and returning souls.
The term 'original parts' is crucial for later refutations.
2
Identify the proof from the Qur'an
Sanusi provides two Qur'anic verses. Read them and notice how they assert resurrection directly.
3
Reflect on the necessity of original parts
Consider why Sanusi specifies 'original parts' instead of all parts. This will be important for the next lesson.
This definition avoids the cannibal dilemma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والبعث) وهو أن يبعث الله تعالى الموتى من القبور، بأن يجمع أجزاءهم الأصلية ويعيد الأرواح إليها. (حق) لقوله تعالى: ﴿ثُمَّ إِنَّكُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ تُبْعَثُونَ﴾ [المؤمنون: ١٦] وقوله تعالى: ﴿قُلْ يُحْيِيهَا الَّذِي أَنْشَأَهَا أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ﴾ [يس: ٧٩] إلى غير ذلك من النصوص القاطعة الناطقة بحشر الأجساد. وأنكر الفلاسفة، بناء على امتناع إعادة المعدوم بعينه، وهو مع أنه لا دليل لهم عليه يعتد به غير مضر بالمقصود. لأن مرادنا: أن الله تعالى يجمع الأجزاء الأصلية للإنسان، ويعيد روحه إليه، سواء سمي ذلك إعادة المعدوم بعينه، أو لم يسم. وبهذا يسقط ما قالوا إنه لو أكل إنسان إنسانا، بحيث صار جزءا منه، فتلك الأجزاء إما أن تعاد فيهما، وهو محال، أو في أحدهما، فلا يكون الآخر معادا بجميع أجزائه. وذلك لأن المعاد إنما هو الأجزاء الأصلية الباقية من أول العمر إلى آخره، والأجزاء المأكولة فضلة في الأكل، لا أصلية. (١) هم دائما يقيسون أمور الآخرة على أمور الدنيا ولم يعلموا أن الله على كل شيء قدير.
('Al-Ba'th' (Resurrection): It is that Allah Almighty sends forth the dead from the graves by gathering their original parts and returning the souls to them. (It is true) due to His saying: 'Then indeed you, on the Day of Resurrection, will be raised.' [23:16] And His saying: 'Say: He will revive them who produced them the first time.' [36:79] and other decisive texts which speak of the gathering of bodies. The philosophers denied it, based on the impossibility of returning the non-existent exactly as it was. And this, despite the fact that they have no valid proof for it, does not harm the intended purpose. Because what we mean is: Allah Almighty gathers the original parts of the human and returns his soul to him, whether that is called returning the non-existent exactly as it was or not. And by this, what they said falls: that if a human eats another human such that he becomes a part of him, then those parts are either returned in both, which is impossible, or in one of them, so the other would not be returned with all his parts. That is because what is returned is only the original parts that remain from the beginning of life to its end, while the eaten parts are surplus in eating, not original. (1) They always analogize matters of the Hereafter to matters of this world and do not know that Allah is over all things competent.)
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage defines the resurrection (al-ba'th) and proves it, while refuting the philosophers' objection. The author first defines resurrection as Allah raising the dead from their graves by gathering their original (asliyya) parts and returning the souls to them. He then declares it true, citing Qur'anic verses: 'Then indeed you, on the Day of Resurrection, will be raised' (23:16) and 'Say: He will revive them who produced them the first time' (36:79), along with other decisive texts about bodily gathering. Next, he mentions that the philosophers (al-falasifa) denied resurrection based on the impossibility of 'returning the non-existent exactly as it was' (i'ādat al-ma'dūm bi 'aynihi). The author responds that even if this is impossible, it does not harm the intended meaning because what is meant is not the return of an identical particular body but the gathering of the original parts. The objection about a cannibal eating another person is then addressed: the returned parts are only the original parts that persist throughout life, not the acquired parts from food. The footnote criticizes those who analogize the afterlife to this world, forgetting Allah's omnipotence.

Key Terms
البعث
الأجزاء الأصلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does Allah gather in resurrection?
A) The entire body including all acquired parts.
B) The souls only.
C) The original parts of the dead.
D) A new body from scratch.

Key Takeaway
Resurrection is the reassembly of the original parts of the body with the soul returned to it, proven by explicit Qur'anic verses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe in the resurrection, but do you live with the certainty that every single atom of your body will be gathered and held accountable? What would change in your daily choices if you truly felt that certainty?
?
When you look at a dead body or think of your own death, does the idea of the original parts being reassembled feel more real, or do you subconsciously think it's just a metaphor? What can you do today to strengthen your conviction?
?
If the resurrection is proven by decisive texts like 23:16 and 36:79, why do you still procrastinate preparing for that day? What specific action will you take within the next 48 hours to live with the Hereafter in mind?

Refuting the Philosophers on Resurrection
Sanusi refutes the philosophers' objection and solves the cannibal dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' objection based on 'returning the non-existent' and Sanusi's refutation by redefining resurrection as gathering original parts, including the cannibal dilemma solution.

Core Idea
Resurrection does not require returning an identical 'non-existent' – it is regathering original parts.

Philosophers denied bodily resurrection arguing it is impossible to return something that has ceased to exist identically. Sanusi responds by clarifying that resurrection is not the return of an exact numerical copy but the reassembly of the persisting original parts. He then addresses the cannibal dilemma to show that this definition remains coherent.

Guided Path
1
Understand the philosophers' argument
Read the phrase 'بناء على امتناع إعادة المعدوم بعينه' and its translation. The philosophers claim it's impossible to return a non-existent thing in its exact previous state.
This is a famous argument from Islamic philosophy.
2
See Sanusi's response
Sanusi says this objection does not harm the intended purpose because resurrection is defined as gathering original parts and returning the soul. It need not be called 'returning the non-existent'.
3
Examine the cannibal dilemma
Read the objection about a cannibal eating another person. Sanusi solves it by distinguishing original parts from acquired parts.
Only parts that were with the person from birth to death count as original.
4
Note the footnote on analogy
The footnote criticizes those who analogize the afterlife to this world, forgetting Allah's power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والبعث) وهو أن يبعث الله تعالى الموتى من القبور، بأن يجمع أجزاءهم الأصلية ويعيد الأرواح إليها. (حق) لقوله تعالى: ﴿ثُمَّ إِنَّكُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ تُبْعَثُونَ﴾ [المؤمنون: ١٦] وقوله تعالى: ﴿قُلْ يُحْيِيهَا الَّذِي أَنْشَأَهَا أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ﴾ [يس: ٧٩] إلى غير ذلك من النصوص القاطعة الناطقة بحشر الأجساد. وأنكر الفلاسفة، بناء على امتناع إعادة المعدوم بعينه، وهو مع أنه لا دليل لهم عليه يعتد به غير مضر بالمقصود. لأن مرادنا: أن الله تعالى يجمع الأجزاء الأصلية للإنسان، ويعيد روحه إليه، سواء سمي ذلك إعادة المعدوم بعينه، أو لم يسم. وبهذا يسقط ما قالوا إنه لو أكل إنسان إنسانا، بحيث صار جزءا منه، فتلك الأجزاء إما أن تعاد فيهما، وهو محال، أو في أحدهما، فلا يكون الآخر معادا بجميع أجزائه. وذلك لأن المعاد إنما هو الأجزاء الأصلية الباقية من أول العمر إلى آخره، والأجزاء المأكولة فضلة في الأكل، لا أصلية. (١) هم دائما يقيسون أمور الآخرة على أمور الدنيا ولم يعلموا أن الله على كل شيء قدير.
('Al-Ba'th' (Resurrection): It is that Allah Almighty sends forth the dead from the graves by gathering their original parts and returning the souls to them. (It is true) due to His saying: 'Then indeed you, on the Day of Resurrection, will be raised.' [23:16] And His saying: 'Say: He will revive them who produced them the first time.' [36:79] and other decisive texts which speak of the gathering of bodies. The philosophers denied it, based on the impossibility of returning the non-existent exactly as it was. And this, despite the fact that they have no valid proof for it, does not harm the intended purpose. Because what we mean is: Allah Almighty gathers the original parts of the human and returns his soul to him, whether that is called returning the non-existent exactly as it was or not. And by this, what they said falls: that if a human eats another human such that he becomes a part of him, then those parts are either returned in both, which is impossible, or in one of them, so the other would not be returned with all his parts. That is because what is returned is only the original parts that remain from the beginning of life to its end, while the eaten parts are surplus in eating, not original. (1) They always analogize matters of the Hereafter to matters of this world and do not know that Allah is over all things competent.)
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage defines the resurrection (al-ba'th) and proves it, while refuting the philosophers' objection. The author first defines resurrection as Allah raising the dead from their graves by gathering their original (asliyya) parts and returning the souls to them. He then declares it true, citing Qur'anic verses: 'Then indeed you, on the Day of Resurrection, will be raised' (23:16) and 'Say: He will revive them who produced them the first time' (36:79), along with other decisive texts about bodily gathering. Next, he mentions that the philosophers (al-falasifa) denied resurrection based on the impossibility of 'returning the non-existent exactly as it was' (i'ādat al-ma'dūm bi 'aynihi). The author responds that even if this is impossible, it does not harm the intended meaning because what is meant is not the return of an identical particular body but the gathering of the original parts. The objection about a cannibal eating another person is then addressed: the returned parts are only the original parts that persist throughout life, not the acquired parts from food. The footnote criticizes those who analogize the afterlife to this world, forgetting Allah's omnipotence.

Key Terms
إعادة المعدوم بعينه
الفلاسفة
الأجزاء الأصلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection requires the return of an identical nonexistent entity, which is impossible.
Correction: Resurrection is not the return of an identical nonexistent but the reassembly of persisting original parts, which does not violate logical principles.

Checkpoint
How does Sanusi solve the cannibal dilemma?
A) He says Allah can duplicate the eaten parts.
B) He says the eaten parts are not original parts and are not resurrected.
C) He claims the cannibal's body does not truly incorporate the eaten parts.
D) He denies that cannibalism ever occurs.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' objection fails because resurrection is defined as the reassembly of original parts, not the return of an identical non-existent, and the cannibal dilemma is solved by distinguishing original from acquired parts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Allah can reassemble you from nothing, or do you, like the philosophers, subconsciously limit His power by your own reasoning? What would it take for you to completely surrender that doubt?
?
The philosophers argued from analogy to this world. Where in your life are you assuming that what is impossible for you is impossible for Allah? Identify one situation and commit to utter reliance on His power.
?
Sanusi says the consumed parts are 'surplus' and not original. Reflect on your own body: everything you have ever eaten or absorbed has been a trust from Allah. Will you return it to Him obediently on the Day of Judgment? What part of you—your original self—will you present to Him?

Refuting the Accusation of Tanasukh
Sanusi refutes the accusation of tanasukh by distinguishing original parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the resurrection of the body from its original parts does not constitute reincarnation (tanasukh).

Core Idea
Resurrection from original parts is not reincarnation.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses a common objection: if the resurrected body is not identical to the earthly one, doesn't that imply reincarnation? He responds by clarifying that the new body is created from the same original parts—it is not a soul migrating to a completely different body. This distinction refutes the accusation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the translation to understand the objection and Sanusi's response.
Notice the structure: fain qila / qulna.
2
Identify the objector's reasoning
The objector uses hadith descriptions to argue the second body is different, thus implying tanasukh.
3
Understand Sanusi's key distinction
Sanusi says tanasukh would only follow if the second body were not created from the original parts of the first.
This is the core of his refutation.
4
Consider the terminological dispute
Sanusi notes that even if someone calls it tanasukh, it is a mere dispute over names, not substance.
This shows he is not conceding the point.
5
Reflect on the final statement
The passage ends with a reminder that Allah is powerful over all things, criticizing analogies from this world to the next.
This reinforces the theological principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: هذا قول بالتناسخ، لأن البدن الثاني ليس هو الأول، لما ورد في الحديث من أن أهل الجنة جرد مرد مكحلون، وأن الجهنمي ضرسه مثل جبل أحد. ومن ههنا قال من قال: (ما من مذهب إلا وللتناسخ فيه قدم راسخ). قلنا: إنما يلزم التناسخ لو لم يكن البدن الثاني مخلوقا من الأجزاء الأصلية للبدن الأول، وإن سمي مثل ذلك تناسخا، كان ذلك نزاعا في مجرد الاسم. ولا دليل على استحالة إعادة الروح إلى (١). هم دائما يقيسون أمور الآخرة على أمور الدنيا ولم يعلموا أن الله على كل شيء قدير.
If it is said: This is a statement of reincarnation (tanasukh), because the second body is not the first, as per the hadith that the people of Paradise are beardless, white, with kohl, and that the molar of the hell-dweller is like Mount Uhud. And from this, one said: 'There is no school except that reincarnation has a firm foot in it.' We say: Reincarnation would only be necessary if the second body were not created from the original parts of the first body. And if such is called reincarnation, then it is a dispute over mere terminology. And there is no proof for the impossibility of returning the soul to... (1) They always analogize matters of the Hereafter to matters of this world and do not know that Allah is over all things competent.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer concerning the accusation that the author's view on resurrection implies reincarnation (tanasukh). The objector says: if the second body is not identical to the first (since hadiths describe Paradise dwellers as beardless, etc.), then this view implies reincarnation, which is a doctrine held by various sects. The author answers: reincarnation would only follow if the second body were not created from the original parts of the first body. But since it is created from those parts, it is not a case of a soul moving to a completely different body. If someone still calls it reincarnation, it is a mere dispute over the name. He then states there is no proof that returning the soul is impossible, and ends with a criticism of those who apply worldly analogies to the afterlife, forgetting Allah's power.

Key Terms
التناسخ
البدن الثاني
الأجزاء الأصلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection from original parts is a form of reincarnation (tanasukh).
Correction: Tanasukh requires the soul to move to a body not composed of the original parts; resurrection creates a new body from the same original matter.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what would make the resurrection view entail reincarnation (tanasukh)?
A) If the second body is not created from the original parts of the first body.
B) If the soul returns to a different species.
C) If the person remembers past lives.
D) If the body decays completely.

Key Takeaway
The resurrection of the body from its original parts is not tanasukh; it is a new creation from the same matter, and Allah has power over all things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that Allah will resurrect your body from its very dust, how does that reshape your view of death? What fear about your end do you need to entrust to Him specifically, starting today?
?
Sanusi rebukes those who 'analogize the afterlife to this world.' In what area of your faith have you been guilty of limiting Allah's power by your own worldly expectations? Name one concrete way you can think of His power instead of your limitations this week.
?
The objector in this passage calls the resurrection 'reincarnation' to dismiss it. Have you ever dismissed a truth of Islam because it sounded like something you already rejected? What would it take for you to examine it on its own terms, not through a worldly lens?

Definition and Proof of the Resurrection
Definition and proof of al-ba'th via Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic definition of the resurrection (al-ba'th) and its scriptural proof.

Core Idea
Resurrection is the reassembly of original body parts with their souls.

The author begins by defining the resurrection as a foundational belief established by the Quran and Sunnah. This lesson focuses on that definition and the decisive textual proofs that establish it as true.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic carefully, noting the definition and the two Quranic verses cited as proof.
The verse from al-Mu'minun and Ya-Sin are key.
2
Identify the core components
Notice that resurrection involves gathering 'original parts' and returning souls. Understand what 'original parts' means.
This term will be crucial for later objections.
3
Reflect on the strength of the proof
The author mentions 'decisive texts' (nusoos qati'ah). Consider why he emphasizes this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونطق بها الكتاب والسنة، فتكون ثابتة وصرح بحقيقة كل منها تحقيقا وتوكيدا واعتناء بشانه، فقال: ( والبعث) وهو أن يبعث الله تعالى الموتى من القبور، بأن يجمع أجزاء هم الأصلية ويعيد الأرواح إليها . And the Book and the Sunnah spoke of them, so they are established, and he stated the reality of each one in verification, emphasis, and care for its matter, and said: (And the Resurrection) which is that God Almighty raises the dead from the graves, by gathering their original parts and returning the souls to them. (It is true) because of His saying, the Exalted: 'Then indeed you, on the Day of Resurrection, will be resurrected' [al-Mu'minun: 16], and His saying, the Exalted: 'Say, He will give them life who produced them the first time' [Ya-Sin: 79], and other decisive texts speaking of the gathering of bodies. The philosophers denied it, based on the impossibility of recreating the exact non-existent thing, but it is, despite that, there is no evidence for them worth considering that harms the purpose. Because what we mean is that God Almighty gathers the original parts of a person and returns his soul to him, whether that is called recreating the exact non-existent thing or not. And by this falls what they said, that if a person eats another person, such that he becomes a part of him, then those parts are either returned to both, which is impossible, or to one of them, and the other would not be returned with all his parts. That is because what is returned is only the original parts that remain from the beginning of life to its end, and the eaten parts are surplus in eating, not original (1). Then if it is said: This is a statement of transmigration (tanasukh), because the second body is not the first, due to what came in the hadith that the people of Paradise are beardless, white, with kohl, and that the molar of the Hell-dweller is like Mount Uhud – and from here said whoever said: 'There is no school except that transmigration has a firm foot in it.' We say: Transmigration would only be necessary if the second body were not created from the original parts of the first body, and if such is called transmigration, that is a dispute about the mere name. And there is no proof of the impossibility of returning the soul to (1) They always measure the matters of the Hereafter by the matters of this world and do not know that God is over all things powerful. such a body; rather, proofs are established for its truth, whether it is called transmigration or not.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the resurrection (al-ba'th) with proof and refutation of objections. It begins by stating that the resurrection is the act of God raising the dead from graves by gathering their original body parts and returning their souls. This is proven by Quranic verses (al-Mu'minun 16, Ya-Sin 79) and other decisive texts. Then it addresses the philosophers' denial based on the impossibility of recreating the exact nonexistent thing. The author argues that this objection does not harm the purpose because what is meant is the gathering of the original parts, not the exact same atoms. Then it refutes the cannibalism objection: if one person eats another, the original parts of each remain distinct; only the original parts are resurrected, not the consumed surplus. Then it answers the objection that this implies tanasukh (transmigration of souls). The objection claims the second body is not the first. The answer is that transmigration would only apply if the second body were not created from the first body's original parts; calling it tanasukh is a terminological dispute. There is no proof that God cannot return the soul to such a body; rather, proofs support its truth. The footnote adds that objectors mistakenly measure the afterlife by worldly standards, forgetting God's omnipotence.

الأجزاء الأصلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, what is the resurrection?
A) The soul alone being rewarded or punished.
B) God gathering the original body parts and returning the soul to them.
C) A spiritual rebirth of the soul into a new body.
D) The recreation of the exact same physical atoms.

Key Takeaway
The resurrection is the reassembly of the original body parts and the reunion with the soul, proven by decisive Quranic texts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that your resurrection involves the very same parts that make up your body now. Does this certainty affect how you use these limbs today—your tongue, your hands, your eyes? What would you change if you truly believed that every atom of your body will be brought back to testify?
?
The Quranic proofs for resurrection are decisive (qati'ah). Do you hold that conviction in your heart, or are there whispers of doubt? What specific action can you take today to strengthen your certainty in the resurrection?
?
If your original parts are reassembled and your soul returned, you will face the consequences of what those parts did. Are you ready to stand before Allah with that same body? What is one sin you must repent from before that day arrives?

Refutation of the Philosophers' and Cannibalism Objections
Refutation of two objections: philosophical impossibility and cannibalism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the philosophers' objection based on the impossibility of recreating the nonexistent and the cannibalism argument.

Core Idea
Resurrection concerns original parts, not the exact atoms of the eaten.

Having defined resurrection, the author now addresses two objections: the philosophers' claim that recreating the exact nonexistent is impossible, and the cannibalism paradox. He shows both objections collapse because resurrection only requires gathering the original parts.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage that starts with 'wa ankar al-falasifah' and ends with 'la asliyyah'. Note the two objections.
The footnotes may contain important clarifications.
2
Understand the philosophers' objection
The philosophers argue that recreating the exact non-existent thing is impossible. The author dismisses this due to lack of evidence.
The key move: the author redefines what is meant by 'resurrection'.
3
Examine the cannibalism objection
If one person eats another, whose parts get resurrected? The solution: only the original parts of each person are resurrected, not the consumed surplus.
Original parts are those present from birth to death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The answer is that transmigration would only apply if the second body were not created from the first body's original parts; calling it tanasukh is a terminological dispute. There is no proof that God cannot return the soul to such a body; rather, proofs support its truth. The footnote adds that objectors mistakenly measure the afterlife by worldly standards, forgetting God's omnipotence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection requires recreating the exact same physical atoms, which is impossible after decay or consumption.
Correction: Resurrection only requires gathering the original parts that remain from birth to death; the consumed parts are surplus.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The resurrection of the body involves only the original parts, so neither the philosophers' impossibility argument nor the cannibalism paradox poses a problem.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
When you hear objections to resurrection that seem logical, like the cannibalism argument, do you immediately trust Allah’s promise or do you let the doubt linger? Starting now, commit to one way you will actively strengthen your certainty in the Hereafter.

Refutation of the Transmigration (Tanasukh) Objection
Refutation of the transmigration (tanasukh) objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the resurrection is not a form of transmigration (tanasukh) and how the author refutes that objection.

Core Idea
Resurrection uses original parts of the first body, so it is not tanasukh.

Some critics argued that the resurrection as described implies transmigration of souls (tanasukh), because the second body is not identical to the first. The author responds by clarifying that tanasukh would only apply if the second body were not created from the original parts of the first. He also notes that the objection is merely a terminological dispute.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage starting with 'fa in qeela' to the end, including the footnote. The footnote contains an important reminder about God's power.
2
Understand the tanasukh objection
Critics say resurrection implies tanasukh because the second body is not the first, as per hadith descriptions of Paradise and Hell.
The objection points to differences between earthly and resurrected bodies.
3
Follow the author's answer
The author says tanasukh only applies if the second body is not made from the first body's original parts. Since it is, calling it tanasukh is a name dispute. He also asserts that there is no proof that God cannot return the soul to such a body.
