⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونطق بها الكتاب والسنة، فتكون ثابتة وصرح بحقيقة كل منها تحقيقا وتوكيدا واعتناء بشانه، فقال: ( والبعث) وهو أن يبعث الله تعالى الموتى من القبور، بأن يجمع أجزاء هم الأصلية ويعيد الأرواح إليها . (حق) لقوله تعالى: ﴿ ثُمَّ إِنَّكُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَة تُبْعَثُونَ ) المؤمنون : ١٦] وقوله تعالى: ﴿قُل يُحْيِيهَا الَّذِي أَنشَأَهَا أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ يس : ۷] إلى غير ذلك من النصوص القاطعة الناطقة بحشر الأجساد . وأنكر الفلاسفة ، بناء على امتناع إعادة المعدوم بعينه، وهو مع أنه لا دليل لهم عليه يعتد به غير مضر بالمقصود. لأن مرادنا : أن الله تعالى يجمع الأجزاء الأصلية للإنسان، ويعيد روحه إليه، سواء سمى ذلك إعادة المعدوم بعينه، أو لم يسم . وبهذا يسقط ما قالوا إنه لو أكل إنسان إنسانا، بحيث صار جزءا منه، فتلك الأجزاء إما أن تعاد فيهما، وهو محال، أو في أحدهما ، فلا يكون الآخر ،معادا، بجميع أجزائه . وذلك لأن المعاد إنما هو الأجزاء الأصلية الباقية من أول العمر إلى آخره والأجزاء المأكولة فضلة فى الأكل، لا أصلية (١) . فإن قيل : هذا قول بالتناسخ، لأن البدن الثاني ليس هو الأول، لما ورد فى الحديث من أن أهل الجنة جرد مرد مكحلون وأن الجهنمي ضرسه مثل جبل أحد - ومن ههنا قال من قال : ( ما من مذهب إلا وللتناسخ فيه قدم راسخ . قلنا : إنما يلزم التناسخ لو لم يكن البدن الثاني مخلوقا من الأجزاء الأصلية للبدن الأول، وإن سمى مثل ذلك تناسخا، كان ذلك نزاعا في مجرد الاسم. ولا دليل على استحالة إعادة الروح إلى (۱) هم دائما يقيسون أمور الآخرة على أمور الدنيا ولم يعلموا أن الله على كل شيء قدير. مثل هذا البدن بل الأدلة قائمة على حقيته، سواء سمي تناسخا أم لا .
And the Book and the Sunnah spoke of them, so they are established, and he stated the reality of each one in verification, emphasis, and care for its matter, and said: (And the Resurrection) which is that God Almighty raises the dead from the graves, by gathering their original parts and returning the souls to them. (It is true) because of His saying, the Exalted: 'Then indeed you, on the Day of Resurrection, will be resurrected' [al-Mu'minun: 16], and His saying, the Exalted: 'Say, He will give them life who produced them the first time' [Ya-Sin: 79], and other decisive texts speaking of the gathering of bodies. The philosophers denied it, based on the impossibility of recreating the exact non-existent thing, but it is, despite that, there is no evidence for them worth considering that harms the purpose. Because what we mean is that God Almighty gathers the original parts of a person and returns his soul to him, whether that is called recreating the exact non-existent thing or not. And by this falls what they said, that if a person eats another person, such that he becomes a part of him, then those parts are either returned to both, which is impossible, or to one of them, and the other would not be returned with all his parts. That is because what is returned is only the original parts that remain from the beginning of life to its end, and the eaten parts are surplus in eating, not original (1). Then if it is said: This is a statement of transmigration (tanasukh), because the second body is not the first, due to what came in the hadith that the people of Paradise are beardless, white, with kohl, and that the molar of the Hell-dweller is like Mount Uhud – and from here said whoever said: 'There is no school except that transmigration has a firm foot in it.' We say: Transmigration would only be necessary if the second body were not created from the original parts of the first body, and if such is called transmigration, that is a dispute about the mere name. And there is no proof of the impossibility of returning the soul to (1) They always measure the matters of the Hereafter by the matters of this world and do not know that God is over all things powerful. such a body; rather, proofs are established for its truth, whether it is called transmigration or not.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the resurrection (al-ba'th) with proof and refutation of objections. It begins by stating that the resurrection is the act of God raising the dead from graves by gathering their original body parts and returning their souls. This is proven by Quranic verses (al-Mu'minun 16, Ya-Sin 79) and other decisive texts. Then it addresses the philosophers' denial based on the impossibility of recreating the exact nonexistent thing. The author argues that this objection does not harm the purpose because what is meant is the gathering of the original parts, not the exact same atoms. Then it refutes the cannibalism objection: if one person eats another, the original parts of each remain distinct; only the original parts are resurrected, not the consumed surplus. Then it answers the objection that this implies tanasukh (transmigration of souls). The objection claims the second body is not the first. The answer is that transmigration would only apply if the second body were not created from the first body's original parts; calling it tanasukh is a terminological dispute. There is no proof that God cannot return the soul to such a body; rather, proofs support its truth. The footnote adds that objectors mistakenly measure the afterlife by worldly standards, forgetting God's omnipotence.

Misconception: Resurrection is a form of transmigration (tanasukh) because the resurrected body is not identical to the earthly body.
Correction: Resurrection is not tanasukh because the second body is created from the original parts of the first body.

The Weighing of Deeds (al-Wazn) and Response to Mu'tazila
Definition, proof, and refutation of Mu'tazila objection to weighing deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of the weighing of deeds (al-wazn), its scriptural basis, the nature of the balance, and how the objection of the Mu'tazila is answered.

Core Idea
The weighing of deeds is true, but its modality is beyond reason, and it is the books of deeds that are weighed.

In this lesson, we examine the belief in the weighing of deeds on the Day of Judgment, a tenet derived from the Quran. The author, al-Nasafi, affirms it as true, clarifies what is meant by the balance, and then refutes the rational objections raised by the Mu'tazila. This passage illustrates the interplay between transmitted evidence and rational inquiry in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the overall sense. Notice the key terms and the flow from affirmation to objection to answer.
2
Identify the Quranic proof and definition
The passage begins by citing Quran 7:8 as evidence. Then it defines the balance as that by which the measure of deeds is known, noting that the intellect cannot grasp its modality. This is the core doctrinal claim.
The balance is not necessarily a physical scale as we know it.
3
Understand the Mu'tazila objection
The Mu'tazila argued that deeds are accidents (a'rāḍ) and cannot be recreated and weighed after death, especially since God already knows them. This is a rational objection based on their views on the nature of accidents and divine knowledge.
4
Analyze the two-part response
The author gives two answers: first, hadith indicate that the books (records) of deeds are weighed, resolving the impossibility of weighing accidents; second, even if one concedes that God's actions have purposes (which Ash'aris deny), there may be wisdom hidden from us. Our ignorance does not make the act futile.
The second argument is a concession for the sake of debate.
5
Reflect on the core idea
The core idea is that the weighing is true, but its exact nature is unknown; the hadith clarifies that it is the records that are weighed. This balances transmitted truth with rational limits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( والوزن (حق) لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَالْوَزْنُ يَوْمَئِدِ الْحَقُّ [الأعراف: ۸] والميزان عبارة عما يعرف به كيفية مقادير الأعمال، والعقل قاصر عن إدراك كيفيته . وأنكره المعتزلة لأن الأعمال أعراض، وإن أمكن إعادتها لم يمكن وزنها، لأنها معلومة الله تعالى فوزنها . والجواب : أنه قد ورد في الحديث: أن كتب الأعمال هي التي توزن، فلا إشكال . وعلى تقدير تسليم كون أفعال الله تعالى معللة بالأغراض، لعل فى الوزن حكم لا تطلع عليها، وعدم اطلاعنا على الحكمة، لا توجب العبث .
(And the weighing (is true) because of His saying, the Exalted: 'And the weighing on that Day is the truth' [al-A'raf: 8]. And the balance is an expression for that by which the measure of deeds is known, and the intellect is incapable of perceiving its modality. And the Mu'tazila denied it because deeds are accidents, and even if their recreation were possible, they could not be weighed, because they are known to God Almighty, so their weighing [is unnecessary]. And the answer: It has come in the hadith that the books of deeds are what are weighed, so there is no problem. And on the assumption of conceding that God's actions are based on purposes, perhaps in the weighing there is a wisdom we do not perceive, and our lack of knowledge of the wisdom does not entail futility.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage defines the weighing of deeds (al-wazn) as true, citing Quran 7:8. The balance is described as that by which the measure of deeds is known; its modality is beyond reason. The Mu'tazila objected because deeds are accidents and cannot be weighed. The answer is that the hadith specifies that the books (records) of deeds are weighed, removing the difficulty. Even if one concedes that God's actions have purposes (which the Ash'aris deny), there may be a wisdom we do not perceive; our ignorance does not make the action futile.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the weighing is a literal weighing of physical deeds or objects, and that its modality is fully comprehensible by reason.
Correction: The weighing is true, but its modality is unknown to the intellect; the hadith indicates that it is the books of deeds that are weighed.

Checkpoint

B) He says the hadith indicates that the books of deeds are weighed.
C) He denies that deeds are accidents.
D) He claims the scale is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The weighing of deeds is true, and the hadith clarifies that the books of deeds are weighed, resolving the rational objection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Book of Deeds and Its Distribution
Definition of the book recording deeds and its giving to believers and disbelievers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Book of Deeds is a real record given physically to believers in their right hands and to disbelievers in their left hands and behind their backs, as proven by the Quran.

Core Idea
The Book of Deeds is literally given to each person on Judgment Day.

In this passage, Sanusi explains the nature of the Book of Deeds—a real record of all human actions. He then specifies how it will be distributed: to believers on the right and to disbelievers on the left and behind. This teaching is grounded in explicit Quranic verses, affirming that the book is a tangible reality, not a metaphor.

The proof is based on the literal meaning of the verses.

The Weighing of Deeds (Al-Wazn) is True
Sanusi affirms weighing, defines balance, and refutes Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni affirmation of the weighing of deeds, the definition of the balance, and the refutation of the Mu'tazila objection.

Core Idea
The weighing of deeds is real, though its modality is beyond reason, and it is the books of deeds that are weighed.

This lesson addresses a sam'iyyat topic: the weighing of deeds on the Day of Judgment. Sanusi affirms it with Qur'an and defines the balance, then presents and answers the Mu'tazila denial. Understanding this refutation clarifies how Allah's justice operates without human limitations.

Guided Path
1
Read the affirmation and definition
Start by reading the opening lines where Sanusi affirms weighing and defines al-mizan. Notice the Qur'anic proof and the note about the intellect's incapacity.
The definition uses 'عبارة عما يعرف به' — an expression for that by which something is known.
2
Examine the Mu'tazila objection
The Mu'tazila argued that actions are accidents and cannot be weighed. Consider why they thought this undermines the concept. They also claimed it is unnecessary since Allah already knows.
The objection is based on philosophical premises about accidents.
3
Understand the two-part answer
Sanusi gives two responses: first, the hadith says books of deeds are weighed, not the actions directly. Second, even if we concede that Allah's acts have purposes, there may be unknown wisdom in the weighing.
The second response uses a principle: lack of knowledge of wisdom does not imply futility.

(And the weighing (is true) due to His statement, the Most High: 'And the weighing on that day is the truth' [al-A'raf: 8]. And the balance (al-mizan) is an expression for that by which the measure of actions is known, and the intellect is incapable of comprehending its modality. Commentary
This passage is a proof-and-refutation unit. The author first affirms that the weighing (al-wazn) of deeds on the Day of Judgment is true, citing Qur'an 7:8. He defines the balance (al-mizan) as the instrument by which the measures of deeds are known, and notes that reason cannot grasp its modality. Then he presents the objection of the Mu'tazila: actions are accidents (a'rad), and even if Allah were to recreate them, weighing them is impossible because they are known to Allah, so weighing them is superfluous. The answer is given: the hadith states that it is the books of deeds that are weighed, not the actions directly, thus removing the difficulty. Moreover, even if one concedes that Allah's actions have purposes, there may be a wisdom in the weighing that we do not know; our ignorance does not make it futile.

?
The modality of the scale is beyond reason—yet you will stand before it. Are you living as if that day is certain? What would you change if you knew the weighing was tomorrow?

The Book of Deeds is True
Sanusi affirms the book of deeds, its distribution, and refutes the Mu'tazila claim of futility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni affirmation of the book of deeds, how it is distributed to believers and disbelievers on Judgment Day, and the refutation of the Mu'tazila charge of futility.

Core Idea
The book of deeds is a literal, undeniable record of every action, given to each person on Judgment Day.

In this lesson, we explore the doctrine of the kitab (book) in which all human deeds are recorded. Imam al-Nasafi affirms its reality and describes how it will be presented to believers and disbelievers. He cites two Qur'anic verses as proof and notes that the Mu'tazila rejected this doctrine as pointless. The passage shows how Sunni theology grounds eschatological events in revelation and addresses rational objections.

Guided Path
1

The passage also includes an author's note and a refutation.

The answer refers to a previous argument about the scales.

Commentary
This passage is a statement of belief with proof and refutation. The author affirms that the book (al-kitab) in which all deeds are recorded is true. It is given to believers in their right hands, and to disbelievers in their left hands or behind their backs. The proof is from Qur'an 17:13 and 84:7-8. The author notes that the author (al-Maturidi? Actually the text says 'the author' meaning the original author of al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya) did not mention the reckoning, relying on the mention of the book. Then he gives the Mu'tazila objection that this is futile (عبث), and the answer is 'as previously mentioned' – referring to the answer given for the weighing: that our lack of knowledge of the wisdom does not make it futile.

The Questioning on the Day of Judgment Is True
Sanusi affirms the questioning of all creatures, citing Qur'an and hadith about the believer's confession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the questioning on the Day of Judgment is true for all creatures, with believers being questioned privately and mercifully, while disbelievers are shamed publicly.

Core Idea
The questioning is universal, yet the believer's encounter is one of mercy.

This lesson examines the Islamic belief that every soul will be questioned on the Day of Judgment. The Qur'an and hadith affirm this, and a detailed prophetic narration shows how the believer's sins are handled with divine concealment and forgiveness. In contrast, disbelievers and hypocrites face public exposure.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice the two categories: believer vs. disbeliever/hypocrite.
2
Understand the proof from Qur'an and Hadith
Sanusi first cites Qur'an 15:92 as a general proof. Then he narrates a hadith that details the believer's questioning and forgiveness.
The hadith is from the Prophet (peace be upon him).
3
Contrast the treatment of believers and disbelievers
Believers are brought near, covered, and their sins are concealed and forgiven. Disbelievers and hypocrites are publicly called out and cursed.
This shows Allah's mercy to believers and justice to others.

Source Text

(And the questioning (al-su'al) is true due to His statement, the Most High: 'We will surely question them all' [al-Hijr: 92] and due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Allah will bring the believer near and place His cover over him and conceal him, and He will say: Do you recognize such-and-such a sin? Do you recognize such-and-such a sin? Then he will be given his book of good deeds.' As for the disbelievers and hypocrites, they will be called out before the heads of the creatures: 'These are the ones who lied against their Lord. Unquestionably, the curse of Allah is upon the wrongdoers.' [Hud: 18])

Commentary
This passage affirms the reality of the questioning (al-su'al) on the Day of Judgment. The proof is from Qur'an 15:92, which states that all will be questioned. Then a hadith describes the questioning of the believer: Allah brings him near, covers him, and asks him to recognize his sins one by one. The believer admits, and when he thinks he is destroyed, Allah says He concealed them in the world and forgives him today, and then he is given his book of good deeds. For disbelievers and hypocrites, they are publicly shamed before all creation, and the verse from Hud 11:18 is quoted, declaring that the curse of Allah is upon the wrongdoers.

The Reality of the Prophet's Basin (Al-Hawd)
Sanusi affirms the Prophet's basin with Qur'anic and hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's basin (al-Hawd) is a real, physical body of water in the afterlife, affirmed by both the Qur'an and authentic hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet's basin is a literal, physical reality, not a symbol.

In this passage, Sanusi affirms a core belief from the samiyyat (heard matters): the existence of the Prophet's basin on the Day of Judgment. He grounds this belief in clear scriptural evidence and describes its magnificent qualities. The basin is not a metaphor; it is a tangible creation of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the primary evidence
Read the Quranic verse (al-Kawthar) and the hadith quoted. Notice that the first evidence is a direct Quranic mention of 'al-Kawthar', which is interpreted as the basin or a river in Paradise.
The verse is very short but carries immense significance.
2
Examine the description
Look at the detailed description from the hadith: its size (a month's journey), its water being whiter than milk and more fragrant than musk, its vessels more numerous than stars, and the promise that whoever drinks will never thirst. Also note the footnote saying it is square with equal dimensions.
These details emphasize the basin's grandeur and literal nature.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why this belief matters. It is a reward for the Prophet and a blessing for his community. The basin is a source of comfort and hope for believers.
4
Conclude with affirmation
Sanusi ends by stating that the hadiths about the basin are numerous, reinforcing the certainty of this belief. There is no room for doubt.
This cements the basin as a necessary article of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحوض حق لقوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّا أَعْطَيْنَاكَ الْكَوْثَرَ [الكوثر: ١] ولقوله عليه السلام: حوضی مسيرة شهر وزواياه سواء (1) ، وماؤه أبيض من اللبن وريحه أطيب من المسك، وكيزانه أكثر من نجوم السماء. من يشرب منها فلا يظمأ أبدا والأحاديث فيه كثيرة . (۱) عرضه كطوله فهو مربع لا يعلم مساحته إلا من خلقه .
(And the basin (al-hawd) is true due to His statement, the Most High: 'Indeed, We have granted you al-Kawthar' [al-Kawthar: 1] and due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'My basin is a month's journey, its corners are equal (1), its water is whiter than milk, its smell is more fragrant than musk, its vessels are more numerous than the stars of the sky. Whoever drinks from it will never thirst again.' And the hadiths about it are numerous. (1) Its width is like its length, so it is square; none knows its area except the One who created it.)
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage affirms the reality of the Prophet's basin (al-hawd) on the Day of Judgment. Evidence is given from Qur'an 108:1, which mentions al-Kawthar (often interpreted as a river in Paradise or the basin), and from a hadith describing the basin's size (a month's journey), its water whiter than milk, its smell better than musk, its vessels more numerous than stars, and that whoever drinks from it will never thirst. The footnote adds that it is square, with width equal to length, and its area is known only to its Creator. The author concludes that the hadiths on this topic are many.

Key Terms
الحوض
الكوثر
اللبن
المسك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the basin is merely symbolic or metaphorical.
Correction: Sanusi affirms it is a literal, physical body of water with specific properties, based on explicit Quranic and hadith texts.

Checkpoint

A) It is like milk in color and musk in smell.
B) It is whiter than milk and more fragrant than musk.
C) It is sweeter than honey and cooler than snow.
D) It is clear as crystal and tastes like wine.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's basin is a literal, vast body of water in the afterlife, affirmed by the Qur'an and numerous hadith, with specific physical attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to stand at the edge of the Prophet's basin today, would you be among those allowed to drink? What specific deeds or sins in your life right now would determine that? Are you willing to change them to secure your drink?
?
The Prophet described his basin's water as whiter than milk and more fragrant than musk—real pleasures you will experience if you follow him. Are you living in a way that shows you truly desire that reality, or have you become content with worldly substitutes? What one habit can you start today to increase your longing for the afterlife?
?
Whoever drinks once from the basin will never thirst again. What are you currently thirsting for—status, comfort, or approval—that only the Prophet's basin can truly satisfy? How can you redirect your efforts to earn that eternal drink rather than temporary satisfactions?

The Pool (Hawd) is True
Affirms the Pool and describes its attributes through Quran and Hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural basis for belief in the Prophet's Pool (Hawd) and its described attributes.

Core Idea
The Pool is a real, tangible blessing on Judgment Day.

This lesson affirms the reality of the Hawd (Pool) of Prophet Muhammad on the Day of Judgment. The author cites both a Quranic verse and a detailed prophetic hadith to establish its existence and qualities. Understanding this belief reinforces trust in the unseen rewards promised by Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation

The hadith includes several descriptive details.
2
Identify the primary evidence

Al-Kawthar is also the name of a river in Paradise.
3
List the attributes from the hadith

These details emphasize the Pool's magnificence.
4
Understand the cumulative evidence
The author concludes that the hadiths about the Pool are many. This indicates that the belief is well-established and not based on a single narration.
This strengthens the certainty of the belief.

The Bridge (Sirat) is Real and Its Description
Affirmation and physical description of the Bridge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the literal reality of the Bridge over Hell and its described qualities as affirmed in Sunni creed.

Core Idea
The Bridge is a real, physical structure finer than a hair and sharper than a sword.

The author begins by unequivocally stating that the Bridge (sirāt) is true and real. He then provides a vivid description of its physical characteristics to impress upon the believer its actuality and the gravity of crossing it. This passage establishes the Bridge as a literal article of faith, not merely a metaphor.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the opening statement affirming the Bridge's truth and its description as a bridge stretched over Hell, finer than a hair and sharper than a sword.
Notice the literary imagery used to convey precision and danger.
2
Identify the two outcomes
Observe that the passage mentions two opposite results: the people of Paradise cross it safely, while the people of Hell slip and fall.
This contrast underscores the Bridge as a place of divine justice.
3
Reflect on the doctrinal importance
Consider why the author emphasizes the physical reality of the Bridge. This is a point of creed (samiyyat) that distinguishes Sunni belief from those who allegorize it.
The Bridge is one of the events after death that must be believed literally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والصراط حق وهو جسر ممدود على متن جهنم أدق من الشعر وأحد من السيف يعبره أهل الجنة، ويزل به أقدام أهل النار . وأنكره أكثر المعتزلة لأنه لا يمكن العبور عليه وإن أمكن فهو تعذيب للمؤمنين . والجواب : أن الله تعالى قادر على أن يمكن من العبور عليه ويسهله على المؤمنين حتى أن منهم من يجوزه كالبرق الخاطف ومنهم كالريح الهابة، ومنهم كالجواد، إلى غير ذلك مما ورد في الحديث.
And the Bridge is true, and it is a bridge stretched over the middle of Hell, finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. The people of Paradise cross it, and the feet of the people of Hell slip upon it. Most of the Mu'tazila denied it because it is impossible to cross over it, and if possible, it would be torture for the believers. The answer: Allah is able to enable crossing over it and make it easy for the believers, so that some of them cross it like a flash of lightning, some like a blowing wind, some like a steed, and so on as mentioned in the hadith.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage affirms the reality of the Bridge (al-sirāt) over Hell. The author describes it as finer than a hair and sharper than a sword, emphasizing its precariousness. The righteous cross it safely, while the wicked slip and fall. The author then presents the objection of most Mu'tazila: that crossing such a structure is impossible, and even if possible, it would be an act of torture for believers. The reply relies on Allah's absolute power (qudra): He can make the crossing easy, and the hadiths describe varying speeds – some crossing like lightning, wind, or a horse – indicating divine facilitation. This answers the objection that it is impossible or unnecessarily painful.

Key Terms
الصراط
جهنم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Over Paradise
B) Over the middle of Hell
C) Over the earth
D) Over a river

Key Takeaway
The Bridge is a real, physical structure that believers cross safely and unbelievers fall from.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Bridge is described as finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. What weight of faith and deeds do you carry that will prevent you from slipping? Are you truly relying on Allah's mercy to cross, or on your own imagined righteousness?
?
The feet of the people of Hell slip upon it. What sin or attachment in your life makes your footing unsteady right now? What would it take to secure your grip on faith before that day arrives?
?
If you were standing before the Bridge today, what evidence from your life would show that you are among the people of Paradise who cross? Be specific: what actions, beliefs, or priorities demonstrate your readiness?

Refuting the Mu'tazili Objection on the Bridge
Refutation of Mu'tazili doubts about the Bridge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazili objection to the physical Bridge and the Sunni rebuttal based on Allah's absolute power and prophetic reports.

Core Idea
Allah's power makes the impossible crossing easy for believers, as shown in hadith.

After describing the Bridge, the author presents the objection raised by most Mu'tazila: that crossing such a fine and sharp bridge is impossible, and even if possible, it would constitute torture for believers. The response relies on Allah's omnipotence and the variety of crossing speeds narrated in hadith. This lesson defends the literal reality of the Bridge against rationalistic denial.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the part where the author states that most Mu'tazila denied the Bridge, citing two arguments: impossibility of crossing and unjust torment.
Notice that the objection is based on human reasoning.
2
Analyze the rebuttal
See how the author replies: Allah is able to make crossing possible and easy, and the hadith describe different speeds (lightning, wind, horse) for believers.
The rebuttal invokes divine power (qudra) and scriptural evidence.
3
Understand the key principle
Reflect on the principle that Allah's power is not limited by human analogy. What seems impossible to us is easy for Him.
This underscores the importance of relying on revelation over pure reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the Bridge is true, and it is a bridge stretched over the middle of Hell, finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. The people of Paradise cross it, and the feet of the people of Hell slip upon it. Most of the Mu'tazila denied it because it is impossible to cross over it, and if possible, it would be torture for the believers. The answer: Allah is able to enable crossing over it and make it easy for the believers, so that some of them cross it like a flash of lightning, some like a blowing wind, some like a steed, and so on as mentioned in the hadith.

The righteous cross it safely, while the wicked slip and fall. The author then presents the objection of most Mu'tazila: that crossing such a structure is impossible, and even if possible, it would be an act of torture for believers. The reply relies on Allah's absolute power (qudra): He can make the crossing easy, and the hadiths describe varying speeds – some crossing like lightning, wind, or a horse – indicating divine facilitation. ?

?
When you imagine standing before the Bridge, does fear paralyze you or motivate you to change? What specific action will you take today to prepare for that moment?

The Reality of the Sirat (Bridge)
Al-Nasafi affirms the Sirat and refutes the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni affirmation of the Sirat as a real bridge and the rational refutation of the Mu'tazila denial.

Core Idea
The Sirat is real because God can make the impossible possible.

Al-Nasafi affirms that the Sirat is a real bridge stretched over Hell, finer than hair, sharper than a sword, which believers cross with ease and disbelievers fall. The Mu'tazila objected based on impossibility and torment. Al-Nasafi answers with God's absolute power and the varying speeds of crossing as narrated in hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic and English translation. Note the three parts: description of the Sirat, the Mu'tazila objection, and the response.
The Arabic uses concise language; the translation follows literally.
2
Identify the description
Notice that the Sirat is described as a bridge over Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than hair. Understand the imagery: it is a real but extraordinary bridge.
The description emphasizes both its reality and its fine, sharp nature.
3
Analyze the objection
The Mu'tazila deny the Sirat because crossing seems impossible and would torment believers. Ask: Is this a rational or scriptural objection?
The objection is based on human reason without considering God's power.
4
Examine the answer
Al-Nasafi responds that Allah can make crossing possible and easy for believers, citing varied speeds from hadith. This shows God's absolute power over natural laws.
The key is that God’s power is not limited by human impossibility.

The response is that Allah Almighty is able to enable crossing and make it easy for believers, as indicated by the varying speeds mentioned in hadith: like lightning, wind, horse, etc. This demonstrates that what is impossible for humans is possible for God, and the experience for believers is not torment but a swift passage.

Paradise and Hell are Created Now
Al-Nasafi argues that Paradise and Hell are created now, countering the Mu'tazila view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that Paradise and Hell are already created and the evidence from the Qur'an and the story of Adam.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are real, prepared places, not just future promises.

Al-Nasafi begins by affirming that Paradise and Hell are already created and exist now, contrary to the Mu'tazila who say they will be created on the Day of Judgment. He then presents two pieces of evidence: the story of Adam dwelling in Paradise, and the Qur'anic verses using the past tense 'prepared'. Finally, he addresses a potential objection from another verse.

Guided Path
1
Understand the positions
Read the opening sentence: Al-Nasafi states the Sunni view, then the Mu'tazila claim. Note the emphasis on 'created now'.
The repetition 'created now, existing' is for emphasis.
2
Examine the first proof
Consider the story of Adam and Eve dwelling in Paradise. This shows Paradise existed before the Day of Judgment.
3
Examine the second proof
Look at the verses using 'prepared' (u'iddat) in past tense. The author argues there is no need to deviate from the apparent meaning.
Q.3:133 and Q.2:24 are cited.
4
Follow the objection and response
Read the objection from Q.28:83 and Al-Nasafi's answer: the verse can refer to present state or continuity, and even if conceded, the Adam story remains unaffected.
This shows how the author defends his position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهما أى الجنة والنار مخلوقتان الآن موجودتان تكرير وتوكيد . وزعم أكثر المعتزلة : أنهما إنما يخلقان يوم الجزاء. لنا : قصة آدم وحواء - عليهما السلام - وإسكانهما الجنة والآيات الظاهرة في إعدادهما ، مثل : ﴿ أُعِدَّتْ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ ﴾ [آل عمران : ۱۳۳] و ﴿ وأُعدت للكافرين ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٤] إذ لا ضرورة في العدول عن الظاهر. فإن عورض بمثل قوله تعالى : ﴿ تِلْكَ الدَّارُ الْآخِرَةُ نَجْعَلُهَا لِلَّذِينَ لَا يُرِيدُونَ عُلُوًّا فِي الْأَرْضِ وَلَا فَسَادًا ﴾ [ القصص : ۸۳] قلنا : يحتمل الحال والاستمرار ولو سلم فقصة آدم تبقى سالمة عن المعارض.

Our proof: the story of Adam and Eve (peace be upon them) and their dwelling in Paradise, and the clear verses about their preparation, such as 'Prepared for the righteous' (Q.3:133) and 'Prepared for the disbelievers' (Q.2:24), since there is no necessity to depart from the apparent meaning. If it is objected with His saying: 'That is the final abode, We assign it to those who do not desire exaltation in the earth nor corruption' (Q.28:83), we say: It can be interpreted as the present state or continuity, and even if conceded, the story of Adam remains safe from the objection.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage argues that Paradise and Hell are already created now. The author explains that the expression 'created now' is a repetition for emphasis. Most Mu'tazila hold that they are created only on the Day of Judgment. The proof is from the story of Adam and Eve living in Paradise, and from verses that say Paradise is 'prepared' for the righteous and Hell is 'prepared' for the disbelievers, using the past tense verb 'prepared' (u'iddat). Since there is no need to deviate from the apparent meaning, these indicate creation now. Then he presents a possible objection: the verse 'That is the final abode' suggests it will be given in the afterlife. The answer is that the verse can refer to the present state or continuity, and even if interpreted as future, the story of Adam remains an unambiguous proof that Paradise existed before.

The Eternity of Paradise and Hell Defended
Al-Nasafi defends the eternity of Paradise and Hell against the objection from 'everything perishes.'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi reconciles the verses on the eternity of Paradise and Hell with the verse 'Everything is perishing.'

Core Idea
The eternity of Paradise and Hell does not contradict the perishing of individual things.

In this passage, Al-Nasafi addresses a critical objection to the Islamic belief in the eternal abode of Paradise and Hell. Skeptics point to the Quranic verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face' (28:88) to argue that even Paradise and Hell must eventually cease. Al-Nasafi provides a nuanced response, clarifying the meanings of 'perpetual' and 'perishing' and showing that they do not undermine the eternity of the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get the flow of the objection and response. Notice the structure: objection, then three answers, then conclusion.
The passage uses theological reasoning and Quranic verses.
2
Identify the objection
The objectors argue: if Paradise and Hell exist now, then their fruit must be perpetual, but the Quran says everything perishes, so a contradiction arises.
3
Understand the first answer
Al-Nasafi replies that 'perpetual fruit' does not mean the same fruit remains forever; rather, when one fruit perishes, another replaces it. This allows individual perishing while the whole remains.
This answer distinguishes between species and individuals.
4
Understand the second answer
He then argues that 'perishing' (halak) can mean removal from benefit, not absolute annihilation. Thus, the fruit of Paradise can be replaced without contradicting eternity.
5
Understand the third answer and conclusion
Finally, even if we concede the plain meaning, the verse may refer to contingent things being inherently non-existent relative to God. The conclusion: Paradise and Hell are abiding and do not perish.
This is a metaphysical interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قالوا : لو كانتا موجودتين الآن لما جاز هلاك أهل الجنة لقوله تعالى: ﴿ أُكُلُهَا دَائِمٌ ﴾ [الرعد : ۳۵] لكن اللازم باطل، لقوله تعالى : ﴿ كُلُّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُ ﴾ [ القصص : ۸۸] قلنا : لا خفاء فى أنه لا يمكن دوام أكل الجنة بعينه وإنما المراد بالدوام أنه إذا فنى منه شيء جئ ببدله وهذا لا ينافي الهلاك لحظة. على أن الهلاك لا يستلزم الفناء، بل يكفى الخروج عن الانتفاع به. ولو سلم فيجوز أن يكون المراد أن كل شيء ممكن فهو هالك في حد ذاته بمعنى أن الوجود الإمكانى بالنظر إلى الوجود الواجبي بمنزلة العدم . باقيتان لا تفنيان، ولا يفنى (أهلهما) أي دائمتان لا يطرأ عليهما الفناء.
They said: If they were existing now, then the destruction of the people of Paradise would not be permissible because of His saying: 'Its fruit is perpetual' (Q.13:35). But the necessary consequence is false because of His saying: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' (Q.28:88). We say: It is no secret that perpetual cannot mean the very same fruit continues; rather, what is meant by perpetual is that if something perishes, its replacement comes, and this does not contradict perishing at a moment. Moreover, perishing (al-halak) does not necessitate annihilation (al-fana'), rather it suffices as removal from benefiting from it. And even if conceded, it is possible that what is meant is that everything possible is perishing in itself, meaning that possible existence relative to Necessary Existence is like non-existence. They (Paradise and Hell) are abiding, they do not perish, and their inhabitants do not perish—meaning they are eternal, and perishing does not occur to them.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection about the eternity of Paradise and Hell. The objectors argue that if Paradise and Hell exist now, then the sustenance of the people of Paradise would not perish, but the verse 'Everything perishes except His Face' contradicts. The answer is detailed: First, 'perpetual fruit' does not mean the same fruit remains forever, but rather that when one fruit perishes, another replaces it, so perishing of individual fruits is allowed. Second, perishing (halak) does not mean annihilation (fana'), but simply removal from benefit — the people of Paradise benefit from the fruit, but when it is replaced, the previous fruit 'perishes' in that sense. Third, even if it implies annihilation, the meaning of 'Everything perishes' can refer to contingent things being inherently non-necessary, i.e., they could be nonexistent. The conclusion is that Paradise and Hell are abiding and do not perish, and their inhabitants do not perish.

Key Terms
باقيتان
لا تفنيان
هالك
فناء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'everything perishes' proves that Paradise and Hell will eventually end.
Correction: Al-Nasafi explains that 'perishing' can mean replacement or removal from benefit, not absolute annihilation; moreover, the verse may refer to contingent things being inherently non-existent relative to Allah.

Checkpoint
What is the primary answer to the objection that 'everything perishes'?
A) The fruit of Paradise is replaced, so perishing of individual fruit does not contradict eternity.
B) The verse only applies to this world.
C) Paradise and Hell are also part of 'everything' and will perish eventually.
D) The objection is based on a weak hadith.

Key Takeaway
Al-Nasafi defends the eternity of Paradise and Hell by showing that the verse 'everything perishes' does not require absolute annihilation, but can be reconciled with perpetual renewal and the contingent nature of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Paradise and Hell are truly eternal, what does that mean for every single choice you make today? Do you live as though your actions have eternal consequences, or do you act as if this world is all that matters?
?
Al-Nasafi argues that 'perishing' does not mean absolute annihilation. Are you attached to things that will perish—your possessions, status, or relationships—as if they are permanent? How would your priorities shift if you truly believed that only Allah's Face remains?
?
The fruit of Paradise is perpetually renewed. Are you seeking the eternal reward that never runs out, or are you settling for fleeting pleasures that will vanish? What is one habit you can change today to pursue the lasting over the temporary?

Paradise and Hell Are Created Now – The Proof from Adam and Eve
Commentator states Paradise and Hell are created now, refuting the Mu'tazila with two proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ahl al-Sunnah position that Paradise and Hell are already created and the scriptural evidence supporting this view.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell exist now, proven by Adam's story and Quranic past-tense preparation verses.

In this passage, the commentator defends the orthodox view that Paradise and Hell are already created, against the Mu'tazila who claim they will only be created on the Day of Judgment. The proof rests on two clear scriptural evidences: the account of Adam and Eve dwelling in Paradise, and the Quranic verses that use the past tense 'prepared' for both Paradise and Hell. Because there is no compelling reason to interpret these literally, the apparent meaning stands.

Guided Path
1

The verses are from Surah Al Imran and Surah Al-Baqarah.

The Mu'tazila interpret these verses metaphorically or as referring to the future.

This passage defines the Ahl al-Sunnah position that Paradise and Hell are already created now, and provides the proof. The commentator argues that there is no necessity to interpret these verses metaphorically or defer their meaning to the future.

Refuting the First Objection
First objection and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentator refutes the objection that the verse 'That is the abode of the Hereafter' (Al-Qasas: 83) implies Paradise and Hell do not exist now.

Core Idea
Not all verses about the Hereafter deny its present existence.

In this lesson, we examine the first objection raised against the createdness of Paradise and Hell. The objectors cite a verse that calls Paradise the 'abode of the Hereafter' to argue that it does not exist now. The commentator offers two layers of response: interpretation of the verse and an independent proof from the story of Adam.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the verse
Read the objector's citation of Surah Al-Qasas verse 83. Notice how they interpret 'the abode of the Hereafter' to mean it will only be given in the afterlife.
The verse is: 'That is the abode of the Hereafter; We appoint it for those who do not desire exaltation in the earth nor corruption.'
2
Understand the commentator's first response
The commentator says the verse can be interpreted as referring to the present state (the abode is assigned now) or continuity (it will be given in the future). This shows the verse is not definitive against present existence.
This is a linguistic possibility.
3
Note the fallback argument
Even if the objection is conceded, the story of Adam (who lived in Paradise) provides independent evidence that Paradise existed before the Hereafter.
This argument is based on the Qur'anic narrative of Adam in Paradise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن عورض بمثل قوله تعالى : تلْكَ الدَّارُ الآخِرَةُ نَجْعَلُهَا لِلَّذِينَ لا يُرِيدُونَ عَلُوا فِي الْأَرْضِ وَلَا فَسَادًا [ القصص : ٨٣] قلنا : يحتمل الحال والاستمرار ولو سلم فقصة آدم تبقى سالمة عن المعارض . قالوا : لو كانتا موجودتين الآن لما جاز هلاك أهل الجنة لقوله تعالى: ﴿ أُكلها دائم ﴾ [الرعد : ٣٥] لكن اللازم باطل، لقوله تعالى : ﴿ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلا وَجْهَهُ ﴾ [ القصص : ٨٨] قلنا : لا خفاء فى أنه لا يمكن دوام أكل الجنة بعينه وإنما المراد بالدوام أنه إذا فنى منه شيء جئ ببدله وهذا لا ينافي الهلاك لحظة. على أن الهلاك لا يستلزم الفناء، بل يكفى الخروج عن الانتفاع .به ولو سلم فيجوز أن يكون المراد أن كل شيء ممكن فهو هالك في حد ذاته بمعنى أن الوجود الإمكانى بالنظر إلى الوجود الواجبي بمنزلة العدم .
If it is objected by something like His statement: 'That is the abode of the Hereafter; We appoint it for those who do not desire exaltation in the earth nor corruption' [Al-Qasas: 83], we say: it is probable [that it refers to] the present state and continuity; and even if conceded, the story of Adam remains untouched by the objection. They said: If they were both existing now, then the perishing of the people of Paradise would not be permissible because of His statement: 'Its fruit is perpetual' [Ar-Ra'd: 35]; but the consequent is false because of His statement: 'Everything perishes except His face' [Al-Qasas: 88]. We say: it is not hidden that perpetual continuation of the identical fruit is impossible; rather what is meant by perpetuity is that when something perishes, its substitute comes, and this does not contradict perishing at an instant. Moreover, perishing does not necessitate annihilation; rather it suffices to mean removal from beneficial use. And even if conceded, it is possible that the meaning is that every contingent thing is perishing in itself, in the sense that contingent existence in relation to necessary existence is like non-existence.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage contains two objections and their responses. First objection: The verse 'That is the abode of the Hereafter' (Al-Qasas: 83) seems to say that Paradise is only given in the Hereafter, implying it does not exist now. The commentator replies: this verse can refer to the present state (i.e., the abode is determined now) or to continuity. Even if one concedes the objection, the story of Adam (who lived in Paradise) remains as independent evidence. Second objection: If Paradise and Hell exist now, then the perpetuity of the fruit of Paradise (verse: 'its fruit is perpetual') would contradict the verse that everything perishes except God. The answer: The perpetuity of fruit does not mean the same fruit particles last forever; rather it means continuous replenishment. This does not conflict with perishing at a given moment. Furthermore, 'perishing' in the verse may not mean absolute annihilation but rather cessation of benefit, or it may refer to the inherent non-essential nature of contingent things in comparison to the Necessary Being.

Key Terms
الدار الآخرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'That is the abode of the Hereafter' definitively proves Paradise does not exist now.
Correction: The verse can be interpreted as describing the assignment of Paradise in the Hereafter, not necessarily denying its present existence; moreover, the story of Adam shows Paradise existed earlier.

Checkpoint
How does the commentator respond to the objection that the verse 'That is the abode of the Hereafter' (Al-Qasas:83) denies the present existence of Paradise?
A) He says the verse is abrogated.
B) He says the verse can refer to the present state or continuity.
C) He admits the verse proves the objection.
D) He ignores the verse.

Key Takeaway
The first objection is refuted by interpreting the verse flexibly and by an independent proof from Adam's Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Adam lived in Paradise in the present world. Is your life today shaped by the reality that Paradise is not merely a distant hope but can be experienced now through obedience? In what specific area do you need to start living as if Paradise is already near?

Refuting the Second Objection
Second objection and its refutation via scriptural and philosophical reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentator resolves the apparent contradiction between the perpetual fruit of Paradise (Ar-Ra'd:35) and the perishing of all things (Al-Qasas:88).

Core Idea
Perpetuity does not require individual items to last forever.

The second objection is more sophisticated: if Paradise and Hell exist now, then the perpetuity of the fruit of Paradise (from Ar-Ra'd:35) would contradict the verse that everything perishes except God (Al-Qasas:88). The commentator provides a multi-layered explanation involving the replacement of fruit, the meaning of perishing, and a metaphysical distinction between contingent and necessary existence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two verses that appear to conflict
Read the objection: if Paradise and Hell exist now, then the fruit of Paradise is perpetual, yet everything perishes. This creates an apparent contradiction.
The verses are 'Its fruit is perpetual' (Ar-Ra'd:35) and 'Everything perishes except His face' (Al-Qasas:88).
2
Understand the explanation of perpetual fruit
The commentator says perpetual does not mean the same fruit particles last forever; rather, when one fruit perishes, a substitute comes. This allows perishing at an instant without contradicting perpetual renewal.
This resolves the immediate contradiction.
3
Grasp the distinction about 'perishing'
The commentator further explains that 'perishing' in the verse may not mean absolute annihilation but rather removal from beneficial use, or it may refer to the contingent nature of things in relation to God's necessary existence.
These deeper points show the objection is based on misunderstanding the terms.

Paradise and Hell Everlasting – Refutation of Jahmiyya
Affirms eternity of Paradise and Hell and refutes Jahmiyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Paradise and Hell are everlasting based on a clear Qur'anic verse and that the Jahmiyya claim of annihilation is false and contradictory to the Book, Sunnah, and consensus.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell never perish—they are eternal abodes for their inhabitants.

This passage from the Sharh al-Aqaid al-Nasafiyyah establishes a core Sunni belief: Paradise and Hell are everlasting and their inhabitants never perish. The commentator first affirms this truth with a clear Qur'anic verse, then addresses a potential objection, and finally refutes the deviant Jahmiyya sect. Let's read the original text and see how the argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Let the author's flow settle in your mind. Then read the English translation.
Notice how the passage moves from affirmation to proof to rebuttal.
2
Understand the proof from Al-Bayyinah
The commentator cites the verse 'They will abide therein forever' as direct evidence. Consider why this verse is chosen and what it implies about duration.
3
Examine the objection and its answer
The objection is from 'Everything perishes except His face.'The commentator argues this does not contradict the meaning of permanence. Find his reasoning.
He also notes the verse does not explicitly indicate annihilation.
4
Reflect on the Jahmiyya refutation
The Jahmiyya claim is that both Paradise and Hell and their inhabitants perish. The commentator declares this false and lacking proof. Note the three sources it contradicts: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma.
This shows how sectarian views are evaluated against orthodox sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باقيتان لا تفنيان، ولا يفنى (أهلهما) أي دائمتان لا يطراً عليهما عدم مستمر لقوله تعالى في حق الفريقين : خالدين فيها [البيئة : ٨] وأما ما قيل : من أنهما تهلكان، ولو لحظة، تحقيقا لقوله تعالى : كُلَّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكٌ إلا وجهه الله فلا ينافي البقاء بهذا المعنى، على أنك قد عرفت أنه لا دلالة في الآية على الفناء. وذهب الجهمية إلى أنهما يفنيان، ويفني أهلهما . وهو قول باطل مخالف للكتاب والسنة والإجماع، وليس عليه شبهة، فضلا عن حجة .
Both are everlasting, not perishing, and their inhabitants do not perish. That is, they are perpetual, upon which continuous non-existence does not intrude, due to His statement concerning both groups: 'They will abide therein forever' [Al-Bayyinah: 8]. As for what has been said: that they perish, even for a moment, in realization of His statement: 'Everything perishes except the face of God'—this does not contradict permanence according to this meaning; moreover, you already know that there is no indication in the verse of annihilation. The Jahmiyya held that they both perish, and their inhabitants perish. This is a false statement, contradicting the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, and there is no doubt about it, let alone any proof.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage establishes the Ahl al-Sunnah position that Paradise and Hell are everlasting (baqiyatan). The commentator interprets 'baqiyatan' as perpetual, with no continuous non-existence intruding, citing the verse 'They will abide therein forever' (Al-Bayyinah: 8). Then he addresses the claim that they must perish even for an instant because of the verse 'Everything perishes except His face.' He responds that the verse's meaning does not necessarily imply annihilation; the earlier explanation (that perishing can mean removal from benefit) suffices. Moreover, the verse does not explicitly indicate annihilation. Finally, the commentator rebukes the Jahmiyya who assert that both Paradise and Hell and their inhabitants will be annihilated. He declares this view false, in opposition to the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, and lacking even a plausible argument.

Key Terms
باقيتان
لا تفنيان
الجهمية
خلود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jahmiyya believed that Paradise and Hell will perish along with their inhabitants.
Correction: The correct belief is that Paradise and Hell are everlasting (baqiyatan) and their inhabitants never perish, as supported by the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus.

Checkpoint

A) They are created now.
B) They are everlasting.
C) They will perish along with their inhabitants.
D) They are only spiritual.

Key Takeaway
The eternity of Paradise and Hell is established by the Qur'an, and any claim of their annihilation is false and against the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah.

?

Refutation of the Jahmiyyah on Annihilation of Paradise and Hell
Taftazani refutes the Jahmiyyah claim that Paradise and Hell will be annihilated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Jahmiyyah claim that Paradise and Hell will be annihilated is false according to the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, and why the verse 'Everything is perishing' does not support their view.

Core Idea
The Jahmiyyah claim that Paradise and Hell will be annihilated contradicts the decisive texts and lacks even a plausible doubt.

In this passage, Taftazani addresses a specific theological error: the belief that Paradise and Hell will be annihilated. He first clarifies that the Quranic verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face' does not imply the annihilation of these eternal abodes. Then he dismisses the Jahmiyyah position as baseless and contrary to the core sources of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once and its literal translation to get a sense of Taftazani's argument.
Pay attention to the verse reference.
2
Identify the two main claims refuted
Notice that Taftazani first addresses a claim about the verse implying annihilation, then explicitly states the Jahmiyyah view and condemns it.
3
Understand the refutation's basis
Taftazani argues that the verse does not contradict permanence and that the Jahmiyyah view contradicts the Book, Sunnah, and consensus.
He also says there is not even a doubt, let alone proof.
4
Answer the checkpoint question
Test your understanding by answering the multiple-choice question about the Jahmiyyah view.
This will reinforce the key point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما قيل : من أنهما تهلكان، ولو لحظة، تحقيقا لقوله تعالى : كُلَّ شَيْءٍ هالك إلا وجهه الله فلا ينافي البقاء بهذا المعنى، على أنك قد عرفت أنه لا دلالة في الآية على الفناء. وذهب الجهمية إلى أنهما يفنيان، ويفني أهلهما . وهو قول باطل مخالف للكتاب والسنة والإجماع، وليس عليه شبهة، فضلا عن حجة.
And as for what was said: that they [Paradise and Hell] are destroyed, even for a moment, in realization of His saying, the Most High: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' [Quran 28:88], so it does not contradict permanence in this sense. Moreover, you have known that there is no indication in the verse of annihilation. And the Jahmiyyah held that they [Paradise and Hell] are annihilated, and their inhabitants are annihilated. And it is a false statement, contradictory to the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, and there is not even a doubt upon it, let alone a proof.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two claims: first, the claim that the verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face' necessitates the annihilation of Paradise and Hell, and second, the Jahmiyyah claim that they will be annihilated. The author argues that the verse does not contradict the permanent existence of Paradise and Hell in their intended sense of continuous existence, and that the verse itself contains no evidence for their annihilation. Then he condemns the Jahmiyyah view as false, contradictory to the primary sources of Islam, and lacking even a plausible doubt, let alone a valid proof.

Key Terms
الجهمية (Jahmiyyah)
الفناء (annihilation)
الآية (the verse)
البقاء (permanence)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Everything is perishing' proves that Paradise and Hell will be annihilated.
Correction: The verse does not indicate annihilation of Paradise and Hell; it does not contradict their permanence in the sense of continuous existence.

C) They will change form but not cease to exist
D) They are created but not permanent

Key Takeaway
The Jahmiyyah claim that Paradise and Hell will be annihilated is false because it contradicts the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, and even the verse cited by them does not support it.

Forgiveness Without Repentance and Refutation of Mu'tazila
Affirms that God may forgive minor and major sins without repentance, refuting Mu'tazila objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that Allah may forgive any sin (except shirk) for whomever He wills, with or without repentance, and how the two Mu'tazila objections are refuted.

Core Idea
Allah's mercy is vast; He may forgive any sin without repentance as He wills.

This passage addresses a critical difference between Sunni and Mu'tazila theology: the scope of divine forgiveness. The author states that Allah may forgive any sin (except shirk) for whomever He wills, even without repentance. The Mu'tazila restricted forgiveness, arguing that threats must be fulfilled and that leniency encourages sin. The passage defends the Sunni view by refuting these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the author's clear stance against the Mu'tazila.
The passage is dense with arguments; read slowly.
2
Identify the Sunni position on forgiveness
Locate the opening statement: Allah forgives minor and major sins, with or without repentance, for whom He wills. This is the core Sunni belief.
3
Understand the first Mu'tazila argument and its refutation
The Mu'tazila say the threat verses must be fulfilled. The author replies that they indicate occurrence, not obligation, and that many texts on forgiveness specify the forgiven sinner out of general threats.
4
Understand the second Mu'tazila argument and its refutation
The Mu'tazila argue that the possibility of forgiveness encourages sin. The author counters that the terrifying nature of the threats remains a sufficient deterrent, and punishment for minor sins is still possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويغفر ما دون ذلك لمن يشاء من الصغائر والكبائر مع التوبة أو بدونها، خلافا للمعتزلة. وفى تقرير الحكم ملاحظة للآية الدالة على ثبوته والآيات والأحاديث في هذا المعنى كثيرة . والمعتزلة يخصونها بالصغائر وبالكبائر، المقرونة بالتوبة وتمسكوا بوجهين: الأول : الآيات والأحاديث الواردة في وعيد العصاة. والجواب : أنها على تقدير عمومها إنما تدل على الوقوع دون الوجوب وقد كثرت النصوص في العفو، فيخصص المذنب المغفور من عمومات الوعيد وزعم بعضهم : أن الخلف في الوعيد، كرم فيجوز من الله تعالى . والمحققون على خلافه . كيف؟ وهو تبديل للقول . وقد قال الله تعالى : مَا يُبَدِّلُ الْقَولُ لَدَيَّ ) [ق: 29] الثاني: أن المذنب إذا علم أنه لا يعاقب على ذنبه، كان ذلك تقريرا له على الذنب، وإغراء للغير عليه . وهذا ينافي حكمة إرسال الرسل. فضلا عن العلم. كيف؟ والعمومات الواردة فى الوعيد المقرونة بغاية من التهديد ترجح جانب الوقوع بالنسبة إلى كل واحد وكفى به زاجرا . ويجوز العقاب على الصغيرة سواء اجتنب مرتكبها الكبيرة
And He forgives what is less than that for whomever He wills of minor sins and major sins, with repentance or without it, contrary to the Mu'tazila. And in establishing the ruling there is consideration of the verse that indicates its affirmation, and the verses and hadiths in this regard are many. The Mu'tazila restrict forgiveness to minor sins and to major sins accompanied by repentance, and they adhere to two arguments: First: the verses and hadiths that warn against sinners. The answer: that even if they are general, they only indicate occurrence, not obligation, and there have been many texts on forgiveness, so the forgiven sinner is specified out of the general warnings. Some claim that breaking a threat is generosity, so it is permissible from Allah. But the investigators disagree. How? Because it would be a change of statement, and Allah has said: 'My word is not changed' [Qaf 50:29]. Second: that if the sinner knows that he will not be punished for his sin, that would be an encouragement for him to persist in sin and an incitement for others, and this contradicts the wisdom of sending messengers – not to mention knowledge. How? And the general texts on threat, accompanied by extreme intimidation, make the occurrence more likely with respect to every individual, and that is sufficient as a deterrent. And punishment for a minor sin is permissible even if the perpetrator avoids major sins.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage addresses the scope of Allah's forgiveness for sins other than shirk. The author states the Sunni position: Allah forgives minor and major sins for whomever He wills, whether the sinner repents or not. This is contrary to the Mu'tazila, who restrict forgiveness to minor sins automatically and to major sins only if accompanied by repentance. The Mu'tazila support their view with two arguments. First, they cite verses and hadiths that threaten punishment for disobedient people; they claim that these threats must be carried out, otherwise they would be false. The author responds that even if these texts are general, they indicate that punishment will occur (in some cases), not that it is obligatory in every instance; moreover, there are many texts promising forgiveness, so the forgiven sinner is excluded from the general threats. The author also refutes the claim that breaking a threat is an act of generosity; this would imply that Allah changes His word, which contradicts the Quranic verse 'My word is not changed.' The second Mu'tazila argument is that if sinners know they might be forgiven without repentance, they would be encouraged to sin and others would follow, undermining the purpose of sending prophets. The author answers that the mere possibility of forgiveness does not lead to such certainty; rather, the terrifying nature of the threats makes people fear punishment, which acts as a sufficient deterrent. Finally, the author adds that punishment for minor sins is permissible even if the perpetrator avoids major sins – a statement affirming divine justice and sovereignty.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if Allah can forgive without repentance, sinners have no reason to fear punishment and will sin freely.
Correction: The author argues that the terrifying nature of the divine threats makes punishment likely for each individual, which is a sufficient deterrent, so the possibility of mercy does not encourage sin.

Checkpoint
What is the first argument of the Mu'tazila against the possibility of forgiveness without repentance?
A) That forgiveness would violate divine justice.
B) That the verses of threat indicate punishment is obligatory.
C) That no one would repent if forgiveness is possible.
D) That God cannot change His word.

Key Takeaway
Allah may forgive any sin (except shirk) for whomever He wills, with or without repentance, and the Mu'tazila objections are refuted by showing that threats indicate occurrence not obligation, and that divine threats remain a powerful deterrent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly feel the weight of divine threat, or do you take comfort in the possibility of forgiveness without repentance, using it as a license to continue? Allah sees your heart. What does this reveal about your sincerity?
?
The Mu'tazila argued that the promise of forgiveness without repentance would encourage sin. Are you someone who delays repentance because you assume God will forgive anyway? How does this passage unsettle your assumptions about your own faith?
?
This lesson teaches that God's threats are real even if He might forgive. When you hear verses of threat, do they move you to action, or do you dismiss them because of the hope of mercy? Examine your relationship with the Quran's warnings.

Second Mu'tazila Objection and Its Refutation
Sanusi presents the second Mu'tazila argument and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second Mu'tazila objection that forgiveness encourages sin and why the mere possibility of pardon does not undermine deterrent threats.

Core Idea
Forgiveness possibilities do not cancel the deterrent power of threatening texts.

The Mu'tazila raised a second objection: if God can forgive without punishment, sinners will be emboldened. This seems to contradict the wisdom of sending prophets. Sanusi responds by showing that the possibility of forgiveness does not lead to certainty of impunity, and the Qur'anic threats remain preponderant. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the first part of the passage which states the Mu'tazila argument. Notice the words 'tadrib' (encouragement) and 'ighra' (enticement).
2
Study the response
Sanusi answers by denying that possibility implies certainty. Identify the rhetorical question 'kayfa' and how the threatening texts are described.
The response is concise but decisive.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider how this response preserves both the possibility of divine forgiveness and the effectiveness of warnings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: أن المذنب إذا علم أنه لا يعاقب على ذنبه، كان ذلك تقريرا له على الذنب، وإغراء للغير عليه . وهذا ينافي حكمة إرسال الرسل. والجواب أن مجرد جواز العفو، لا يوجب ظن عدم العقاب عن العلم. كيف؟ والعمومات الواردة فى الوعيد المقرونة بغاية من التهديد ترجح جانب الوقوع بالنسبة إلى كل واحد وكفى به زاجرا .
The second: that if the sinner knows that he will not be punished for his sin, that would be an encouragement for him to sin and an enticement for others to do so. And this contradicts the wisdom of sending messengers. And the answer: that mere permissibility of pardon does not necessitate the assumption of no punishment based on knowledge. How so? And the general texts that have come regarding the threat, coupled with extreme intimidation, give preponderance to the side of occurrence with respect to every individual, and it suffices as a deterrent.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage presents the second Mu'tazila argument against forgiveness without punishment. The argument states that if sinners know they will not be punished, they will be emboldened to sin, and others will be encouraged, which contradicts the purpose of sending prophets. The response clarifies that the mere possibility of pardon does not lead to a definite belief that punishment will not occur. On the contrary, the many threatening texts in revelation, which include severe intimidation, make punishment more likely for each individual, and this itself serves as a sufficient deterrent. Thus, even though forgiveness is possible, the overwhelming evidence of threat still prevents people from taking sin lightly. The author uses the word 'kayfa' (how so?) to emphasize the logical flaw in the Mu'tazila claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If forgiveness is possible, then threats of punishment are ineffective and cannot deter.
Correction: The possibility of forgiveness does not negate the preponderance of threats; the threats remain a strong deterrent because they are supported by many texts and severe warnings.

Checkpoint

A) Forgiveness occurs only after repentance, so no encouragement
B) The possibility of pardon does not create certainty of impunity, and threat texts make punishment more likely
C) The argument applies only to minor sins
D) Sinners do not actually know about forgiveness

Key Takeaway
The mere logical possibility of divine forgiveness does not weaken the deterrent power of revealed threats because those threats are overwhelming and preponderant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The threatening texts are described as 'coupled with extreme intimidation'. Have you become desensitized to verses about punishment in the Quran? What would it take for you to feel their weight as a real deterrent in your daily choices?
?
If you truly believed that punishment for a particular sin is preponderantly likely for you—unless you repent—what would you do today that you have been putting off?

Punishment for Minor Sins and the Mu'tazila View
Sanusi discusses punishment for minor sins and refutes the Mu'tazila who exempt those avoiding major sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on punishment for minor sins, the Mu'tazila exception for those avoiding major sins, and the decisive response that 'absolute major sin' refers specifically to kufr.

Core Idea
Punishment for minor sins is permissible; the promise of expiation is tied to avoiding kufr, not all major sins.

In this passage, Sanusi presents the Sunni theological position that Allah may punish for minor sins regardless of whether one avoids major sins. He then addresses the Mu'tazila claim that avoiding major sins makes punishment for minor sins impossible, citing textual evidence. The response clarifies that the 'absolute major sin' is kufr, thus the promise of expiation is specific to avoiding disbelief, not other sins.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Sunni position on minor sins
Read the first part of the passage where Sanusi states that punishment for a minor sin is permissible whether or not one avoids major sins, and note the supporting verses.
Notice the use of سَوَاء (whether) indicating no condition.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila objection
Read the Mu'tazila view: if one avoids major sins, punishment for minor sins is not permissible. Distinguish between rational impossibility and textual impossibility as they frame it.
They say it is not rationally impossible but does not occur due to textual evidence.
3
Analyze the Sunni response
Read the response that 'absolute major sin' (الكبيرة المطلقة) is kufr, and understand the linguistic principle about collective vs. distributive meaning.
The example 'ركب القوم دوابهم' illustrates that each person rode his own mount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز العقاب على الصغيرة سواء اجتنب مرتكبها الكبيرة أم لا، لدخولها تحت قوله تعالى : ويغفر ما دون ذلك لمَن يَشَاء [النساء: ١١٦] ولقوله تعالى : لا يُغَادِرُ صَغِيرَةً وَلَا كَبِيرَةً إِلَّا أَحْصَاهَا ﴾ [الكهف: ٤٩] والإحصاء إنما يكون بالسؤال والمجازاة، إلى غير ذلك من الآيات والأحاديث: وذهب بعض المعتزلة : إلى أنه إذا اجتنب الكبائر، لم يجز تعذيبه لا بمعني أنه يمتنع عقلا، بل بمعنى أنه لا يجوز أن يقع لقيام الأدلة السمعية على أنه لا يقع. لقوله تعالى : إن تجتنبوا كبائر ما تنهونَ عَنهُ نُكَفِّرْ عَنكُمْ سَيِّئَاتِكُمْ ﴾ [النساء : ٣١] وأجيب : بأن الكبيرة المطلقة هى الكفر، لأنه الكامل في جميع الإثم . بالنظر إلى أنواع الكفر، وإن كان الكل ملة واحدة في الحكم، أو إلى أفراده القائمة بأفراد المخاطبين على ما تمهد من قاعدة أن مقابلة الجمع بالجمع، تقتضى انقسام الآحاد بالآحاد كقولنا ركب القوم دوابهم، وليسوا ثيابهم [؟]
And punishment for a minor sin is permissible, whether its committer avoids major sins or not, because it falls under His statement, may He be exalted: 'And He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' [An-Nisa: 116], and under His statement: 'It leaves no minor or major sin but it has enumerated them' [Al-Kahf: 49]. And enumeration is only for questioning and recompense, and other verses and hadiths. And some Mu'tazila held that if one avoids major sins, it is not permissible to punish him—not in the sense that it is rationally impossible, but in the sense that it is not permissible to occur because of established textual evidences that it does not occur, due to His statement: 'If you avoid the major sins which you are forbidden, We will expiate your misdeeds' [An-Nisa: 31]. And it was answered: that the absolute major sin is disbelief (kufr), because it is perfect in all sinfulness—considering the types of disbelief, even if all are one milla in ruling, or considering its individuals that stand by individuals of the addressed, based on the established principle that the meeting of a collective with a collective requires the division of units by units, as we say: 'The people rode their mounts' [and wore their clothes?]
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on punishment for minor sins and the Mu'tazila exception. The author states that it is permissible for Allah to punish for a minor sin regardless of whether the sinner avoids major sins, citing two verses: one shows forgiveness is for whom He wills, implying some sins may not be forgiven, and the other indicates that all sins are enumerated for recompense. Then a group of Mu'tazila argues that if one avoids major sins, punishment for minor sins cannot occur, not because it is rationally impossible, but because textual evidence shows it does not happen; they cite the verse that promises expiation of misdeeds for those who avoid major sins. The response is that the 'absolute major sin' is disbelief (kufr), because it is the peak of sin. The explanation uses the linguistic principle that when a collective is addressed, the rule may apply to each individual distributively—for example, 'the people rode their mounts' means each person rode his own mount. Thus the verse about avoiding major sins applies to kufr, not to all major sins, so avoiding other major sins does not guarantee expiation. The Arabic example at the end is partially garbled in the OCR.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some Mu'tazila thought avoiding major sins guarantees no punishment for minor sins.
Correction: The promise of expiation applies specifically to avoiding kufr, not all major sins.

Checkpoint

A) Minor sins are automatically forgiven by avoiding major ones
B) Evil deeds can still be punished even if major sins are avoided
C) The absolute major sin is kufr, so the verse does not cover other major sins
D) The Quran contradicts itself on this issue

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position holds that punishment for minor sins is always possible; the Mu'tazila objection fails because the 'major sins' in the promise refer specifically to kufr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Consider your own heart: do you downplay small sins because you feel you're a 'good Muslim' overall? How will this passage's teaching about the possibility of punishment for any sin shape your repentance tonight?
