Affirming Intercession and Its Proofs
Taftazani affirms intercession and provides proofs from Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine of intercession for major sinners and the scriptural proofs that support it, including the clarification of a key logical nuance.

Core Idea
Intercession for major sinners is proven by widespread reports and Quranic context.

Taftazani begins by stating the established position: intercession is granted by prophets and righteous people on behalf of major sinners. This builds on the earlier principle that forgiveness is possible even without intercession. He then presents Quranic and hadith evidence, carefully addressing a potential misunderstanding about logical implication.

Guided Path
1
Read the affirmation
Read the first sentence noting that intercession is established for major sinners against the Mu'tazila, based on widespread reports.
The author is building on a prior principle: forgiveness is permissible without intercession, so with intercession it is even more fitting.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
Look at the two Quranic verses cited: one commanding the Prophet to seek forgiveness for believers, and the other denying intercession's benefit for disbelievers. Understand how the denial implies benefit for believers.
The author argues that denying intercession for disbelievers would be pointless if intercession did not benefit believers; context proves the point.
3
Clarify the logical nuance
Note the author's clarification: this argument does not rely on the concept of opposite implication (mafhūm al-mukhālafa). It is based on contextual appropriateness, not a universal logical rule.
This avoids a common objection from those who reject opposite implication.
4
Confirm hadith evidence
Read the prophetic hadith 'My intercession is for those who commit major sins from my community' and note that such hadiths are mutawātir in meaning.
This provides strong, multi-chain evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشفاعة ثابتة للرسل، والأخيار في حق أهل الكبائر بالمستفيض من الأخبار خلافا للمعتزلة. وهذا مبنى على ما سبق من جواز العفو والمغفرة بدون الشفاعة، فبالشفاعة أولى . وعندهم : لما لم يجز، لم تجز. لنا : قوله تعالى: ﴿ واستغفر لذنبك وللمؤمنينَ وَالْمُؤْمِنَاتِ ) [محمد: ١٩] وقوله تعالى : فما تنفعهم شفاعة الشافعين ﴾ [المدثر: ٤٨] فإن أسلوب هذا الكلام يدل على ثبوت الشفاعة في الجملة. وإلا لما كان لنفى نفعها عن الكافرين عند القصد إلى تقبيح حالهم وتحقيق بأسهم معنى. لأن مثل هذا المقام يقتضى أن يوسموا بما يخصهم لا بما يعمهم وغيرهم. وليس المراد أن تعليق الحكم بالكافر يدل على نفيه عما عداه، حتى يرد عليه أنه إنما يقوم حجة على من يقول بمفهوم المخالفة . وقوله عليه السلام : « شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتى ) وهو مشهور، بل الأحاديث فى باب الشافعة متواترة المعني: واحتجت المعتزلة بمثل قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَاتَّقُوا يَوْمًا لا تَجْزِي نَفْسٌ عَن نَّفْسٍ شَيئا ولا يقبل منها شَفَاعَة ﴾ [البقرة: ٤٨] وقوله تعالى: ﴿مَا للظالمين مِن حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شفيع يطاع كه [غافر: ١٨] :والجواب بعد تسليم دلالتها على العموم في الأشخاص والأزمان والأحوال - أنه : يجب تخصيصها بالكفار جمعا بين الأدلة . ولما كان أصل العفو والشفاعة ثابتا بالأدلة القطعية من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع، قالت المعتزلة بالعفو عن الصغائر مطلقا، وعن الكبائر بعد التوبة، وبالشفاعة لزيادة الثواب . كلاهما فاسد . أما الأول : فلان التائب ومرتكب الصغيرة المجتنب عن الكبيرة . لا يستحقان العذاب عندهم فلا معنى للعفو وأما الثاني: فلان النصوص الدالة على الشفاعة، بمعنى طلب العفو عن الجناية .
And intercession is established for the messengers and the righteous on behalf of those who commit major sins, according to widespread reports (mustafīḍ min al-akhbār), contrary to the Mu'tazila. This is based on what preceded regarding the permissibility of pardon and forgiveness without intercession, so by intercession it is even more so. According to them: since it is not permissible, it does not occur. Our proof: the saying of the Most High: 'And ask forgiveness for your sin and for the believing men and believing women' [Muhammad 19], and His saying: 'So the intercession of intercessors will not benefit them' [al-Muddaththir 48]. For the style of this speech indicates the establishment of intercession in general. Otherwise, there would be no meaning to denying its benefit for the disbelievers when the intent is to make their condition abhorrent and to realize their misery, because such a context requires that they be characterized by what is specific to them, not by what is common to them and others. And it is not intended that the attachment of the judgment to the disbeliever indicates its negation from others, such that it might be objected that it only constitutes an argument for those who hold the concept of opposite implication (mafhūm al-mukhālafa). And his saying, peace be upon him: 'My intercession is for those who commit major sins from my community' – and it is well-known; rather, the hadiths on the topic of intercession are mutawātir in meaning. The Mu'tazila argued with verses such as His saying: 'And fear a Day when no soul will avail another at all, nor will intercession be accepted from it' [al-Baqara 48], and His saying: 'For the wrongdoers there is no friend and no intercessor to be obeyed' [Ghafir 18]. The answer: after conceding their generality over persons, times, and circumstances – it is necessary to specify them to the disbelievers in order to reconcile the evidences. Since the principle of pardon and intercession is established by definitive proofs from the Book, the Sunna, and consensus, the Mu'tazila said: pardon for minor sins absolutely, and for major sins after repentance, and intercession for increase in reward. Both are corrupt. As for the first: because the repentant person and the committer of a minor sin who avoids major sins – according to them they do not deserve punishment, so pardon has no meaning. As for the second: because the texts indicating intercession are in the sense of seeking pardon for the offense.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal proof and refutation. It begins by affirming intercession for prophets and righteous people on behalf of major sinners, citing widespread reports against the Mu'tazila. The author notes that this builds on the previously established permissibility of forgiveness without intercession, making intercession even more fitting. He then presents proofs from the Quran: the command to the Prophet to seek forgiveness for believers implies intercession is possible; and the denial of intercession's benefit for disbelievers implies its benefit for believers, otherwise the denial would be meaningless. The author clarifies that this is not a fallacious argument relying on the concept of opposite implication (mafhūm al-mukhālafa), but a contextual inference. He also cites the prophetic hadith 'My intercession is for those who commit major sins from my community,' noting that the hadiths on intercession are mutawātir in meaning. The Mu'tazila object with verses that deny intercession in general terms; the author's response is to specify those verses to disbelievers in order to reconcile all evidence. Finally, the author refutes two corrupt views of the Mu'tazila: (1) that pardon is only for minor sins or major sins after repentance, which is meaningless because the repentant and those avoiding major sins don't deserve punishment; (2) that intercession is only for increase of reward, whereas the texts show it is for seeking pardon for offenses.

أهل الكبائر
المعتزلة
المستفيض
مفهوم المخالفة
متواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic proof from denying intercession for disbelievers relies on the fallacy of opposite implication.
Correction: Taftazani clarifies that it is based on contextual appropriateness, not on the logical rule of mafhum al-mukhalafa.

Intercession for major sinners is firmly established by Quranic context and mutawātir hadith, and the proof does not depend on a controversial logical principle.

Refuting Mu'tazila Objections and Corrupt Views
Taftazani refutes Mu'tazila objections and their two views on pardon and intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila objections to intercession and Taftazani's response, including the necessity of specifying general verses, and why their two views on pardon and intercession are corrupt.

Core Idea
General verses denying intercession are specified to disbelievers; Mu'tazila views on pardon contradict their own principles.

The Mu'tazila attempted to reject intercession by citing verses that seem to deny it universally. Taftazani responds by specifying those verses to disbelievers in order to harmonize all evidence. He then refutes two additional Mu'tazila positions: that pardon applies only to minor sins or after repentance, and that intercession is only for increasing reward. Both are shown to be inconsistent with the texts and the Mu'tazila's own reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila objections
Read the verses the Mu'tazila use to argue against intercession: al-Baqara 48 and Ghafir 18.
These verses seem to deny interception absolutely.
2
Understand the response
Taftazani concedes the verses are general but argues they must be specified to disbelievers to reconcile with the definitive proofs for intercession.
This is a standard principle of usul: general texts can be specified by other evidence.
3
Examine the two corrupt views
Read the Mu'tazila two views: (1) pardon only for minor sins or major after repentance, (2) intercession only for increase of reward. Understand why each is corrupt.
4
Refute the first view
The author points out that according to Mu'tazila, the repentant person and one who avoids major sins do not deserve punishment, so there is no need for pardon.
Thus their concept of pardon becomes meaningless.
5
Refute the second view
The author states that the texts about intercession refer to seeking pardon for offenses, not just increasing reward.
This aligns with the Sunni understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشفاعة ثابتة للرسل، والأخيار في حق أهل الكبائر بالمستفيض من الأخبار خلافا للمعتزلة. وهذا مبنى على ما سبق من جواز العفو والمغفرة بدون الشفاعة، فبالشفاعة أولى . وعندهم : لما لم يجز، لم تجز. لنا : قوله تعالى: ﴿ واستغفر لذنبك وللمؤمنينَ وَالْمُؤْمِنَاتِ ) [محمد: ١٩] وقوله تعالى : فما تنفعهم شفاعة الشافعين ﴾ [المدثر: ٤٨] فإن أسلوب هذا الكلام يدل على ثبوت الشفاعة في الجملة. وإلا لما كان لنفى نفعها عن الكافرين عند القصد إلى تقبيح حالهم وتحقيق بأسهم معنى. لأن مثل هذا المقام يقتضى أن يوسموا بما يخصهم لا بما يعمهم وغيرهم. وليس المراد أن تعليق الحكم بالكافر يدل على نفيه عما عداه، حتى يرد عليه أنه إنما يقوم حجة على من يقول بمفهوم المخالفة . وقوله عليه السلام : « شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتى ) وهو مشهور، بل الأحاديث فى باب الشافعة متواترة المعني: واحتجت المعتزلة بمثل قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَاتَّقُوا يَوْمًا لا تَجْزِي نَفْسٌ عَن نَّفْسٍ شَيئا ولا يقبل منها شَفَاعَة ﴾ [البقرة: ٤٨] وقوله تعالى: ﴿مَا للظالمين مِن حَمِيمٍ وَلَا شفيع يطاع كه [غافر: ١٨] :والجواب بعد تسليم دلالتها على العموم في الأشخاص والأزمان والأحوال - أنه : يجب تخصيصها بالكفار جمعا بين الأدلة . ولما كان أصل العفو والشفاعة ثابتا بالأدلة القطعية من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع، قالت المعتزلة بالعفو عن الصغائر مطلقا، وعن الكبائر بعد التوبة، وبالشفاعة لزيادة الثواب . كلاهما فاسد . أما الأول : فلان التائب ومرتكب الصغيرة المجتنب عن الكبيرة . لا يستحقان العذاب عندهم فلا معنى للعفو وأما الثاني: فلان النصوص الدالة على الشفاعة، بمعنى طلب العفو عن الجناية .
And intercession is established for the messengers and the righteous on behalf of those who commit major sins, according to widespread reports (mustafīḍ min al-akhbār), contrary to the Mu'tazila. This is based on what preceded regarding the permissibility of pardon and forgiveness without intercession, so by intercession it is even more so. According to them: since it is not permissible, it does not occur. Our proof: the saying of the Most High: 'And ask forgiveness for your sin and for the believing men and believing women' [Muhammad 19], and His saying: 'So the intercession of intercessors will not benefit them' [al-Muddaththir 48]. For the style of this speech indicates the establishment of intercession in general. Otherwise, there would be no meaning to denying its benefit for the disbelievers when the intent is to make their condition abhorrent and to realize their misery, because such a context requires that they be characterized by what is specific to them, not by what is common to them and others. And it is not intended that the attachment of the judgment to the disbeliever indicates its negation from others, such that it might be objected that it only constitutes an argument for those who hold the concept of opposite implication (mafhūm al-mukhālafa). And his saying, peace be upon him: 'My intercession is for those who commit major sins from my community' – and it is well-known; rather, the hadiths on the topic of intercession are mutawātir in meaning. The Mu'tazila argued with verses such as His saying: 'And fear a Day when no soul will avail another at all, nor will intercession be accepted from it' [al-Baqara 48], and His saying: 'For the wrongdoers there is no friend and no intercessor to be obeyed' [Ghafir 18]. The answer: after conceding their generality over persons, times, and circumstances – it is necessary to specify them to the disbelievers in order to reconcile the evidences. Since the principle of pardon and intercession is established by definitive proofs from the Book, the Sunna, and consensus, the Mu'tazila said: pardon for minor sins absolutely, and for major sins after repentance, and intercession for increase in reward. Both are corrupt. As for the first: because the repentant person and the committer of a minor sin who avoids major sins – according to them they do not deserve punishment, so pardon has no meaning. As for the second: because the texts indicating intercession are in the sense of seeking pardon for the offense.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal proof and refutation. It begins by affirming intercession for prophets and righteous people on behalf of major sinners, citing widespread reports against the Mu'tazila. The author notes that this builds on the previously established permissibility of forgiveness without intercession, making intercession even more fitting. He then presents proofs from the Quran: the command to the Prophet to seek forgiveness for believers implies intercession is possible; and the denial of intercession's benefit for disbelievers implies its benefit for believers, otherwise the denial would be meaningless. The author clarifies that this is not a fallacious argument relying on the concept of opposite implication (mafhūm al-mukhālafa), but a contextual inference. He also cites the prophetic hadith 'My intercession is for those who commit major sins from my community,' noting that the hadiths on intercession are mutawātir in meaning. The Mu'tazila object with verses that deny intercession in general terms; the author's response is to specify those verses to disbelievers in order to reconcile all evidence. Finally, the author refutes two corrupt views of the Mu'tazila: (1) that pardon is only for minor sins or major sins after repentance, which is meaningless because the repentant and those avoiding major sins don't deserve punishment; (2) that intercession is only for increase of reward, whereas the texts show it is for seeking pardon for offenses.

Correction: The texts show intercession is for seeking pardon for offenses, as Taftazani states.

Key Takeaway
General Quranic verses that seem to deny intercession are specified to disbelievers, and the Mu'tazila views on pardon and intercession are logically and textually corrupt.

Believers Who Commit Major Sins Will Not Remain in Hell Forever
Taftazani proves that sinful believers are not eternally in Hell and refutes Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ash'ari theology affirms that sinful believers are not eternally in Hell, based on Quranic texts and rational justice, and how it differs from the Mu'tazila position.

Core Idea
Faith guarantees eventual salvation, even if sin requires punishment.

This passage from Taftazani's commentary addresses a critical question in Islamic theology: the fate of believers who die without repenting from major sins. The Ash'ari position holds that faith ultimately secures Paradise, though punishment may be experienced. Taftazani presents Quranic and rational arguments to show that eternal Hell is reserved for disbelievers alone, then introduces the opposing Mu'tazila view for contrast.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own argument come through.
2
Identify the Quranic proofs
The author cites three verses. Note how each supports the idea that sinful believers will eventually be saved.
The first verse is from Surah al-Zalzala, the others from Surah al-Tawba and Surah al-Kahf.
3
Understand the rational argument
The author argues that eternal punishment would be unjust for a believer, as it exceeds the measure of the crime.
This is a justice-based argument.
4
Contrast with the Mu'tazila position
The Mu'tazila argue that anyone in Hell is either a disbeliever or an unrepentant major sinner, and both are eternal.
Their first reason: one cannot simultaneously deserve pure lasting harm and pure lasting benefit.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this doctrine balances divine justice and mercy, and its practical effect on a believer's hope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( وأهل الكبائر من المؤمنين لا يخلدون في النار) وإن ماتوا من غير توبة لقوله تعالى : فمن يعمل مثقال ذرة خيرا يره ﴾ [الزلزلة : ٧] ونفس الإيمان عمل خير لا يمكن أن يرى جزاءه قبل دخول النار، ثم يدخل النار فيخلد، لأنه باطل بالإجماع. فتعين الخروج من النار . ولقوله تعالى : ( وَعَدَ اللهُ الْمُؤمِنِينَ وَالْمُؤمِنَاتِ جَنَّاتٍ تَجْرِي مِن تَحْتِهَا الأنهار ﴾ [التوبة : ٧٢] ولقوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ كَانت لَهم جنات الفردوس نزلا ﴾ [الكهف : ١٠٧] إلى غير ذلك من النصوص الدالة على كون المؤمن من أهل الجنة، مع ما سبق من الأدلة القاطعة على أن العبد لا يخرج بالمعصية عن الإيمان وأيضا : الخلود في النار من أعظم العقوبات. وقد جعل جزاء للكفر الذي هو أعظم الجنايات فلو جوزى به غير الكافر، لكان زيادة على قدر الجناية، فلا يكون عدلا . وذهبت المعتزلة إلى أن من أدخل النار فهو خالد فيها لأنه إما كافر أو صاحب كبيرة مات بلا توبة إذ المعصوم والتائب وصاحب الصغيرة إذا اجتنبوا الكبائر، ليسوا من أهل النار - على ما سبق من أصولهم - والكافر مخلد بالإجماع. وكذا صاحب الكبيرة بلا توبة .(۱) لوجهين أحدهما : أنه يستحق العذاب وهو مضرة خالصة دائمة فينافي استحقاق الثواب، الذى هو منفعة خالصة دائمة .
And those who commit major sins among the believers will not remain eternally in Hell, even if they die without repentance, due to His saying, the Most High: 'So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it' [al-Zalzala 7]. And faith itself is a good deed; it is impossible that its reward be seen before entering Hell, then he enters Hell and remains eternally, because that is invalid by consensus. So exiting from Hell is determined. And due to His saying, the Most High: 'Allah has promised the believing men and believing women gardens beneath which rivers flow' [al-Tawba 72], and His saying: 'Indeed, those who have believed and done righteous deeds – they will have the Gardens of Paradise as a lodging' [al-Kahf 107], and other texts indicating that the believer is among the people of Paradise, along with what preceded of definitive proofs that a servant does not exit faith by sin. And also: eternal stay in Hell is among the greatest punishments, and it has been made the recompense for disbelief, which is the greatest crime. So if someone other than a disbeliever were punished with it, it would be an excess beyond the measure of the crime, and it would not be just. And the Mu'tazila held that whoever is entered into Hell is eternal in it, because he is either a disbeliever or a committer of a major sin who died without repentance, since the infallible, the repentant, and the committer of a minor sin who avoids major sins are not among the people of Hell – according to what preceded of their principles – and the disbeliever is eternal by consensus. Likewise, the committer of a major sin without repentance. (1) For two reasons: one of them is that he deserves punishment, which is a pure and lasting harm, and it contradicts the deserving of reward, which is a pure and lasting benefit.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal proof for the Ash'ari position that believers who commit major sins will not be eternally in Hell. The author provides several Quranic proofs. Firstly, the verse 'whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it' – and faith is a good deed that must see its reward; if the believer enters Hell and remains eternally, the good deed's reward is never seen, which is invalid by consensus. Therefore, the believer must exit Hell. Secondly, several verses promise Paradise to believers absolutely, implying they will eventually enter it. Thirdly, the principle that sin does not remove faith, so the believer remains a believer and thus deserves Paradise ultimately. Fourthly, a justice argument: eternal punishment is for the greatest crime, i.e., disbelief; punishing a believer with eternal punishment would be an unjust excess. Then the author presents the Mu'tazila position: they argue that whoever enters Hell is eternal because they are either a disbeliever or a major sinner without repentance, and since minor sinners and repentant people do not enter Hell, only those two categories enter, and both are eternal. They give two reasons: (1) the one who deserves punishment (pure lasting harm) cannot also deserve reward (pure lasting benefit). The text gives only the first reason on this page.

Key Terms
الخلود (eternity)
الكبائر (major sins)
الإيمان (faith)
المعتزلة (Mu'tazila)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Ash'ari position means sin is insignificant or that believers will not be punished at all.
Correction: The Ash'ari view does not deny punishment for major sins; rather, it holds that faith guarantees eventual salvation, even if punishment occurs in Hell before entering Paradise.

Checkpoint

A) Because all believers are forgiven without punishment
B) Because faith is a good deed that must see its reward, and eternal Hell would prevent that
C) Because God's mercy overrides justice
D) Because major sins are not really punishable

Key Takeaway
Faith, even with sin, ensures that a believer will ultimately enter Paradise after any necessary punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What would change in your life if you fully internalized that your faith is a good deed that Allah will surely reward—even after any punishment He may decree?
?

?
The Mu'tazila argue that a pure lasting harm cannot coexist with pure lasting benefit. Do you live as though your good deeds and bad deeds are in competition, or do you trust that Allah can forgive and still grant Paradise? What would you need to change to live with that trust?

First Response to Eternal Punishment Claim
Sanusi denies the necessity of eternal punishment for major sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the claim that major sinners must be eternally punished by denying both the necessity of perpetuity and the notion of obligatory punishment.

Core Idea
God's punishment is just, not obligatory; His mercy can override it.

This lesson presents Sanusi's first response to the objection that major sinners deserve eternal punishment. He counters by distinguishing between entitlement (istihqāq) and necessity (ījāb), and by framing reward as grace and punishment as justice. This preserves God's absolute sovereignty and mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the concise style and the key terms.
Pay attention to the words 'al-dawām' (perpetuity) and 'isti'jāb' (necessitation).
2
Identify the two denials
The passage makes two denials: first, denying the condition of perpetuity; second, denying the sense of entitlement as necessity. Find these and see how they connect.
3
Understand the positive statement
The passage then states that reward is grace (faḍl) and punishment is justice ('adl). Reflect on how this reframes the discussion.
Justice does not imply obligation; it means God acts appropriately.
4
Consider the implications
Think about how this answer upholds both God's mercy (He may forgive) and His justice (He may punish for a time).
This preserves God's absolute sovereignty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب منع قيد الدوام، بل منع الاستحقاق بالمعنى الذي قصدوه وهو الاستيجاب. وإنما الثواب فضل منه والعذاب عدل. فإن شاء عفا وإن شاء عذبه مدة ثم يدخله الجنة.
The answer is to deny the condition of perpetuity, rather to deny entitlement in the sense they intended, which is necessity. Reward is but His bounty and punishment is justice. If He wills, He forgives; if He wills, He punishes him for a period then admits him to Paradise.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage presents the first response to the objection that major sinners deserve eternal punishment. It is a refutation of the claim that punishment is necessarily perpetual. The author denies two things: first, the condition of perpetuity (al-dawām) as inherent to the punishment, and second, the very notion that the sinner deserves punishment in the sense of it being obligatory (isti'jāb) upon God. Instead, reward is a pure favor (faḍl) from God, while punishment is an act of justice ('adl). This means God is not obliged to punish; He may forgive entirely. If He does punish, it need not be eternal—He may punish for a limited duration and then admit the person to Paradise. The argument preserves God's absolute sovereignty and mercy while upholding His justice.

Key Terms
الاستحقاق
الاستيجاب
الفضل
العدل
الخلود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'justice' here implies God must punish, or that the sinner has a right to punishment.
Correction: The passage clarifies that justice does not mean obligation; it means God's actions are appropriate. Punishment is not necessitated by any external claim.

Checkpoint

B) Because the condition of perpetuity is denied and punishment is not necessary
C) Because all sinners are forgiven automatically
D) Because punishment is not justice

Key Takeaway
God's justice does not obligate eternal punishment; He may forgive or punish temporarily according to His will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says reward is pure bounty (فضل) from God. When you do good deeds, do you expect God to reward you out of obligation? How can you cultivate a mindset that sees every blessing as undeserved favor, and how would that transform your gratitude?
?
If punishment is justice but not necessary, and God may forgive or punish temporarily, then every moment you are alive is a chance for His mercy. What are you doing today to seek that mercy, knowing that it is not guaranteed but is a gift? Will you let this truth move you to sincere action?

Second Response: Refuting Eternal Punishment Verses
Sanusi answers three verses used to prove eternal punishment for sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets verses about eternal punishment to apply only to disbelievers, and how he uses alternative meanings and textual opposition to refute the objection.

Core Idea
Eternal punishment verses actually target disbelievers, not believing sinners.

The objection that certain Qur'anic verses threaten believers with eternal punishment is met with a nuanced response. Sanusi shows that these verses describe disbelievers, that the word 'khulūd' can mean a long stay, and that other texts contradict eternal punishment for believers. This lesson unpacks that multi-layered defense.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three verses cited
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice which three verses are quoted to support the claim of eternal punishment.
The verses are from Surah al-Nisa' and Surah al-Baqarah.
2
Understand the first level of response: the persons are disbelievers
Sanusi argues that the killer of a believer, the one who transgresses all limits, and the one encompassed by sin are actually disbelievers. Reflect on why this interpretation removes the threat from sinful believers.
This is the primary refutation.
3
Study the second and third responses
Even if the verses applied to believers, Sanusi offers two further defenses: 'khulūd' can mean a lengthy stay, and other texts oppose eternal punishment. Notice how each level strengthens the argument.
These are conditional responses ('if it were granted').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : النصوص الدالة على الخلود . كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مؤمنا متعمدا فجزاؤه جهنم خالدا فيها ﴾ [النساء: ٩٣ ] وقوله تعالى : ومن يعص الله ورسوله ويتعدَّ حدوده يدخلهُ نَارًا خَالِدًا فِيهَا . [النساء : ١٤) وقوله تعالى : مَن كَسَبَ سَيِّئَةً وَأَحَاطَتْ بِهِ خَطِيئَتَهُ فَأُولَئِكَ أَصْحَاب النَّارِ هم فيها خالدون ﴾ [البقرة : ۸۱] والجواب : أن قاتل المؤمن لكونه مؤمنا لا يكون إلا الكافر. وكذا تعدى جميع الحدود وكذا من أحاطت به خطيئته وشملته من كل جانب. ولو سلم، فالخلود قد يستعمل في المكث الطويل كقولهم: سجن مخلد . ولو سلم. فمعارض بالنصوص الدالة على عدم الخلود - كما مر.
Second: the texts indicating eternity (al-khulūd). Such as His saying: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein forever.' [Sūrat al-Nisā', 93] And His saying: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger and transgresses His limits, He will cause him to enter a fire, abiding therein forever.' [Sūrat al-Nisā', 14] And His saying: 'Whoever earns evil and his sin encompasses him, those are the companions of the Fire, they will abide therein forever.' [Sūrat al-Baqarah, 81] And the answer: That the killer of a believer, on account of being a believer, is none other than a disbeliever. Likewise, transgressing all the limits, and likewise the one whose sin encompasses him and surrounds him from every side. And if it were granted, then 'eternity' (al-khulūd) may be used to mean lengthy stay, as they say: an eternal prison. And if it were granted, then it is opposed by texts indicating non-eternity, as has passed.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage presents a second objection and its answer concerning verses that explicitly use 'khālidan fīhā' (abiding forever) for certain sinners. The objection cites three verses: one about intentional murder of a believer, one about disobeying God and His Messenger and transgressing limits, and one about being encompassed by sin. The answer offers three levels of response. First, the persons described in these verses are actually disbelievers, not believers who commit minor sins. The intentional killer of a believer is a disbeliever because killing a believer is kufr; similarly, transgression of all limits and being entirely surrounded by sin indicates unbelief. Second, even if the verses referred to sinful believers, the word 'khulūd' can mean a long duration, not necessarily eternal. Third, even if it meant eternal, these verses are opposed by other texts that indicate non-eternity for believers who enter Hell, as previously mentioned. Thus the objection is refuted.

Key Terms
الخلود
النصوص
المكث الطويل
المعارضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verses about eternal punishment prove that sinful believers will remain in Hell forever.
Correction: The verses either describe disbelievers, use 'khulūd' in a non-eternal sense, or are opposed by other texts that affirm eventual salvation for believers.

Checkpoint
What is the primary interpretation given for the verse about the killer of a believer?
A) The killer is a believer who will be forgiven
B) The killer is a disbeliever because killing a believer makes one a disbeliever
C) The verse is abrogated
D) The word 'khulūd' means a few days

Key Takeaway
Verses threatening eternal punishment are directed at disbelievers, not sinful believers; the term 'khulūd' can also mean a lengthy stay, and other texts oppose eternal punishment for believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading Sanusi's argument, do you still fear that a major sin (excluding disbelief) will cause you to remain in Hell forever? What verse or reasoning from this lesson gives you hope, and how will you use that hope to motivate repentance instead of despair?
?
The lesson shows that 'khulūd' can mean a long time, not necessarily forever. Does your understanding of Allah's mercy allow for a temporary punishment for believers? How does this affect your view of God's justice and mercy in your own life?
?
Sanusi argued that the intentional killer of a believer is a disbeliever. Reflect: Do you harbor hatred or enmity towards any believer that could be seen as a form of 'killing' (spiritually)? What step will you take today to purify your heart from such feelings?

The Number of Prophets and the Caution Against Specifying
Discussion on the number of prophets and caution against specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why specifying a precise number for the prophets is discouraged in Islamic theology and the reasons based on Quran and hadith methodology.

Core Idea
It is safer not to specify the number of prophets than to risk error.

This passage from the Sharh al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya deals with a common question: how many prophets were sent? While a hadith mentions numbers like 124,000 or 224,000, the author advises caution. He explains that specifying a number can lead to serious errors, and that such reports are not reliable enough for matters of belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic carefully
Read the passage once, noting the two narrations and the Quranic verse. Let the author's own words guide your initial understanding.
Pay attention to the phrase 'والأولي أن لا يقتصر على عدد'.
2
Identify the author's main point
The author says it is preferable not to restrict to a number. Why does he say that? What evidence does he present?
3
Understand the reasoning
The reasoning involves two parts: the risk of including/excluding prophets, and the weakness of solitary reports (khabar al-wahid) in matters of belief.
The author says that even if such a report meets all conditions, it only yields probability (zann), which carries no weight in beliefs.
4
Reflect on the application
Consider how this principle applies to other matters of belief. Why would a number term be problematic?
Number terms are precise and do not allow addition or subtraction, so a mistake would be serious.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عدد الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام. وقد روى بيان عدتهم في بعض الأحاديث على ما روى أن النبي عليه السلام سئل عن عدد الأنبياء. فقال : ( مائة ألف وأربع وعشرون ألفا وفى رواية : ( مائنا ألف وأربع وعشرون ألفا ) والأولي أن لا يقتصر على عدد في التسمية فقد قال الله تعالى : ﴿ ورسلا قد وَرَسُلاً قَصَصْناهُمْ عَلَيْكَ من قَبْلُ وَرُسُلاً لَّمْ نَقْصُصْهُمْ عَلَيْكَ ﴾ [النساء: ١٦٤] ولا يؤمن في ذكر العدد أن يدخل فيهم من ليس منهم إن ذكر عدد أكثر من عددهم. أو يخرج منهم من هو فيهم إن ذكر عدد أقل من عددهم م یعنى أن خبر الواحد على تقدير اشتماله على جميع الشرائط المذكورة في أصول الفقه، لا يفيد إلا الظن ولا عبرة بالظن في باب الاعتقادات خصوصا إذا اشتمل على اختلاف رواية وكان القول بموجبه مما يفضى إلى مخالفة ظاهر الكتاب. وهو أن بعض الأنبياء لم يذكر للنبي عليه السلام ويحتمل مخالفة الواقع. وهو عد النبي عليه السلام من غير الأنبياء وغير النبى من الأنبياء، بناء على أن اسم العدد خاص فى مدلوله لا يحتمل الزيادة ولا النقصان .
The number of prophets, peace be upon them. And it has been narrated regarding the statement of their number in some hadiths according to what was narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, was asked about the number of prophets. So he said: 'One hundred thousand and twenty-four thousand.' And in a narration: 'Two hundred thousand and twenty-four thousand.' And the preferable is not to restrict to a number in naming, for Allah Most High said: 'And messengers We have mentioned to you before and messengers We have not mentioned to you.' [an-Nisa:164]. And one is not safe in mentioning the number from including among them those who are not of them if a number greater than their number is mentioned, or excluding from them those who are among them if a number less than their number is mentioned. That is, the solitary report (khabar al-wahid), on the assumption that it includes all the conditions mentioned in the principles of jurisprudence (usul al-fiqh), yields only probability (zann), and probability has no weight in matters of beliefs, especially if it includes a difference in narration and acting upon it leads to opposing the apparent meaning of the Book. And that is that some prophets were not mentioned to the Prophet, peace be upon him, and it may contradict reality. And it is counting the Prophet, peace be upon him, among non-prophets and a non-prophet among prophets, based on the fact that the number term is specific in its denotation, not allowing increase or decrease.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the number of prophets and a caution against specifying a precise number. It begins by stating the topic and then mentions a hadith giving 124,000 or 224,000 prophets. The author then advises that it is preferable not to restrict to a specific number, citing Quran 4:164 which indicates that there are prophets not mentioned. The reason given is that if one specifies a number higher than the actual count, one might include false prophets; if lower, one might exclude true ones. The author then explains that this concern arises because the hadith in question is a solitary report (khabar al-wahid), which only yields probability (zann) and is not reliable in matters of belief, especially when it conflicts with the Quran's general statement. Furthermore, specifying a number could lead to serious errors like counting a prophet as a non-prophet or vice versa, because number terms are precise and do not tolerate addition or subtraction.

Key Terms
عدد الأنبياء
خبر الواحد
ظن
اعتقادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is obligatory to believe that the number of prophets is exactly 124,000 or 224,000.
Correction: The author advises against specifying a number because such reports are only probable and can lead to error. It is safer to affirm that there are many prophets, some known and some unknown.

Checkpoint
Why does the author advise against specifying a number for the prophets?
A) Because hadith reports are weak
B) Because the Quran mentions all prophets
C) Because it risks including false prophets or excluding true ones
D) Because the number is unknown

Key Takeaway
In matters of belief, it is better to rely on certain knowledge from the Quran and mutawatir reports rather than on solitary reports that only yield probability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you accept a belief about your faith based on a single hadith or opinion without verifying it against the Quran and certain knowledge? What is one such belief you hold that you have not examined critically?
?
If you were to find out that you have been acting on a weak assumption in a matter of belief, would you be willing to change your stance? What would that require from you today?
?
The passage warns against including or excluding prophets. In your daily life, where are you quick to categorize people or beliefs as 'correct' or 'incorrect' without sufficient certainty? How can you apply this caution?

Angels: Servants Without Gender
Definition of angels and negation of gender attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic definition of angels as servants of Allah who act by His command, and why they are not described as male or female.

Core Idea
Angels are Allah's obedient servants; they have no gender.

Before discussing the attributes of angels, the author establishes their fundamental nature as servants of Allah who act solely by His command. He also clarifies a common misconception: angels are not male or female, as neither revelation nor reason supports such a description.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get a feel for the language and structure. Notice the citation of two Qur'anic verses.
The verses are from Surat al-Anbiya'.
2
Identify the key attributes
Look for the attributes mentioned: acting by Allah's command, not preceding Him in speech, not weary of worship, and not being described as male or female.
3
Understand the basis for negating gender
The author states that no scriptural transmission (naql) nor reason ('aql) supports describing angels as male or female. Consider why this is important in the context of refuting polytheistic beliefs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الملائكة والملائكة عباد الله تعالى العاملون بأمره على ما دل عليه قوله تعالي : لا يَسْبِقُونَهُ بالقَول وَهُم بِأَمْرِه يَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الانبياء : ٢٧] ولا يَسْتَكْبِرُونَ عَنْ عِبَادَتِهِ وَلَا يستخسرون [الأنبياء : ١٩] لا يوصفون بذكورة ولا أنوثة إذ لم يرد بذلك نقل ولا دل عليه عقل وما زعم عبدة الأصنام أنهم بنات الله تعالى محال باطل، وإفراط في شأنهم. كما أن قول اليهود إن الواحد منهم قد يرتكب الكفر ويعاقبه الله بالمسخ ، تفريط وتقصير في حالهم. فإن قيل : اليس قد كفر إبليس، وكان من الملائكة، بدليل صحة استثنائه منهم ؟ . قلنا : لا بل كان من الجن، ففسق عن أمر ربه، لكنه لما كان في صفة الملائكة في باب العبادة ورفع الدرجة وكان جنيا واحدا مغمورا بالعبادة فيما بينهم، صح استثناؤه منهم تغليبا .
Discourse on angels. And the angels are servants of Allah Almighty, acting by His command, as indicated by His saying, the Most High: 'They do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command' [Qur'an 21:27], and 'They do not disdain His worship nor do they become weary' [Qur'an 21:19]. They are not described as male or female, since no transmission (naql) has come regarding that, nor does reason indicate it. And what the idolaters claimed—that they are daughters of Allah—is impossible, false, and exaggeration regarding their status. Likewise, the saying of the Jews that one of them may commit disbelief and Allah punishes him by transformation (maskh) is deficiency and shortcoming in their state. If it is said: 'Did not Iblis commit disbelief, and was he from the angels, as proven by the validity of his exclusion from them?' We say: No, rather he was from the jinn, and he deviated from the command of his Lord. However, since he was in the likeness of the angels in terms of worship and high rank, and he was a single jinn overwhelmed by worship among them, his exclusion from them is valid as a predominant consideration (taghlīb).
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a theological discourse on angels. It begins by defining angels as servants of Allah who act by His command, citing Qur'an 21:27 and 21:19. It then states that angels are not described as male or female, because no revelation (naql) or reason supports such description. The passage refutes two false beliefs: first, the idolaters' claim that angels are daughters of God—this is impossible, false, and an exaggeration. Second, the Jews' claim that some angels commit disbelief and are punished by transformation (maskh) into animals—this is a deficiency in understanding their status. Then an objection is raised: Did not Iblis commit disbelief, and was he not from the angels, as proven by the validity of his exclusion from them in the Qur'an (when they were commanded to prostrate, Iblis was excluded)? The answer is: No, Iblis was from the jinn, not angels; he deviated from his Lord's command. However, because he resembled angels in worship and high rank, and he was a single jinn immersed in worship among them, his exclusion from them is valid as a predominant consideration (taghlīb), meaning he is included in the address predominantly despite being of a different kind.

Key Terms
ملائكة
ذكورة
أنوثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Angels are either male or female.
Correction: Neither revelation nor reason indicates any gender for angels; they are purely spiritual beings.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what do the Qur'anic verses cited indicate about angels?
A) They are greater than Allah in rank
B) They act by Allah's command and worship tirelessly
C) They have free will to disobey
D) They are male

Key Takeaway
Angels are obedient servants of Allah, without gender, as both scripture and reason affirm.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly see yourself as a servant of Allah, acting by His command in all matters, or do you sometimes act based on your own desires? How can you embody the angels' example of obedience today?
?
The passage says angels are not described as male or female. How does this challenge any assumptions you might have about gender roles in worship or status with Allah? Are you holding onto any cultural beliefs that limit your understanding of devotion?
?
Angels never weary of worship. When do you find yourself weary in your worship? What change can you make today to seek sincerity rather than convenience?

Refuting False Beliefs About Angels and the Case of Iblis
Refutation of false beliefs and the Iblis objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refutation of two false beliefs about angels and the explanation of why Iblis, though a jinn, is excluded from the angels by taghlib.

Core Idea
False beliefs about angels are refuted, and Iblis is clarified as a jinn, not an angel.

After establishing the true attributes of angels, the author addresses two erroneous beliefs: that angels are daughters of God (as claimed by polytheists) and that angels can commit disbelief and be punished by transformation (as claimed by Jews). He then tackles an objection about Iblis, explaining that Iblis was a jinn, not an angel, and his exclusion is valid due to taghlib.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on refutations
Read the Arabic text that refutes the idolaters' and Jews' claims. Notice the strong language: 'impossible, false' and 'deficiency'.
The refutations are based on the earlier definition of angels as obedient servants.
2
Analyze the objection about Iblis
Read the objection and answer. Note the claim that since Iblis was excluded from the angels, he must have been an angel. The answer uses the principle of taghlib.
Taghlib means giving predominance to the majority.
3
Understand the taghlib principle
The author explains that Iblis was from the jinn, but due to his resemblance to angels in worship and rank, he was included under the term 'angels' in the verse commanding prostration. This is a linguistic and contextual usage.

Angels: Nature and Refutation of Deviant Views
Defines angels and refutes deviant views on their nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic definition of angels, their genderlessness, and the refutation of extreme views about them.

Core Idea
Angels are genderless servants of Allah, neither daughters of Allah nor agents of sin.

This lesson begins the discourse on angels by establishing their nature as obedient servants of Allah. It clarifies that they are not described as male or female, and then refutes two erroneous beliefs: the polytheists' claim that angels are Allah's daughters, and the Jewish notion that some angels can commit disbelief and be punished by transformation. Understanding these refutations is key to maintaining a balanced creed about the angelic realm.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening definition
Read the Arabic passage from 'الكلام في الملائكة' to 'ولا يستحسرون'. Notice how the author uses Quranic verses to define angels as obedient servants.
The verses are from Surah Al-Anbiya.
2
Understand the genderlessness
The author states angels are not described as male or female because no textual or rational evidence supports it. This is a point of tawqif (reliance on revelation).
3
Refute the idolaters' claim
The polytheists said angels are daughters of Allah. The author declares this impossible, false, and excessive. Reflect on why this is a serious deviation.
The refutation is based on divine transcendence.
4
Refute the Jewish claim
The Jews suggested some angels could commit disbelief and be punished by transformation. The author calls this neglect and deficiency. Compare this with the earlier excess.
Both extremes are rejected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الملائكة ) والملائكة عباد الله تعالى العاملون بأمره على ما دل عليه قوله تعالي : لا يَسْبِقُونَهُ بالقَول وَهُم بِأَمْرِه يَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الانبياء : ٢٧] ولا يَسْتَكْبِرُونَ عَنْ عِبَادَتِهِ وَلَا يستخسرون ) [الأنبياء : ١٩] (لا يوصفون بذكورة ولا أنوثة إذ لم يرد بذلك نقل ولا دل عليه عقل وما زعم عبدة الأصنام أنهم بنات الله تعالى محال باطل، وإفراط في شأنهم. كما أن قول اليهود إن الواحد منهم قد يرتكب الكفر ويعاقبه الله بالمسخ ، تفريط وتقصير في حالهم. فإن قيل : اليس قد كفر إبليس، وكان من الملائكة، بدليل صحة استثنائه منهم ؟ . قلنا : لا بل كان من الجن، فسق عن أمر ربه، لكنه لما كان في صفة الملائكة في باب العبادة ورفع الدرجة وكان جنيا واحدا مغمورا بالعبادة فيما بينهم، صح استثناؤه منهم تغليبا . وأما هاروت وماروت فالأصح أنهما ملكان ، لم يصدر عنهما کفر ولا كبيرة، وتعذيبهما إنما هو على وجه المعاتبة، كما يعاتب الأنبياء على الزلة والسهو، وكانا يعظان الناس، ويعلمان السحر ، ويقولان : إِنَّمَا نَحْنُ فتنة فلا تكفر ﴾ [البقرة : ١٠٢] ولا كفر في تعليم : السحر، بل في اعتقاده والعمل به
The discourse on angels. And the angels are the servants of Allah Almighty, acting by His command according to His statement: 'They do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command' [Al-Anbiya 27] and 'They do not grow arrogant in worshiping Him nor do they become weary' [Al-Anbiya 19]. They are not described as male or female, as no transmitted text or reason indicates that. And what the idolaters claimed that they are daughters of Allah is impossible, false, and excess regarding them. Also, the saying of the Jews that one of them may commit disbelief and Allah punishes him by transformation is neglect and deficiency concerning their state. If it is said: Did not Iblis disbelieve, and he was from the angels, based on the validity of excluding him from them? We say: No, rather he was from the jinn, so he transgressed against the command of his Lord; but since he was in the form of the angels in terms of worship and high rank, and he was a single jinni immersed in worship among them, the exclusion of him from them is valid by way of prevalent classification. As for Harut and Marut, the most correct is that they are two angels; no disbelief or major sin issued from them; their punishment is only by way of rebuke, just as the prophets are rebuked for slip-ups and oversight. And they used to admonish people and teach sorcery, and they said: 'We are only a trial, so do not disbelieve' [Al-Baqarah 102]. There is no disbelief in teaching sorcery, but rather in believing in it and acting upon it.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion on angels. It begins by defining angels as obedient servants of Allah, citing two Quranic verses. Then it states that angels are not characterized by gender because no revelation or reason supports that. Next, it refutes two extreme views: the polytheists who claimed angels are Allah's daughters (excess) and the Jews who said some angels can commit disbelief and be punished by transformation (neglect). The author then addresses an objection: if Iblis disbelieved, and he was from the angels (since the Quran excludes him from them in the prostration command), how can angels be sinless? The answer is that Iblis was actually from the jinn, not angels. He was included among the angels only by prevalent classification because he resembled them in worship and rank. Finally, the author discusses Harut and Marut: they are two angels who did not commit disbelief or major sin. Their punishment was only a light rebuke, similar to prophets being rebuked for minor slips. They taught magic as a trial, but they warned people not to disbelieve. The sin is in believing and practicing magic, not in teaching it.

Key Terms
الملائكة
عباد
ذكورة
أنوثة
بنات الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Angels are daughters of Allah or can sin and be transformed.
Correction: Angels are genderless servants; they are neither daughters of Allah nor capable of sin as per the Quran and reason.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why are angels not described as male or female?
A) Because reason alone shows they have no gender
B) Because no transmitted text or reason indicates that
C) Because they are spirits only
D) Because they are all male

Key Takeaway
Angels are obedient, genderless servants; claims that they are divine or sinful are extremes to be avoided.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The polytheists called angels 'daughters of Allah'—an exaggeration; the Jews said angels could sin—a belittlement. Which extreme are you more prone to in your own thoughts about Allah's creation? Will you commit today to holding the balanced position that angels are honorable servants, neither divine nor sinful?
?
You have now learned that angels never disobey and never weary. How does this compare to your own worship? Is there any act of obedience you find too burdensome, or any sin you think you cannot avoid? Let this lesson remind you of beings who serve Allah tirelessly. Will you ask Allah to increase your sincerity and endurance?
?
The author says angels are 'not described as male or female' because no text or reason supports it. Have you ever imagined angels with human attributes without evidence? How does this teach you to submit to revelation alone when the intellect cannot decide? Can you identify another area where you might be speaking about the unseen without proof?

Iblis: Not an Angel, But Jinni Resembling Angels
Answers the objection about Iblis's origin and exclusion from angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Iblis is excluded from the angels in the Quran and why he was actually from the jinn.

Core Idea
Iblis was a jinni whose exclusion from angels is by prevalent classification due to resemblance.

A common objection arises from the Quranic verse where Iblis is excepted from the angels' prostration to Adam. Does this imply Iblis was an angel? The author addresses this clearly: Iblis was from the jinn, not angels. His inclusion among the angels in the exception is due to his resemblance in worship and rank. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and clarifies a potential confusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read from 'فإن قيل : اليس قد كفر إبليس' to 'صح استثناؤه منهم تغليبا'. Notice the objection and the author's reply.
The objection uses the exception in the Quran (إلا إبليس).
2
Understand the author's claim
The author says Iblis was from the jinn, not angels, and explains that his exclusion is 'taghliban' (prevalent classification). He was a single jinni immersed in worship among angels.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.
3
Reflect on the term 'taghlib'
'Taghlib' means treating something as predominant or including it under a category due to similarity. This is a linguistic and legal principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الملائكة ) والملائكة عباد الله تعالى العاملون بأمره على ما دل عليه قوله تعالي : لا يَسْبِقُونَهُ بالقَول وَهُم بِأَمْرِه يَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الانبياء : ٢٧] ولا يَسْتَكْبِرُونَ عَنْ عِبَادَتِهِ وَلَا يستخسرون ) [الأنبياء : ١٩] (لا يوصفون بذكورة ولا أنوثة إذ لم يرد بذلك نقل ولا دل عليه عقل وما زعم عبدة الأصنام أنهم بنات الله تعالى محال باطل، وإفراط في شأنهم. كما أن قول اليهود إن الواحد منهم قد يرتكب الكفر ويعاقبه الله بالمسخ ، تفريط وتقصير في حالهم. فإن قيل : اليس قد كفر إبليس، وكان من الملائكة، بدليل صحة استثنائه منهم ؟ . قلنا : لا بل كان من الجن، فسق عن أمر ربه، لكنه لما كان في صفة الملائكة في باب العبادة ورفع الدرجة وكان جنيا واحدا مغمورا بالعبادة فيما بينهم، صح استثناؤه منهم تغليبا . وأما هاروت وماروت فالأصح أنهما ملكان ، لم يصدر عنهما کفر ولا كبيرة، وتعذيبهما إنما هو على وجه المعاتبة، كما يعاتب الأنبياء على الزلة والسهو، وكانا يعظان الناس، ويعلمان السحر ، ويقولان : إِنَّمَا نَحْنُ فتنة فلا تكفر ﴾ [البقرة : ١٠٢] ولا كفر في تعليم : السحر، بل في اعتقاده والعمل به

As for Harut and Marut, the most correct is that they are two angels; no disbelief or major sin issued from them; their punishment is only by way of rebuke, just as the prophets are rebuked for slip-ups and oversight. And they used to admonish people and teach sorcery, and they said: 'We are only a trial, so do not disbelieve' [Al-Baqarah 102]. There is no disbelief in teaching sorcery, but rather in believing in it and acting upon it.

?

?
The passage teaches that outward resemblance to the righteous does not change one's inner reality. You may appear to others as a pious person, but what hidden sin or attitude—like Iblis's origin from jinn—do you conceal that contradicts that image? Will you expose it to Allah today and repent before it destroys you?
?
Iblis was given a high rank among the angels because of his worship, but that rank did not prevent his fall. What position or reputation do you hold in your community that you think distinguishes you in Allah's sight? How might you be deceived by that status, and what step will you take this week to humble yourself before Him alone?

Harut and Marut: Angels Teaching Magic as a Trial
Clarifies Harut and Marut's angelic nature and their role in teaching magic as a test.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct view about Harut and Marut: they are angels, did not sin, and teaching magic is permissible as a trial.

Core Idea
Harut and Marut were sinless angels who taught magic as a divine trial, and sin lies in practicing magic.

The story of Harut and Marut often raises questions: Did these angels commit sins? Why were they punished? The author clarifies that the most correct view is that they are indeed angels, and they did not commit disbelief or major sin. Their punishment was a gentle rebuke for a minor slip, similar to prophets. They taught sorcery as a test from Allah, warning people not to disbelieve by practicing it. This lesson explains the distinction between teaching magic and believing in it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Harut and Marut
Read from 'وأما هاروت وماروت' to the end. Note the author's key points.
The passage addresses their nature, punishment, and their teaching of magic.
2
Understand their sinlessness
The author says the most correct view is they are angels, and no kufr or major sin issued from them. Their punishment was 'mu'ataba' (rebuke).
Compare with prophets who are rebuked for zalla (slip).
3
Understand the warning about magic
They taught magic but said 'We are only a trial, so do not disbelieve.' Teaching magic is not kufr; believing in it and acting upon it is.
This refutes those who condemn teaching magic absolutely.

Source Text

Revealed Scriptures and the Superiority of the Quran
Al-Nasafi on the divine origin, ranking, and abrogation of scriptures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all revealed scriptures are the speech of Allah, one in essence, and that the Quran is the most excellent and abrogates previous scriptures.

Core Idea
All scriptures are Allah's speech, but the Quran is the final and most excellent.

In this lesson, al-Nasafi explains the nature of the revealed books. He affirms that they are all the speech of Allah, but clarifies that the excellence of the Quran lies in its recited form and that it abrogates previous scriptures. This helps us understand the unique status of the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation. Notice how al-Nasafi moves from the nature of scriptures to their ranking and finally to abrogation.
The passage is dense with theological points.
2
Understand the unity of divine speech
The passage states that all scriptures are the speech of Allah, which is one. The multiplicity is in the recited and heard wording only. This is a key concept in Islamic theology.
The Quran is considered the direct word of God, and here the same applies to previous scriptures.
3
Grasp the order of excellence and abrogation
The author gives a hierarchy: Quran is best, then Torah, then Gospel, then Psalms. Then he notes that previous books are abrogated by the Quran in recitation, writing, and some rulings.
The Quran being the final revelation supersedes all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما أنزل على الأنبياء من الكتب ( والله كتب أنزلها على أنبيائه، وبين فيها أمره ونهيه ووعده ووعيده وكلها كلام الله تعالى وهو واحد وإنما التعدد والتفاوت في النظم المقروء والمسموع . وبهذا الاعتبار كان الأفضل هو القرآن ثم التوراة ثم الإنجيل ثم الزبور . كما أن القرآن كلام واحد ولا يتصور فيه تفضيل . ثم باعتبار الكتابة والقراءة يجوز أن يكون بعض السور أفضل كما ورد في الحديث. وحقيقة التفضيل : أن قراءته أفضل لما أنه أنفع أو ذكر الله تعالى فيه أكثر ، ثم الكتب قد نسخت بالقرآن تلاوتها وكتابتها وبعض أحكامها .
What was revealed to the prophets of books. And Allah has books which He sent down to His prophets, and in them He explained His command, His prohibition, His promise, and His threat. All of them are the speech of Allah Almighty, and it is one. Rather, multiplicity and difference are in the recited and heard wording. By this consideration, the most excellent is the Quran, then the Torah, then the Gospel, then the Psalms. Also, the Quran is one speech, and preference within it is not conceivable. Then by the consideration of writing and recitation, it is permissible that some surahs are better, as is reported in the hadith. The reality of preference is that its recitation is better because it is more beneficial or because the remembrance of Allah is more abundant in it. Then the books have been abrogated by the Quran in their recitation and writing and some of their rulings.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the revealed scriptures. It begins by stating that Allah sent down books containing His commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats. All these books are the speech of Allah, which is one in essence; the multiplicity and difference are only in the recited and heard expression (nazm). Based on this, the Quran is the most excellent, followed by the Torah, then the Gospel, then the Psalms. The author then explains that within the Quran, there is no preference between its parts in terms of the divine speech itself, but in terms of recitation and writing, some surahs can be preferred, as reported in hadith. The reason for such preference is that reciting them is more beneficial or contains more remembrance of Allah. Finally, the author states that the previous scriptures have been abrogated by the Quran in their recitation and writing and in some of their rulings.

Key Terms
الكتب
كلام الله
القرآن
التوراة
الإنجيل
الزبور
النسخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Quran is better than other scriptures in its very essence as divine speech.
Correction: The author clarifies that the divine speech itself is one; the excellence pertains to the recited form and the Quran's abrogating status.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the order of preference among the scriptures?
A) Torah, Quran, Gospel, Psalms
B) Quran, Torah, Gospel, Psalms
C) Quran, Psalms, Torah, Gospel
D) Torah, Gospel, Psalms, Quran

Key Takeaway
The Quran is the most excellent of scriptures and abrogates previous ones in recitation, writing, and some rulings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe the Quran is the most excellent scripture, why do you not spend more time reciting and reflecting on it daily? What would need to change in your schedule to make the Quran your primary focus?
?
The passage says the Quran abrogates previous scriptures. Are you still seeking spiritual guidance from non-Islamic sources or traditions? What step can you take this week to deepen your reliance solely on the Quran and Sunnah?
?
Al-Nasafi states that the excellence of the Quran lies in its benefit and abundant remembrance of Allah. In your own life, where have you experienced the Quran's benefit most tangibly? If you can't point to a specific example, what is holding you back from experiencing that benefit?

The Prophet's Mi'raj: A Wakeful Journey
The author affirms the Prophet's ascension (Mi'raj) occurred in wakefulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's Mi'raj was a physical event that occurred in a state of wakefulness, not a dream or spiritual vision.

Core Idea
The Mi'raj was a real, physical journey in wakefulness.

This brief but powerful statement from the author establishes a fundamental article of faith: the Prophet's night journey and ascension to the heavens was not a dream or metaphor, but a literal, physical event. The clarification that it occurred 'in wakefulness' is crucial for understanding Sunni creed on this matter.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Begin by reading the original Arabic sentence and its literal English translation. Notice the concise style.
2
Identify the key terms
Focus on the words 'المعراج' (al-Mi'raj) and 'اليقظة' (al-yaqzah). Understand their meanings: Mi'raj means 'ascension' and yaqzah means 'wakefulness'.
These terms are central to the doctrine.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why the author emphasizes 'in wakefulness'. What does this exclude? It excludes the possibility that the Mi'raj was a dream or a purely spiritual experience. This affirms the physical reality of the event.
This is a point of creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما قيل في المعراج والمعراج لرسول الله عليه الصلاة والسلام في اليقظة
What has been said concerning the Mi'raj: And the Mi'raj of the Messenger of Allah, prayers and peace be upon him, was in wakefulness.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This is a brief statement affirming that the Prophet's night journey and ascension (Mi'raj) took place in a state of wakefulness, not in a dream. The author states this as a definitive fact, implying that the event was physical and real, as opposed to a spiritual vision. This is a key article of faith in Sunni creed.

Key Terms
المعراج
اليقظة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mi'raj was a spiritual experience or a dream.
Correction: The author affirms it was in wakefulness, meaning a physical, real event.

Checkpoint
How does the author describe the occurrence of the Mi'raj?
A) In a dream
B) In wakefulness
C) Only spiritually
D) Both in wakefulness and in a dream

Key Takeaway
The Mi'raj of the Prophet ﷺ was a real, physical event that occurred in a state of wakefulness, not in a dream.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Mi'raj was a physical, wakeful event, how does that challenge your naturalistic assumptions about what is possible? Are you willing to submit to Allah's power even when it defies human logic? What step will you take today to strengthen your conviction in the unseen?
?
The Prophet's journey in wakefulness shows that faith is not a dream—it is a lived reality. In what area of your life are you treating your faith as if it were a distant ideal rather than a present truth? What will you do today to make your faith more wakeful?

Harut and Marut: Angels Teaching Sorcery as a Trial
Explanation of Harut and Marut's nature and teaching of sorcery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct Islamic position on Harut and Marut: that they are angels, did not commit disbelief or major sin, and that teaching sorcery is not itself disbelief.

Core Idea
Harut and Marut are angels; teaching sorcery is not disbelief—only believing and practicing it is.

This passage addresses a common question about the angels Harut and Marut mentioned in Surah al-Baqarah. The author clarifies their status and the nature of their punishment, distinguishing between teaching sorcery and committing disbelief. Understanding this helps reconcile Quranic verses about angels being infallible with the narrative of Harut and Marut.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the author's sequence of claims.
Notice that the author uses a very assertive tone – 'the most correct (view) is'.
2
Identify the key claims
List the four main points the author makes: (1) Harut and Marut are angels, (2) no disbelief or major sin from them, (3) their punishment is a reprimand, (4) teaching sorcery is not disbelief.
3
Reflect on the distinction
Ask yourself: why is teaching sorcery not disbelief? The author answers: disbelief is in believing it and acting upon it. This is a crucial distinction in Islamic law.
It's similar to teaching about poison – teaching is not a crime, but using it to harm is.
4
Connect to broader angelology
Consider how this passage fits with the Islamic belief that angels are sinless and obedient. The author's explanation preserves that by saying their punishment is a reprimand, not a punishment for sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما هاروت وماروت فالأصح أنهما ملكان ، لم يصدر عنهما كفر ولا كبيرة، وتعذيبهما إنما هو على وجه المعاتبة، كما يعاتب الأنبياء على الزلة والسهو، وكانا يعظان الناس، ويعلمان السحر ، ويقولان : إِنَّمَا نَحْنُ فِتْنَةٌ فَلَا تَكْفُرْ [البقرة : ١٠٢] ولا كفر في تعليم السحر، بل في اعتقاده والعمل به
As for Harut and Marut, the most correct (view) is that they are two angels. From them there occurred neither disbelief nor a major sin. Their punishment is only by way of reprimand, just as the prophets are reprimanded for slips and oversights. They used to admonish the people and teach sorcery, and they would say: 'We are only a trial, so do not disbelieve' [al-Baqarah 2:102]. There is no disbelief in teaching sorcery, but rather in believing it and acting upon it.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage clarifies the status of Harut and Marut mentioned in the Quran. The author states the more correct position: they are angels, and they did not commit disbelief or a major sin. Their punishment (mentioned in some traditions) is understood as a gentle reprimand, similar to how prophets are rebuked for unintentional errors. They taught sorcery to people as a test from Allah, warning them not to fall into disbelief. The key distinction: teaching sorcery is not itself disbelief; disbelief lies in believing that sorcery has independent effect and acting upon it.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Teaching sorcery is itself an act of disbelief.
Correction: The author clarifies that teaching sorcery is not disbelief; disbelief lies in believing in sorcery and acting upon it.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct view regarding Harut and Marut?
A) They were angels who sinned and were punished severely.
B) They were angels and did not commit disbelief or major sin, and their punishment was like a reprimand.
C) They were humans who taught sorcery and were punished.
D) They were angels who taught sorcery and became disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
Harut and Marut are angels who taught sorcery as a test; teaching sorcery is not disbelief—only believing and acting on it is disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you acquire knowledge of something morally ambiguous or dangerous, do you stop and consider that it might be a trial from Allah for you? What safeguards do you have in place to prevent that knowledge from corrupting your belief or actions?
?
The angels warned, 'Do not disbelieve.' In your daily life, what are the subtle temptations or ideologies that you entertain without recognizing them as trials that could lead you away from true faith?
?
If teaching sorcery is not kufr but believing and acting on it is, then where do you draw the line in your own heart between learning about something and actually internalizing it? How often do you catch yourself drifting from mere exposure to acceptance?

Definition of the Wali and His Karamah
Definition of wali and karamah with distinction from istidraj and mu'jiza

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of a wali (saint) and his karamah (miracle), and how karamah is distinguished from istidraj (gradual deceit) and mu'jiza (prophetic miracle).

Core Idea
A saint's miracle is real, but it's not a prophecy claim.

In this passage, the author affirms the reality of saintly miracles (karamat) and provides clear definitions. Before we can discuss specific miracles, we need to know who a saint is and what makes a miracle saintly rather than prophetic or deceptive. This passage gives us the essential criteria.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own words introduce the definitions.
Notice that the passage begins by affirming the reality of karamat.
2
Identify the three types of supernatural events
The passage mentions three categories: karamah, istidraj, and mu'jiza. Find each one and note the defining condition for each.
The key condition is the presence or absence of faith and a claim to prophethood.
3
Understand the criterion for each
Ask: What distinguishes a karamah from a mu'jiza? What distinguishes a karamah from istidraj? The passage gives clear answers.
Karamah is not accompanied by a claim to prophethood; istidraj lacks faith and good deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكرامات الأولياء حق والولى هو العارف بالله تعالى وصفاته، بحسب ما يمكن المواظب على الطاعات المجتنب عن المعاصي، المعرض عن الانهماك في اللذات والشهوات . وكرامته ظهور أمر خارق للعادة من قبله غير مقارن لدعوى النبوة، فما لا يكون مقرونا بالإيمان والعمل الصالح، يكون استدراجا. وما يكون مقرونا بدعوى النبوة يكون معجزة . كون مصحوة
And the miracles of the saints are true. The saint is the one who knows Allah Most High and His attributes, to the extent possible, the one who is constant in acts of obedience, avoids sins, and turns away from immersion in pleasures and desires. And his miracle is the appearance of a matter that breaks custom from him, not accompanied by a claim to prophethood. So what is not accompanied by faith and righteous deeds is istidraj (gradual leading to destruction). And what is accompanied by a claim to prophethood is a mu'jiza (prophetic miracle). [Unclear: 'kun mus-hawa'?]
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage defines two key terms: the wali (saint) and his karamah (miracle). It begins by affirming that the karamat of saints are true (haqq). The wali is defined as one who knows Allah and His attributes according to human capacity, who is constant in obedience, avoids sins, and turns away from indulgence in pleasures and desires. This describes the spiritual and moral state of the saint. Then the karamah is defined as a supernatural event (amr khariq lil-'ada) that appears from the saint, but crucially it is not accompanied by a claim to prophethood. The passage then distinguishes karamah from two other types of supernatural events: if such an event is not accompanied by faith and righteous deeds, it is istidraj (a gradual leading to destruction, i.e., a miracle granted to a non-believer as a test). If it is accompanied by a claim to prophethood, it is a mu'jiza (a prophetic miracle). This distinction is essential to safeguard the unique status of prophetic miracles while affirming the possibility of saintly miracles.

Key Terms
ولي
كرامة
استدراج
معجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that any supernatural event from a pious person is a prophetic miracle.
Correction: The passage clarifies that a karamah is specifically not accompanied by a claim to prophethood, distinguishing it from a mu'jiza.

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between a karamah (saintly miracle) and a mu'jiza (prophetic miracle)?
A) A karamah is always accompanied by a claim to prophethood.
B) A mu'jiza is not accompanied by a claim to prophethood.
C) A karamah is not accompanied by a claim to prophethood, while a mu'jiza is.
D) Both are the same thing.

Key Takeaway
The karamah of a saint is a real supernatural event, but it is distinguished from a prophetic miracle by the absence of a claim to prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You read that the wali is 'constant in acts of obedience, avoids sins, and turns away from immersion in pleasures and desires.' Look at your own life honestly: which of these three qualities is most lacking in you? What specific change will you make today to move closer to that description?
?
The passage warns that supernatural events without righteousness are istidraj — a trap leading to destruction. Have you ever been impressed by someone's spiritual experiences or 'miracles' while ignoring whether their daily life reflects true obedience? How can you guard your heart against being deceived by outward signs?
?
If you were to die today, would you be content knowing that your relationship with Allah is based on obedience and avoidance of sins, or are you secretly hoping for some miraculous sign to confirm your status? What does your answer reveal about your true spiritual priority?
