The Proof for Karamah (Saintly Miracles)
Sanusi presents the proof for karamah from tawatur and Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the primary proofs for the reality of karamah: mass transmission and Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Karamah is proven by tawatur and the Quran.

Before examining the various manifestations of saintly miracles, we must first establish that they are real. Sanusi argues that karamah is proven by a combination of tawatur (mass transmission) from the Companions and explicit mention in the Quran. This lesson presents that foundational proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
Read the Arabic source passage once, then read the translation to understand the argument.
Notice that the author uses two distinct proofs.
2
Identify the two proofs
Look for the first proof (tawatur) and the second proof (Quranic mention). How do they work together?
3
Understand the logical conclusion
The author says that once occurrence is established, there is no need to prove permissibility. Why is that important?
This shifts the burden from possibility to actuality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل على حقيقة الكرامة : ما تواتر عن كثير من الصحابة ومن بعدهم، بحيث لا يمكن إنكاره خصوصا الأمر المشترك. وإن كانت التفاصيل آحادا . وأيضا : الكتاب ناطق بظهورها من «مريم» ومن صاحب (سليمان ) - عليه السلام - وبعد ثبوت الوقوع لا حاجة إلى إثبات الجواز . ثم أورد كلاما يشير إلى تفسير الكرامة، وإلى تفصيل بعض جزئياتها المستبعدة جدا. فقال : فتظهر الكرامة على طريق نقض العادة للولى، من قطع المسافة البعيدة في المدة القليلة كإتيان صاحب سليمان عليه السلام وهو آصف بن برخيا على الأشهر بعرش بلقيس » قبل ارتداد الطرف، مع بعد المسافة . وظهور الطعام والشراب واللباس عند الحاجة إليها كما في حق مريم، فإنه تعالى قال : كلما دخل عليها زكريا المحراب وجد عندها رزقا قال يا مريم أنى لك هذا قالت هو من عند الله [آل عمران : ٣٧] والمشى على الماء كما نقل عن كثير من الأولياء . (وفى الهواء) كما نقل عن : جعفر بن أبي طالب ) ، ( ولقمان السرخسى ) وغيرهما. وكلام) الجماد والعجماء ) واندفاع المتوجه من البلاء، وكفاية المهم من الأعداء . أما كلام الجماد فكما روى أنه كان بين يدى سليمان وأبى الدرداء رضي الله عنهما قصعة فسبحت وسمعا تسبيحها . وأما كلام العجماء فتكليم الكلب لأصحاب الكهف وكما روى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : ( بينا رجل يسوق بقرة قد حمل عليها، إذا التفتت البقرة إليه. وقالت : إنى لم أخلق لهذا، إنما خلقت للحرث (۱). فقال الناس : سبحان الله بقرة تتكلم ؟ فقال النبي عليه السلام آمنت بهذا وغير ذلك من الأشياء مثل رؤية عمر رضي الله عنه، وهو على المنبر بالمدينة جيشه : بـ «نهاوند» حتى أنه قال لأمير جيشه : يا سارية. الجبل, الجبل. تحذيرا له من وراء الجبل لمكر العدو هنالك وسماع سارية كلامه مع بعد المسافة . وكشرب خالد رضي عنه السم من غير تضرر به . وكجريان النيل بكتاب عمر رضى الله عنه وأمثال هذا أكثر من أن تحصى.
And the proof for the reality of karamah is what has been transmitted by tawatur (massively) from many of the Companions and those after them, to the extent that it cannot be denied, especially the common aspect. Even if the details are ahad (isolated reports). Also, the Book (Quran) speaks of its appearance from Maryam and from the companion of Sulayman (peace be upon him). And after the occurrence is established, there is no need to prove its permissibility. Then he (the author) mentioned words indicating an explanation of karamah and a detailing of some of its very remote particulars. He said: So the karamah appears in the way of breaching custom for the saint, such as covering a long distance in a short time, like the coming of the companion of Sulayman (peace be upon him)—who according to the most famous opinion is Asif ibn Barkhiya—with the throne of Bilqis before the blink of an eye, despite the distance. And the appearance of food, drink, and clothing when needed, as in the case of Maryam, for Allah Most High said: 'Whenever Zechariah entered the sanctuary upon her, he found with her provision. He said, 'O Maryam, from where does this come to you?' She said, 'It is from Allah.'' [Al 'Imran: 37]. And walking on water, as transmitted from many saints. (And walking in the air), as transmitted from Ja'far ibn Abi Talib and Luqman al-Sarakhsi and others. And the speech of inanimate objects and animals, and the repelling of impending affliction, and the sufficiency against important enemies. As for the speech of inanimate objects, it is narrated that between the hands of Sulayman and Abu Darda' (may Allah be pleased with them) there was a bowl that glorified (Allah) and they heard its glorification. As for the speech of animals, it includes the conversation of the dog with the Companions of the Cave, and as narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'While a man was driving a cow on which he had loaded (something), the cow turned to him and said: I was not created for this; I was created for plowing.' The people said: 'Glory be to Allah, a cow speaks?' The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'I believe in this.' And among such things is the vision of 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) while he was on the pulpit in Medina seeing his army at Nahawand, such that he said to his commander: 'O Sariyah, the mountain, the mountain,' warning him from behind the mountain of the enemy's trickery there, and Sariyah hearing his words despite the distance. And the drinking of poison by Khalid (may Allah be pleased with him) without being harmed by it. And the flowing of the Nile at the command of 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) by his letter. And examples of this kind are too numerous to be counted.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage provides the proof for the reality of karamat (saintly miracles) and details many examples. The proof is twofold: first, mass transmission (tawatur) from the Companions and later generations, so that the occurrence cannot be denied overall, even if specific details come through isolated reports (ahad). Second, the Quran itself speaks of miraculous events from Maryam (provision from Allah) and from the companion of Sulayman (Asif ibn Barkhiya) who brought the throne of Bilqis in the blink of an eye. Once such events are established as having occurred, there is no further need to prove that they are possible (ja'iz). The author then explains that the karamah appears as a breach of custom (naqd al-'ada) for the saint, and he enumerates several types: 1) Covering a long distance in a short time, exemplified by Asif's feat. 2) Provision of food, drink, and clothing when needed, as with Maryam. 3) Walking on water, reported of many saints. 4) Walking in the air, reported of Ja'far ibn Abi Talib and Luqman al-Sarakhsi. 5) Speech of inanimate objects (e.g., a bowl glorifying Allah in the presence of Sulayman and Abu Darda'). 6) Speech of animals (e.g., the dog of the Cave, the cow speaking to its handler). 7) Repelling impending affliction and sufficiency against enemies. 8) Clairvoyance and long-distance communication, like 'Umar seeing his army at Nahawand and calling out to Sariyah, who heard him. 9) Immunity from harm, like Khalid drinking poison without effect. 10) Miraculous control over nature, like the Nile flowing by 'Umar's letter. The author concludes that such examples are too numerous to count. The overall argument is that the reality of karamah is proven by strong evidence and that these events are not to be denied.

Key Terms
تواتر
آحاد
كرامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that karamah is impossible or just superstition.
Correction: The passage shows that karamah is established by massive evidence and Quranic mention, so it is a real phenomenon.

Checkpoint
What is the primary basis for the proof of karamah according to this passage?
A) Rational argument
B) Mass transmission (tawatur) and Quranic mention
C) Consensus of scholars
D) Personal experience

Key Takeaway
Karamah is proven by tawatur and Quranic stories, making its reality undeniable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the occurrence of karamah is proven by overwhelming evidence (tawatur and the Quran), why do you find yourself hesitant to believe that Allah still grants such miracles to His righteous servants? What does that hesitation reveal about your trust in Allah's power and His care for the awliya?
?
The passage says that after occurrence is established, there is no need to debate permissibility. In your own faith, are there truths you already know but continue to debate? What would it take for you to stop discussing and start submitting to what has already been established?
?
When you read about Maryam receiving provisions or Asif bringing the throne, do you simply pass over these as stories, or do they remind you that Allah can intervene in your life in ways beyond natural means? How can you actively expect and seek His miraculous support today?

Manifestations of Karamah: Breaches of Custom
Sanusi enumerates types of karamah as breaches of custom with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the various types of karamah (saintly miracles) as breaches of natural custom, with examples from the Quran and tradition.

Core Idea
Karamah is manifested as a breach of custom in many forms.

After establishing the reality of karamah, Sanusi explains that it appears as a breach of custom (naqd al-‘ada) and provides a detailed list of miraculous phenomena. Examples range from instant travel and provision from unseen to speaking animals and inanimate objects. This lesson surveys these manifestations.

Read the enumeration

The author begins with a general statement about breaching custom.

3
Reflect on the significance

The multiplicity strengthens the case for karamah.

As for the speech of animals, it includes the conversation of the dog with the Companions of the Cave, and as narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'While a man was driving a cow on which he had loaded (something), the cow turned to him and said: I was not created for this; I was created for plowing.' The people said: 'Glory be to Allah, a cow speaks?' The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'I believe in this.' And among such things is the vision of 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) while he was on the pulpit in Medina seeing his army at Nahawand, such that he said to his commander: 'O Sariyah, the mountain, the mountain,' warning him from behind the mountain of the enemy's trickery there, and Sariyah hearing his words despite the distance. And the drinking of poison by Khalid (may Allah be pleased with him) without being harmed by it. And the flowing of the Nile at the command of 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) by his letter. And examples of this kind are too numerous to be counted.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage provides the proof for the reality of karamat (saintly miracles) and details many examples. The proof is twofold: first, mass transmission (tawatur) from the Companions and later generations, so that the occurrence cannot be denied overall, even if specific details come through isolated reports (ahad). Second, the Quran itself speaks of miraculous events from Maryam (provision from Allah) and from the companion of Sulayman (Asif ibn Barkhiya) who brought the throne of Bilqis in the blink of an eye. Once such events are established as having occurred, there is no further need to prove that they are possible (ja'iz). The author then explains that the karamah appears as a breach of custom (naqd al-'ada) for the saint, and he enumerates several types: 1) Covering a long distance in a short time, exemplified by Asif's feat. 2) Provision of food, drink, and clothing when needed, as with Maryam. 3) Walking on water, reported of many saints. 4) Walking in the air, reported of Ja'far ibn Abi Talib and Luqman al-Sarakhsi. 5) Speech of inanimate objects (e.g., a bowl glorifying Allah in the presence of Sulayman and Abu Darda'). 6) Speech of animals (e.g., the dog of the Cave, the cow speaking to its handler). 7) Repelling impending affliction and sufficiency against enemies. 8) Clairvoyance and long-distance communication, like 'Umar seeing his army at Nahawand and calling out to Sariyah, who heard him. 9) Immunity from harm, like Khalid drinking poison without effect. 10) Miraculous control over nature, like the Nile flowing by 'Umar's letter. The author concludes that such examples are too numerous to count. The overall argument is that the reality of karamah is proven by strong evidence and that these events are not to be denied.

Key Terms
نقض العادة
كرامة
ولي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that karamah is limited to one type, like healing.
Correction: The passage shows many diverse types of miraculous events that saints can experience.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of karamah through speech of an inanimate object?
A) The cow speaking to its handler
B) A bowl glorifying Allah in the presence of Sulayman and Abu Darda
C) The dog speaking to the Companions of the Cave
D) Maryam receiving food

Key Takeaway
Karamah appears in many forms, all as breaches of custom that affirm divine support for saints.

The Best of Humankind After the Prophets
States the excellence of Companions after all prophets and recommends phrasing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the best of creation after the prophets and the recommended phrasing.

Core Idea
The Companions are the best of humanity after all prophets.

This brief passage from the Aqeedah an-Nasafiyyah settles a key question: who are the most excellent people after the Prophet? The author points to the Companions but recommends precise phrasing to avoid misunderstanding. This lesson unpacks that teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the passage once to get the rhythm. Notice the repetition of the phrase 'the best of humankind after our Prophet'.
The repetition may be for emphasis or a scribal variant.
2
Identify the two statements
The passage makes two claims: first, that the best after our Prophet (Muhammad) are the Companions; second, that it is better to say 'after the prophets', meaning after all prophets.
This refines the first statement to include all prophets.
3
Consider why 'after the prophets' is better
By saying 'after the prophets', we avoid implying that only after Muhammad are Companions best, and we acknowledge that earlier prophets are superior to all humans, including Companions.
This shows respect for all prophets.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Some might use this passage to debate which specific Companion is best. But the passage only establishes that Companions in general are best after prophets, not which individual.
The focus is on general excellence, not ranking.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أفضل البشر بعد نبينا عليه الصلاة والسلام وأفضل البشر بعد نبينا والأحسن أن يقال : بعد الأنبياء.
The best of humankind after our Prophet, may peace and blessing be upon him. And the best of humankind after our Prophet, and it is better to say: after the prophets.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage addresses the doctrinal issue of who is the most excellent (afdal) of humanity after the Prophet Muhammad. The author first says 'the best of humankind after our Prophet' (referring to the Companions). He then suggests it is better to say 'after the prophets' (i.e., after all prophets). The point is that the Companions are the best of creation after the prophets, but one should phrase it as 'after the prophets' to be more precise and inclusive of earlier prophets. The repetition in the text may indicate a revision or emphasis.

Key Terms
أفضل البشر
بعد الأنبياء
الصحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Someone might think this passage settles which Companion (e.g., Abu Bakr) is the best individually.
Correction: The passage only affirms that the Companions collectively are the best after all prophets. It does not rank them among themselves.

Checkpoint
What phrasing does the author recommend for describing the most excellent humans after the Prophet?
A) After the Companions
B) After the prophets
C) After the messengers
D) After the caliphs

Key Takeaway
The Companions are the best of creation after all prophets, and it is doctrinally precise to say 'after the prophets' rather than just 'after our Prophet'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly honor the Companions as the best of creation after the prophets? In what specific ways does your life reflect that belief—or fail to reflect it? What will you change today to align your actions with this reality?
?

The Thirty-Year Caliphate: Prophecy and Interpretation
The author explains the hadith of thirty-year caliphate and resolves the problem of later rulers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author reconciles the hadith of thirty-year caliphate with the historical recognition of later caliphs.

Core Idea
The perfect caliphate was thirty years; later rulers may still be caliphs.

This passage tackles a classic theological puzzle: the Prophet foretold that the caliphate would last thirty years, yet later rulers like the Abbasids were widely recognized as legitimate caliphs. The author explains the hadith while maintaining respect for the consensus of the community. Read on to see his elegant solution.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the hadith and the problem it raises.
The passage includes a hadith about the caliphate becoming oppressive kingship.
2
Identify the problem
Notice that the author states that Mu'awiyah and after are not caliphs, but then acknowledges that the community accepted Abbasids and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz.
This creates a tension.
3
Understand the resolution
The author says 'perhaps the intended meaning is that the complete caliphate... is thirty years.' This means the ideal caliphate ended, but later rulers can still be called caliphs in a broader sense.
The phrase 'after that it may exist and may not' allows for later legitimate caliphs.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Relate this back to the learning objective: the reconciliation is through distinguishing between perfect and imperfect caliphate.
This is a common approach in Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخلافة ثلاثون سنة ثم بعدها ملك وإمارة) لقوله عليه :السلام الخلافة بعدى ثلاثون سنة، ثم تصير ملكا عضوضا. وقد استشهد على رضى الله عنه على رأس ثلاثين سنة من وفاة رسول الله . فمعاوية ومن بعده لا يكونون خلفاء، بل كانوا ملوكا وأمراء. وهذا مشكل لأن أهل الحل والعقد من الأمة قد كانوا متفقين على خلافه الخلفاء العباسيين، وبعض المروانيين كعمر بن عبد العزيز .مثلا ولعل المراد : أن الخلافة الكاملة التي لا يشوبها شيء من وميل عن المتابعة، تكون ثلاثين سنة. وبعدها قد يكون وقد لا يكون .
And the caliphate is thirty years, then after it is kingship and emirate, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years, then it becomes oppressive kingship.' And 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, was martyred exactly thirty years after the death of the Messenger of Allah. So Mu'awiyah and those after him are not caliphs, but rather kings and emirs. But this is problematic, because the people of binding and loosing from the community had agreed upon the caliphate of the Abbasid caliphs, and some of the Marwanids like 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz, for example. Perhaps the intended meaning is that the complete caliphate, which is not mixed with anything of deviation from following (the Sunnah), is thirty years. After that it may exist and may not.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage discusses the well-known hadith that the caliphate after the Prophet will last thirty years, then become oppressive kingship. The author notes that 'Ali was martyred exactly thirty years after the Prophet's death, and thus Mu'awiyah and subsequent rulers are kings, not caliphs. However, this raises a problem because the scholars and leaders of the community recognized the Abbasid caliphs and some Umayyads like 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz as legitimate caliphs. The author resolves this by proposing that the hadith refers to the ideal, perfect caliphate (al-khilafah al-kamilah) free from any deviation from the Prophetic path. That perfect caliphate was only thirty years. After that, a caliphate may or may not exist (i.e., some later rulers may still be considered caliphs in a qualified sense, but not the perfect caliphate).

Key Terms

ملك
إمارة
متابعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith invalidates all later caliphates completely.
Correction: The hadith refers to the perfect caliphate free from deviation; later rulers may still be considered caliphs in a broader sense.

Checkpoint
How does the author reconcile the hadith of thirty-year caliphate with the recognition of later caliphs like the Abbasids?
A) He denies the hadith's authenticity.
B) He says the hadith refers only to the perfect caliphate free from deviation.
C) He says later caliphs are not caliphs at all.
D) He says the thirty years started from 'Umar.

Key Takeaway
The perfect caliphate lasted only thirty years; later rulers may be considered caliphs but not in the perfect sense.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have a certain image of what a perfect Muslim society looks like. When you see the reality of Muslim communities today with all their shortcomings, do you find yourself dismissing them entirely, or do you still see them as part of the ummah? The author of this passage did not reject later caliphs completely; he understood the hadith as describing a perfect model, but allowed for imperfect continuation. How does that challenge your own tendency to either idealize or reject the Muslim community around you? What would it mean for you to hold onto the ideal while still engaging with the imperfect reality?
?
This lesson shows that the Prophet's promise of a thirty-year perfect caliphate is over. We now live in the era of kingship. But the author also acknowledged that some later rulers could still be considered caliphs in a qualified sense. Think about your own life: you may feel that the 'golden age' of your faith is in the past. How does this affect your hope for the future? Are you using the past as an excuse to give up on reform, or are you finding ways to live out the prophetic model in a less-than-ideal world? Be honest: do you secretly believe that a true Islamic society is impossible today? What would it take for you to still strive for it?
?
The passage mentions 'the complete caliphate which is not mixed with anything of deviation from following (the Sunnah)'. Consider your own practice of Islam. Can you identify one specific area where you have accepted a lower standard instead of striving for the complete following of the Sunnah? What step will you take today to move towards that ideal?

The Obligation of Appointing an Imam and Its Proofs
Al-Nasafi proves the obligation of appointing an imam by consensus, hadith, and practical necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation of appointing an imam, the three main proofs (consensus, hadith, and necessity), and the theological nuance regarding whether this obligation is on God or the people.

Core Idea
The imam is obligatory by scripture, consensus, and necessity – without him, Islam cannot function.

This lesson tackles a foundational political doctrine in Sunni Islam: the obligation to have a single leader (imam). The author, al-Nasafi, states that there is consensus on the obligation but a disagreement on its basis. He then provides three proofs: a prophetic hadith, the practice of the Companions, and practical necessity. Understanding this establishes why leadership is not optional in Islam.

Guided Path
1
Understand the consensus and the disagreement
The passage begins by stating consensus that appointing an imam is obligatory, but scholars differ on whether it is on God or the people, and whether the proof is rational or scriptural. Notice this nuance.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The primary scriptural proof is a hadith warning that dying without knowing the imam of one's time is a death of ignorance. This makes knowledge of the imam a religious duty.
3
Observe the Companions' practice
After the Prophet's death, the Companions prioritized appointing an imam (Abu Bakr) over even burying the Prophet, showing its supreme importance.
The footnote confirms they agreed on Abu Bakr at Saqifah before burial.
4
Consider the practical necessity
The imam is needed for many obligatory duties: judgments, punishments, defense, charities, prayers, disputes, etc. These cannot be done by individuals, so a leader is indispensable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الإجماع على أن نصب الإمام واجب، وإنما الخلاف فى أنه هل على الله تعالى أو على الخلق بدليل سمعي أو عقلي ؟ . والمذهب : أنه يجب على الخلق سمعا لقوله عليه السلام : « من مات ولم يعرف إمام زمانه مات ميتة جاهلية ) . ولأن الأمة قد جعلوا أهم المهمات بعد وفاة النبي عليه السلام نصب الإمام، حتى قدموه على الدفن (1) . وكذا بعد موت كل إمام. ولأن كثيرا من الواجبات الشرعية يتوقف عليه كما أشار إليه بقوله : والمسلمون لا بد لهم من إمام يقوم بتنفيذ أحكامهم، وإقامة حدودهم وسد ثغورهم، وتجهيز جيوشهم، وأخذ صدقاتهم، وقهر المتغلبة، والمتلصصة، وقطاع الطريق، وإقامة الجمع والأعياد، وقطع المنازعات الواقعة بين العباد، وقبول الشهادات القائمة على الحقوق، وتزويج الصغار والصغائر الذين لا أولياء لهم، وقسمة الغنائم ونحو ذلك من الأمور التي لا يتولاها آحاد الأمة .
(1) فقد أجمعوا على خلافة أبي بكر في سقيفة بني ساعدة قبل دفن جسد النبي
Then there is consensus that appointing an imam is obligatory. The only disagreement is whether it is obligatory upon Allah Almighty or upon the creation, by a scriptural or rational proof. The doctrine is that it is obligatory upon the creation by scripture, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever dies and does not know the imam of his time dies a death of ignorance.' And because the community made the most important of important matters after the death of the Prophet, peace be upon him, the appointment of an imam, such that they prioritized it over burial (1). And likewise after the death of every imam. And because many obligatory duties depend upon it, as he indicated by his saying: And the Muslims must have an imam who carries out their legal judgments, establishes their prescribed punishments, guards their borders, equips their armies, collects their charity, suppresses oppressors, brigands, and highway robbers, establishes Friday and 'Eid prayers, resolves disputes among subjects, accepts testimonies establishing rights, marries minors (boys and girls) who have no guardians, divides spoils, and similar matters which cannot be undertaken by ordinary individuals. (1) For they agreed on the caliphate of Abu Bakr in the Saqifah of Banu Sa'idah before the burial of the Prophet's body.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage establishes the obligation of appointing an imam (nusb al-imam). The author begins by stating consensus (ijma') on the obligation, but notes a difference of opinion: is it obligatory upon God or upon the people, and is the proof scriptural or rational? The author's school holds it is obligatory upon the people by scriptural evidence (sam'an). He gives three proofs: 1) The hadith: 'Whoever dies without knowing the imam of his time dies a death of jahiliyyah.' 2) The practice of the Companions: after the Prophet's death, they prioritized appointing an imam (Abu Bakr) even over burying the Prophet, as indicated in the footnote. 3) Practical necessity: many obligatory duties depend on the existence of an imam. The author then lists these duties: executing judgments, hudud, guarding borders, equipping armies, collecting zakat, suppressing aggressors, brigands, and highway robbers, establishing Friday and 'Eid prayers, settling disputes, accepting testimonies, marrying minors without guardians, dividing spoils, etc. These cannot be done by ordinary individuals, so a leader is needed. The footnote confirms the historical fact that the Companions agreed on Abu Bakr's caliphate in Saqifah before burying the Prophet.

Key Terms
نصب الإمام
إجماع
سمع
عقل
موتة جاهلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the imam is not necessary because Muslims can manage without a central authority.
Correction: The passage shows that many obligatory duties depend on the imam, such as judgments, punishments, border defense, charity collection, and resolving disputes. Without an imam, these cannot be fulfilled, making his appointment a practical necessity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary scriptural proof for the obligation of appointing an imam?
A) The consensus of the community.
B) The hadith 'Whoever dies without knowing the imam of his time dies a death of ignorance.'
C) The practical necessity for implementing laws.
D) The prioritization of imam appointment over burial.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of appointing an imam is proven by consensus, hadith, and practical necessity, establishing it as a fundamental religious duty.

The Validity of Wiping over Leather Socks
Affirms permissibility of wiping over khuffs in travel and residence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the practice of wiping over khuffs is affirmed by the Sunni tradition, established through widely transmitted hadith and the consensus of the Companions.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is a sunna established by authentic reports, not a bid‘a.

This passage from the Sharh al-‘Aqa’id al-Nasafiyya defends the practice of wiping over leather socks during both travel and residence. The author acknowledges that it is not explicitly in the Quran but argues it is firmly established through widely transmitted hadith and the practice of the Companions. Let’s examine the evidence presented.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic carefully, noting the key terms like مسح على الخفين and خبر مشهور.
Pay attention to the structure: claim, acknowledgment, then evidence.
2
Identify the main claim
Notice that the author states the ruling (ونرى المسح على الخفين) and then provides evidence to support it.
3
Examine the four pieces of evidence
Go through each: Ali's hadith specifying time limits, Abu Bakr's narration confirming the concession, Hasan al-Basri's testimony of seventy Companions, and Abu Hanifa's statement about clear evidence.
Understand why each piece is cited.
4
Understand the condition
The footnote clarifies that the socks must be put on after performing wudu (on a state of purity).
This is a key condition for the validity of wiping.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this practice is important in Sunni fiqh – it shows that sunna can supplement Quranic commands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونرى المسح على الخفين في السفر والحضر لأنه وإن كان زيادة على الكتاب، ولكنه ثابت بالخبر المشهور، سئل على بن أبى طالب رضى الله عنه عن المسح على الخفين . فقال : « جعل رسول الله مدته ثلاثة أيام ولياليهن للمسافر ويوما وليلة صلى الله عليه وسلم للمقيم. وروى أبو بكر عن رسول الله له أنه رخص للمسافر ثلاثة أيام ولياليهن، وللمقيم يوما وليلة، إذا تطهر فلبس خفيه أن يمسح عليهما. وقال الحسن البصري - رحمه الله - ( أدركت سبعين نفرا من الصحابة رضى الله عنهم - يرون المسح على الخفين . ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : ( ما قلت بالمسح حتى جاءني فيه دلیل مثل ضوء النهار. (1) أى إن لبسهما على طهارة.
And we hold the wiping over the leather socks (khuffs) in travel and residence, because although it is an addition to the Book (Quran), it is established by the widely transmitted report (khabar mashhur). Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) was asked about wiping over the khuffs, and he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made its period three days and their nights for the traveler, and one day and one night for the resident.' And Abu Bakr narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he granted a concession to the traveler for three days and their nights, and to the resident for one day and one night, that if he purifies himself and then wears his khuffs, he may wipe over them. And al-Hasan al-Basri (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'I met seventy of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) who held the wiping over the khuffs.' And for this reason Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'I did not speak of wiping until evidence came to me for it like the light of day.' (Meaning: that he wore them after purification.)
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage affirms the practice of wiping over leather socks (al-mash 'ala al-khuffayn) during travel and residence. The author acknowledges that this ruling is an addition to the Quran (i.e., not explicitly mentioned in it), but it is established by a khabar mashhur (widely transmitted hadith). He then provides evidence: first, the statement of Ali ibn Abi Talib specifying the time limits for traveler and resident; second, a narration from Abu Bakr confirming the same concession; third, the testimony of Hasan al-Basri that he encountered seventy Companions who practiced it; fourth, the statement of Abu Hanifa that he only accepted it after clear evidence. The footnote clarifies that the wiping is valid only if the socks were put on after performing wudu (on a state of purity).

Key Terms
مسح على الخفين
خبر مشهور
رخصة
السفر
الحضر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Wiping over khuffs is a rejected innovation because it is not explicitly in the Quran.
Correction: The passage shows it is established by khabar mashhur and the consensus of the Companions, making it a valid sunna.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Hasan al-Basri say about wiping over khuffs?
A) He rejected it because it is not in the Quran.
B) He met seventy Companions who held that view.
C) He only permitted it for travelers.
D) He said Abu Hanifa was mistaken.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is a confirmed sunna supported by multiple authentic narrations and the practice of the Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a practice that is not in the Quran but is from authentic sunna, do you accept it with the same conviction as a Quranic command? What reluctance hides in your heart that makes you hesitate?

The Companions practiced wiping over khuffs despite it being an 'addition' to the Book. How many sunnas have you abandoned because they seemed unfamiliar or inconvenient? Will you commit today to revive one such sunna in your life?
?
Abu Hanifa waited until evidence came like daylight. Do you seek evidence for your religious practices, or do you follow inherited customs blindly? What one practice will you verify from the sunna starting tomorrow?

Testifying for the Ten and the General Rule
The author lists those testified for paradise and states the general principle for others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which specific individuals are testified to be in Paradise according to Sunni doctrine, and the general principle that for others we hope but do not judge.

Core Idea
Specific testimony for Paradise is limited to those explicitly named in revelation; for others we hope but do not judge.

This passage from the Aqidah al-Nasafiyyah addresses a delicate theological point: how do we know who is in Paradise? While we have explicit texts for some, for others we must maintain hope without certainty. The author lists the ten promised Paradise (here continuing with five), adds Fatima, Hasan, and Husayn from hadith, and then explains the general rule for the rest.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the list of names and the reasoning for Fatima, Hasan, and Husayn.
This passage is a continuation from an earlier listing of the ten.
2
Identify the specific testimonies
Find the five Companions from the ten promised Paradise: al-Zubayr, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Sa'id ibn Zayd, and Abu Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah. Then note Fatima, Hasan, and Husayn are added with explicit hadith evidence.
The author uses the phrase 'كذا وكذا' to indicate 'and likewise' for Fatima and the two grandsons.
3
Understand the general rule
Notice that after naming these individuals, the author states that for all other Companions we only mention them well and hope for them more than other believers, but we do not testify for or against any specific person individually.
This balances reverence for the Companions with theological caution.
4
Connect to broader doctrine
Reflect on why this distinction matters: It preserves the integrity of revelation by limiting specific testimony to where there is explicit text, and it maintains hope for believers without presuming upon Allah's judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والزبير في الجنة، وعبد الرحمن بن عوف فى الجنة، وسعد بن أبي وقاص فى الجنة، وسعيد بن زيد في الجنة، وأبو عبيدة بن الجراح في الجنة (١) وكذا وكذا نشهد بالجنة لفاطمة والحسن والحسين لما روى في الحديث الصحيح أن فاطمة سيدة نساء أهل الجنة، وأن الحسن والحسين سيدا شباب أهل الجنة وسائر الصحابة لا يذكرون إلا بخير ويرجى لهم أكثر مما يرجى لغيرهم من المؤمنين. ولا نشهد بالجنة أو النار لأحد بعينه، بل نشهد بأن المؤمنين من أهل الجنة والكافرين من أهل النار
And al-Zubayr is in Paradise, and 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf is in Paradise, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas is in Paradise, and Sa'id ibn Zayd is in Paradise, and Abu 'Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah is in Paradise (1). And likewise we testify to Paradise for Fatima and al-Hasan and al-Husayn because of what is narrated in the authentic hadith that Fatima is the mistress of the women of Paradise, and that al-Hasan and al-Husayn are the masters of the youth of Paradise. And the rest of the Companions are mentioned only with goodness, and we hope for them more than we hope for other believers. And we do not testify to Paradise or Hell for any specific person; rather we testify that the believers are among the people of Paradise and the disbelievers are among the people of Hell.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement on testifying for specific individuals being in Paradise. It begins by listing several of the ten Companions promised Paradise (al-'ashara al-mubashshara), namely al-Zubayr, 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Sa'id ibn Zayd, and Abu 'Ubayda ibn al-Jarrah. It then extends the testimony to Fatima, al-Hasan, and al-Husayn based on authentic hadith. After naming these individuals, the author states that for the remaining Companions, we only mention them well and hope for them more than for ordinary believers, but we do not testify for or against any specific person (except those named). The general principle is that believers as a whole are destined for Paradise and disbelievers for Hell, without assigning individuals to either fate without explicit scriptural evidence.

Correction: We testify specifically only for those with explicit texts (the ten and some family members), and for all other believers we hope for mercy without specific testimony.

The Ruling on Nabidh al-Tamr (Date Drink) Not Being Haram
The author states the Sunni position on nabidh al-tamr and explains its historical abrogation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunnah do not declare nabidh al-tamr (date drink) as haram, based on the principle of abrogation.

Core Idea
Nabidh al-tamr is not haram because its early prohibition was abrogated.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling from the chapter on samiyyat (hear-say matters) in the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah. The author clarifies that nabidh al-tamr, a drink made by steeping dates or raisins in water, is not considered prohibited, contrary to the view of the Rafidis. Understanding this ruling requires a brief look at its historical context and the principle of naskh (abrogation).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and its literal translation. Notice the concise style: the ruling, the definition, the reason for early prohibition, and the abrogation.
The passage is a single continuous statement.
2
Identify the key components
Break down the passage: 1) The ruling (not haram). 2) The definition of nabidh. 3) The historical reason for prohibition. 4) The abrogation. 5) The sectarian contrast.
3
Understand the role of abrogation
The passage explains that the initial prohibition was due to the jars being previously used for wine, not because of the drink itself. Then it was abrogated, so the ruling changed to non-prohibition.
This highlights the principle of naskh in Islamic law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القول في نبيذ التمر ولا نحرم نبيذ التمر وهو أن ينبذ تمر أو زبيب في الماء فيجعل في إناء من الخزف، فيحدث فيه لذع كما للفقاع، فكأنه نهى عن ذلك في بدء الإسلام لما كانت الجرار أواني الخمور، ثم نسخ فعدم تحريمه من قواعد أهل السنة والجماعة، خلافا للروافض.
The statement concerning nabidh al-tamr (date drink): And we do not declare nabidh al-tamr as prohibited. It is that dates or raisins are steeped in water, and placed in a vessel of ceramic, and a bite occurs in it like that of fuqqa' (a fermented drink). It is as if it was prohibited at the beginning of Islam because jars were vessels of wine, then it was abrogated. So its non-prohibition is from the principles of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, contrary to the Rafidis.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage defines nabidh al-tamr (a drink made by steeping dates or raisins in water) and explains its ruling. The author begins by stating the position of Ahl al-Sunnah: they do not declare it haram. He describes how nabidh is prepared in a ceramic vessel, and it develops a mild intoxicating effect (ludh') similar to fuqqa'. The author then provides historical context: it was prohibited at the beginning of Islam because the jars used were previously used for wine, but that prohibition was later abrogated (naskh). Therefore, not deeming it haram is a foundational principle of Ahl al-Sunnah, in contrast to the Rafidis (Shia) who consider it haram. The passage clarifies that the ruling is based on abrogation, and it emphasizes that this is a point of consensus among Sunnis.

Key Terms
نبيذ التمر
الفقاع
النسخ
الروافض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think nabidh is intoxicating and therefore haram.
Correction: The passage only deals with non-intoxicating nabidh; the mild 'ludh'' mentioned is not the same as intoxication. The prohibition was abrogated.

Checkpoint
Why was nabidh prohibited at the beginning of Islam according to the passage?
A) It was always intoxicating.
B) Because jars were vessels of wine.
C) Because dates were scarce.
D) It is a Rafidi innovation.

Key Takeaway
The non-prohibition of nabidh al-tamr is a Sunni principle based on abrogation of an earlier ruling.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Ruling on Intoxicating Nabidh
The author distinguishes the intoxicating case where nabidh becomes haram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that intoxicating nabidh is haram in both small and large quantities, based on the principle that any intoxicant is forbidden.

Core Idea
Intoxicating nabidh is haram in any amount, even if a small amount does not intoxicate.

In previous lessons, we learned that non-intoxicating nabidh is permissible. However, if nabidh becomes strong and intoxicating, a different ruling applies. This passage clarifies that many scholars from Ahl al-Sunnah consider both small and large amounts of such intoxicating nabidh as haram.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the author's point.
Notice the contrast with the previous ruling.
2
Identify the condition for haram
Find the condition that makes nabidh become haram: when it becomes strong (ishtadda) and intoxicating (muskira).
3
Understand the ruling on quantity
Note that the ruling applies to both small and large amounts, a key principle of Islamic law regarding intoxicants.
This is based on the authority of many Ahl al-Sunnah scholars.
4
Connect to broader principle
Reflect on the general rule: any intoxicating substance is haram in any quantity, regardless of whether a small amount intoxicates.
This prevents gradual consumption leading to intoxication.
5
Address common misunderstanding
Contrast this with the view that all nabidh is haram. This passage only makes intoxicating nabidh haram, not non-intoxicating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا بخلاف ما إذا اشتد فصار مسكرا، فإن القول بحرمة قليله وكثيره، مما ذهب إليه كثير من أهل السنة والجماعة.
And this is different from when it becomes strong and becomes intoxicating; for the statement that its small amount and large amount are prohibited is something that many of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah have held.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage provides the exception to the previous ruling on nabidh. While non-intoxicating nabidh is not haram, if the drink becomes strong (ishtadda) and becomes intoxicating (muskira), then it becomes haram. Importantly, the author notes that many of Ahl al-Sunnah hold that both small and large amounts of such intoxicating nabidh are haram, even if a small amount does not intoxicate. This is a standard principle in Islamic jurisprudence: any intoxicating substance is haram in any quantity. The passage shows that the ruling is not based on the substance itself (dates or raisins) but on the property of intoxication.

Key Terms
مسكر
حرمة قليله وكثيره

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All nabidh (date drink) is haram.
Correction: Only intoxicating nabidh is haram; non-intoxicating nabidh is permissible.

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible in small amounts.
B) Its small and large amounts are haram.
C) It is only haram if it becomes wine.
D) It is halal if not drunk to intoxication.

Key Takeaway
Intoxicating nabidh is haram in any quantity, according to the dominant Sunni view.

Do the Deeds of the Living Benefit the Deceased?
Argues that prayers and charity benefit the deceased, citing hadith against the Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the orthodox Sunni position that supplications and charity benefit the deceased, supported by authentic hadith that refute the Mu'tazila denial.

Core Idea
Prayers and charity of the living cross the grave and benefit the dead.

This lesson addresses a comforting question: Can our prayers and charity help our deceased loved ones? The Mu'tazila denied this, arguing each soul is only responsible for its own deeds. In contrast, the Sunni position is supported by authentic hadith and continuous practice of the early Muslim community. We will examine the key proofs from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
Read the opening lines to see the author's main assertion: supplication and charity from the living benefit the deceased.
Notice the phrase 'نفع لهم' — benefit for them.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila objection
Look for the arguments of the Mu'tazila: the decree does not change, each soul is pledged for its own deeds, and a person is rewarded only for his own work.
This is the opposing view the author refutes.
3
Examine the first proof: intercession of 100
Read the hadith about a hundred Muslims praying for a deceased person. Note that their intercession is accepted, showing benefit to the dead.
This hadith directly challenges the Mu'tazila position.
4
Examine the second proof: charity of water
Read the story of Sa'd ibn 'Ubada digging a well for his mother. The Prophet's approval shows charity benefits the deceased.
The well was dedicated to the mother of Sa'd.
5
Reflect on the continuous practice
The author notes that the Salaf transmitted this practice; if it had no benefit, it would be meaningless.
This is a practical argument from tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في دعاء الأحياء للأموات وتصدقهم عنهم وفى دعاء الأحياء للأموات وتصدقهم أى تصدق الأحياء. ( عنهم) أى عن الأموات . (نفع لهم ) أى للأموات، خلافا للمعتزلة تمسكا بأن القضاء لا يتبدل وكل نفس مرهونة بما كسبت والمرء مجزى بعمله لا بعمل غيره . ولنا : ما ورد في الأحاديث الصحاح من الدعاء للأموات ، خصوصا في صلاة الجنازة. وقد توارثه السلف فلو لم يكن للأموات نفع فيه لما كان له معنى . قال : ( ما من ميت يصلى عليه أمة من المسلمين يبلغون مائة كلهم يشفعون له إلا شفعوا فيه وعن سعد بن عبادة أنه قال : يا رسول الله إن أم سعد ماتت . فأى الصدقة أفضل ؟ قال : الماء فحفر بئرا . وقال : هذه لأم سعد
The discussion concerning the supplication of the living for the dead and their charity on their behalf. And regarding the supplication of the living for the dead and their charity, i.e., the charity of the living. 'On their behalf' (anhum), i.e., on behalf of the dead. 'Benefit for them' (naf' lahum), i.e., for the dead, contrary to the Mu'tazila, who adhere to the argument that the decree does not change and every soul is pledged for what it has earned, and a person is rewarded for his own deed, not for the deed of another. And we have what is reported in the authentic hadiths concerning supplication for the dead, especially in the funeral prayer. And the Salaf have transmitted it; if there were no benefit for the dead in it, it would have no meaning. He said: 'There is no deceased person over whom a community of Muslims prays, reaching one hundred, all of them interceding for him, except that they are granted intercession for him.' And from Sa'd ibn 'Ubada that he said: 'O Messenger of Allah, the mother of Sa'd has died. Which charity is best?' He said: 'Water.' So he dug a well and said: 'This is for the mother of Sa'd.'
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage defends the orthodox position that the supplications (du'a) and charity (sadaqa) of the living benefit the deceased. It states that the Mu'tazila deny this, arguing that the divine decree (qada') does not change, that every soul is pledged for its own deeds, and that a person is only requited for his own work, not another's. In response, the author cites two proofs from authentic hadith. First, the hadith that if a hundred Muslims pray for a deceased person and intercede, their intercession is granted. Second, the hadith of Sa'd ibn 'Ubada who asked the Prophet about the best charity for his deceased mother; the Prophet advised giving water, so Sa'd dug a well and dedicated it to her. These narrations show that the acts of the living can benefit the dead. Moreover, this practice has been transmitted by the Salaf (predecessors) continuously; if it had no benefit, it would be meaningless.

Key Terms

صدقة
أموات
معتزلة
شفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only one's own deeds matter; the deeds of others cannot benefit the deceased.
Correction: The hadith of the hundred intercessors and the well of Sa'd show that supplication and charity of the living do benefit the deceased.

Checkpoint
What argument do the Mu'tazila use to deny that the deeds of the living benefit the dead?
A) The dead cannot sense anything.
B) Each soul is pledged for what it has earned and a person is rewarded only for his own deed.
C) The Prophet forbade supplication for the dead.
D) The Quran states that no one can bear another's burden.

Key Takeaway
Supplications and charity from the living benefit the deceased, as confirmed by authentic hadith and continuous practice of the early Muslim community.

Benefit of Supplication and Charity for the Dead
Proves that prayers and charity from the living benefit the dead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the living's supplication and charity benefit the dead, based on scriptural evidence and contrary to the Mu'tazila position.

Core Idea
Prayers and charity from the living reach the dead — affirmed by sound hadiths and Salaf practice.

The question of whether our deeds can benefit the deceased touches on divine justice and mercy. The Mu'tazila argued that each soul is only recompensed for its own work, but the Sunni position, grounded in hadith and the consensus of the Salaf, holds that supplication and charity do benefit the dead. This lesson presents the key evidence from the source.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila objection
Read the passage to identify the Mu'tazila argument: decree does not change, each soul is pledged for its deeds, and a person is only recompensed for his own work. Ask yourself why this seems logical.
The objection is based on rational principles of justice.
2
Examine the Sunni response – the hadith evidence
The author cites multiple hadiths: the funeral prayer with 100 intercessors, the well dug for Umm Sa'd, supplication repelling calamity, and the scholar passing by a graveyard. Notice how each hadith directly demonstrates benefit.
The Salaf's continuous practice reinforces the acceptance of these hadiths.
3
Reflect on the implications for practice
Consider how this doctrine impacts our actions: we should supplicate for the deceased, give charity on their behalf, and attend funeral prayers. This is a source of hope and communal responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في دعاء الأحياء للأموات وتصدقهم أى تصدق الأحياء. عنهم أى عن الأموات. نفع لهم أى للأموات، خلافا للمعتزلة تمسكا بأن القضاء لا يتبدل وكل نفس مرهونة بما كسبت والمرء مجزى بعمله لا بعمل غيره. ولنا : ما ورد في الأحاديث الصحاح من الدعاء للأموات، خصوصا في صلاة الجنازة. وقد توارثه السلف فلو لم يكن للأموات نفع فيه لما كان له معنى. قال : ما من ميت يصلى عليه أمة من المسلمين يبلغون مائة كلهم يشفعون له إلا شفعوا فيه وعن سعد بن عبادة أنه قال : يا رسول الله إن أم سعد ماتت. فأى الصدقة أفضل ؟ قال : الماء فحفر بئرا. وقال : هذه لأم سعد وقال عليه السلام : الدعاء يرد البلاء والصدقة تطفئ غضب الرب وقال عليه السلام : إن العالم والمتعلم إذا مرا على قرية، فإن يرفع العذاب عن مقبرة تلك القرية أربعين يوما والأحاديث والآثار فى هذا الباب، أكثر من أن تحصى
Speech about the living supplicating for the dead and their charity—i.e., the charity of the living—on their behalf, i.e., on behalf of the dead, benefiting them, i.e., the dead, contrary to the Mu'tazila who cling to the fact that decree does not change and every soul is pledged for what it earned, and a person is recompensed for his own deed, not for another's deed. Our evidence: what has been reported in sound hadiths about supplication for the dead, especially in the funeral prayer, and the predecessors transmitted it; if there were no benefit for the dead in it, it would have no meaning. He said: 'No dead person is prayed over by a community of Muslims reaching one hundred, all interceding for him, except that they are granted intercession for him.' And from Sa'd ibn 'Ubada that he said: 'O Messenger of God, my mother Umm Sa'd has died. Which charity is best?' He said: 'Water.' So he dug a well and said: 'This is for Umm Sa'd.' And he, peace be upon him, said: 'Supplication repels calamity and charity extinguishes the wrath of the Lord.' And he, peace be upon him, said: 'Indeed, when a scholar and a student pass by a village, the punishment is lifted from the graveyard of that village for forty days.' The hadiths and reports in this chapter are too many to count.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a proof that the supplication and charity of the living benefit the dead, contrary to the Mu'tazila. The author first explains the phrase 'supplication of the living for the dead and their charity on their behalf' as benefiting the dead. Then he presents the Mu'tazila objection: they argue that the divine decree is unchangeable, each soul is pledged for its own deeds, and a person is only recompensed for his own work, not another's. The author then provides evidence from sound hadiths: the practice of supplication in funeral prayer, which the Salaf transmitted and which would be meaningless if it had no benefit; the hadith that a hundred intercessors are granted their intercession; the story of Sa'd ibn 'Ubada digging a well for his mother on the Prophet's advice; and the hadith that supplication repels calamity and charity extinguishes God's wrath, and that the passage of a scholar and student lifts punishment from a nearby graveyard. The author concludes that such hadiths and reports are too numerous to count, establishing the doctrine.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the benefit of charity and supplication for the dead contradicts personal accountability, so it is not possible.
Correction: The author shows that such benefit is established by multiple authentic hadiths and the continuous practice of the Salaf, overriding the rational objection.

D) The fact that the dead ask for it.

Key Takeaway
The living can benefit the dead through supplication and charity, as proven by multiple prophetic traditions and the continuous practice of the early Muslims.

God Answers Prayers: Promise and Conditions
Affirms God's response to prayer and lists conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God answers prayers and the conditions for their acceptance, including sincerity, purity of intention, and presence of heart.

Core Idea
God is Generous and answers prayers when offered with sincerity and trust.

This lesson examines the foundational Islamic belief that God responds to those who call upon Him. The author cites the Quran and hadith to establish that God answers prayers, but also emphasises that there are conditions: the prayer must avoid sin, severance of kinship, and impatience, and must be offered with certainty and attentiveness.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening affirmation
Read the first part of the Arabic passage where the author states that God answers prayers and fulfills needs, and note the Quranic verse cited.
2
Understand the hadith conditions
Examine the two hadiths: the first forbidding sin and severance, the second describing God's generosity. Consider how these shape the etiquette of supplication.
3
Focus on internal conditions
The author then emphasizes sincerity, purity of intention, and presence of heart. Read the hadith 'Supplicate God while you are certain of the answer' and note the warning against heedlessness.
4
Reflect on application
Think about how these conditions relate to your own practice of dua. What does it mean to pray with certainty?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والله - تعالى - يجيب الدعوات، ويقضى الحاجات لقوله تعالى: ادْعُونِي أَستجب لكم (غافر: ٦٠) ولقوله - عليه السلام : لا يستجاب للعبد ما لم يدع بإثم أو قطيعة رحم ما لم يستعجل ولقوله - عليه السلام : إن ربكم حيى كريم، يستحى من عبده إذا رفع يديه إليه أن يردهما صفرا . واعلم أن العمدة فى ذلك صدق النية وخلوص الطوية وحضور القلب لقوله عليه السلام : ادعوا الله وأنتم موقنون بالإجابة . واعلموا : أن الله لا يستجيب الدعاء من قلب غافل لاه. واختلف المشايخ فى أنه هل يجوز أن يقال : يستجاب دعاء الكافر؟ فمنعه الجمهور، لقوله تعالى : وَمَا دُعَاءُ الْكَافِرِينَ إِلا فِي ضلال (غافر: ٥٠) ولأنه لا يدعو الله، لأنه لا يعرفه، ولأنه وإن أقر به، لما وصفه بما لا يليق به فقد نقض إقراره . وما روى فى الحديث : من أن دعوة المظلوم وإن كان كافرا، تستجاب فمحمول على كفران النعمة .
And God—exalted is He—answers prayers and fulfills needs, due to His saying: 'Call upon Me; I will respond to you' (Quran 40:60), and due to his—peace be upon him—saying: 'The servant's prayer is not answered so long as he does not supplicate for sin or severing of kinship, and does not become impatient,' and due to his—peace be upon him—saying: 'Indeed, your Lord is Generous and Kind, He is shy to send back empty the hands of His servant when he raises them to Him.' And know that the foundation in that is sincerity of intention, purity of resolve, and presence of heart, due to his—peace be upon him—saying: 'Supplicate God while you are certain of the answer,' and 'Know that God does not answer the prayer from a heedless, distracted heart.' And the scholars differed on whether it is permissible to say that the prayer of a disbeliever is answered. The majority forbade it, due to His saying: 'And the prayer of the disbelievers is only in error' (Quran 40:50), and because he does not supplicate to God, since he does not know Him, and because even if he acknowledges Him, since he describes Him with what does not befit Him, he has contradicted his acknowledgment. And what is reported in the hadith that the prayer of the oppressed, even if he is a disbeliever, is answered—that is interpreted as [disbelief in] ingratitude for blessings.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal elucidation of God's response to prayer and the conditions for its acceptance. The author begins by affirming that God answers prayers and fulfills needs, citing a Quranic verse (40:60) and two hadiths: one stating that the servant's prayer is accepted unless it involves sin or severing family ties, and another stating that God is too generous to send back empty the hands of a supplicant. The author then emphasizes that the essential conditions for acceptance are sincerity of intention, purity of resolve, and presence of heart, quoting the hadith 'Supplicate God while you are certain of the answer' and that God does not answer the prayer from a heedless heart. Next, the passage addresses a point of disagreement among scholars: whether it is permissible to say that the prayer of a disbeliever is answered. The majority hold it is not, because the Quran says that the prayer of disbelievers is only in error, and the disbeliever does not truly supplicate God due to ignorance or misdescription. The apparent hadith that the prayer of the oppressed, even if a disbeliever, is answered is interpreted as referring specifically to ingratitude for blessings (kufran al-ni'ma) rather than outright disbelief in God.

Key Terms
دعاء
إجابة
صدق النية
حضور القلب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God answers any prayer regardless of the supplicant's inner state.
Correction: The passage shows that God answers prayers only when they are free from sin, offered with sincerity, and with a present heart.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is a necessary condition for a prayer to be answered?
A) The prayer must be in a mosque
B) The supplicant must have a present heart and certainty
C) The supplicant must be a scholar
D) The prayer must be at night

Key Takeaway
God answers prayers when they are offered with sincerity, avoidance of sin, and a heart fully present.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you raise your hands in dua, do you truly believe that God is shy to send them back empty? If so, why does your heart often feel uncertain or distracted? Identify the one distraction that most often steals your presence of heart, and commit to a specific step to remove it before your next prayer.
?
You know that God does not answer a prayer from a heedless heart. But have you ever paused to ask yourself: why do you let your heart wander? What does that wandering say about your trust in God's ability to respond? Sit with that discomfort and write down one concrete change you will make to guard your heart during supplication.
?
The passage teaches that patience is a condition for acceptance. Think of a prayer you have been waiting on for a long time. Has impatience ever crept into your heart? How has that impatience affected your relationship with God? Will you now consciously replace that impatience with certainty that God has heard you, even if the answer is delayed? Make a firm resolve.

The Prayer of the Disbeliever: A Scholarly Disagreement
Scholarly disagreement on whether disbelievers' prayers are answered

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the majority of scholars hold that a disbeliever's prayer is not answered and how the hadith about the oppressed is interpreted.

Core Idea
The prayer of a disbeliever is not accepted because they do not truly know God.

A point of debate among scholars is whether the prayer of a disbeliever is answered. The majority opinion, based on the Quran and theological reasoning, holds that it is not. This lesson explains the reasoning and addresses a hadith that seems to suggest otherwise, showing how it is interpreted as referring to ingratitude for blessings rather than disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the disagreement
Begin by reading the Arabic passage about the scholars differing on whether the prayer of a disbeliever is answered.
2
Understand the majority's position
The majority forbids saying it is answered. Note the three evidences: Quranic verse, the disbeliever's ignorance of God, and his contradictory descriptions of God.
3
Examine the problematic hadith
The hadith about the oppressed disbeliever seems to contradict the majority. Read how the author resolves it: it is interpreted as 'ingratitude for blessings' (kufran al-ni'ma) rather than actual disbelief.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why correct belief about God matters for the acceptance of prayer. The disbeliever's prayer is in error because his conception of God is wrong.

And what is reported in the hadith that the prayer of the oppressed, even if he is a disbeliever, is answered—that is interpreted as [disbelief in] ingratitude for blessings.

The Major Signs of the Hour: Possibility and Certainty
The author enumerates the major signs of the Hour as reported by the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the major signs of the Hour are possible matters reported by the truthful Prophet and must be accepted as true.

Core Idea
The signs of the Hour are real and possible events foretold by the Prophet.

Eschatology in Islam includes specific events that must occur before the final Hour. The Prophet (peace be upon him) informed his companions of these signs, and they are recorded in authentic hadith. This passage provides both a general affirmation of their truth and a detailed list from the Prophet himself, grounding our belief in the certainty of his words.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the overall meaning.
2
Identify the key claim
Notice the assertion that the signs are 'possible matters' and 'true because the truthful one informed of them.' This is the theological foundation.
3
List the signs from the hadith
The hadith of Hudhayfa ibn Asid enumerates ten signs. Identify each one and note that they include cosmic, terrestrial, and human events.
Look for 'the smoke, the Dajjal, the Beast...'
4
Reflect on the doctrinal implication
Ask yourself: why does the author insist on the possibility of these signs? The commentary explains that kalam principles require affirming anything possible that the truthful Prophet reported.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صالة من ما أخبر به أشراط الساعة (وما أخبر به النبي - عليه السلام - من أشراط الساعة أى علاماتها . (من خروج الدجال ودابة الأرض ويأجوج ومأجوج ونزول عيسى - عليه السلام - من السماء وطلوع الشمس من مغربها ، فهو حق لأنها أمور ممكنة، أخبر بها الصادق قال حذيفة بن أسيد الغفارى: اطلع رسول الله علينا ونحن نتذاكر. فقال : « ما تذاكرون ؟ ) قلنا نذكر الساعة . قال : إنها لن تقوم حتى تروا قبلها عشر آيات ) فذكر الدخان والدجال والدابة وطلوع الشمس من مغربها ونزول عيسى ابن مريم ويأجوج ومأجوج وثلاثة خسوف : خسف بالمشرق وخسف بالمغرب، وخسف بجزيرة العرب. وآخر ذلك ،نار، تخرج من اليمن تطرد الناس إلى محشرهم
A section on what he informed of the signs of the Hour. And what the Prophet (peace be upon him) informed of the signs of the Hour, i.e., its indicators: from the emergence of the Dajjal, the Beast of the Earth, Gog and Magog, the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him) from the sky, and the rising of the sun from its west — it is true, because they are possible matters, and the truthful one informed of them. Hudhayfa ibn Asid al-Ghifari said: The Messenger of God looked upon us while we were discussing. He said: 'What are you discussing?' We said: We are mentioning the Hour. He said: 'It will not occur until you see before it ten signs.' Then he mentioned the smoke, the Dajjal, the Beast, the rising of the sun from its west, the descent of Jesus son of Mary, Gog and Magog, three landslides: a landslide in the east, a landslide in the west, and a landslide in the Arabian Peninsula. And the last of that is a fire that comes out from Yemen, driving the people to their gathering place.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage affirms the truth of the major signs of the Hour (ashrat al-sa'ah) as reported by the Prophet. It begins by stating that whatever the Prophet informed of these signs is true (haqq) because they are possible matters (umur mumkinah) and were reported by the truthful one (al-sadiq). The passage then lists the signs: the Dajjal, the Beast of the Earth, Gog and Magog, the descent of Jesus, the sun rising from the west. It then cites the hadith of Hudhayfa ibn Asid al-Ghifari, in which the Prophet enumerates ten specific signs that must appear before the Hour: the smoke, the Dajjal, the Beast, the rising of the sun from the west, the descent of Jesus, Gog and Magog, and three landslides (khusuf) — one in the east, one in the west, and one in the Arabian Peninsula — and finally a fire that will drive the people to their gathering place (mahshar). The passage thus provides both a summary list and a detailed hadith, emphasizing the certainty of these events because they are from the truthful Prophet.

ashrat al-sa'ah
Dajjal
dabbat al-ard
Yajuj and Majuj
nuzul 'Isa
khusuf

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Seven
B) Ten
C) Eight
D) Nine

Key Takeaway
The major signs of the Hour are rationally possible events that the truthful Prophet reported, and they are accepted as true and literal by the Ahl al-Sunnah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that the fire from Yemen could appear today, driving people to the gathering place, what would you change about how you spend your next hour? Be specific: what worry, habit, or conversation would you drop, and what act of obedience would you prioritize?
?
The Prophet truthfully informed of these ten signs. But you also believe he truthfully informed of every command and prohibition. Which command of the Prophet have you been neglecting, thinking it is small or optional? How does the certainty of these signs make that neglect feel now?
?
The signs are all possible events—none are impossible. What 'impossible' barrier in your own life (a sin you think you can't leave, a good deed you think you can't start) would you reclassify as 'possible' if you truly trusted the One who controls all events? Will you ask Allah for that change tonight?

The Signs of the Hour: Truth and Reality
Confirms the reality of the signs of the Hour and lists them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the signs of the Hour are real and possible events, confirmed by authentic hadith, and you will be able to list the ten major signs mentioned by the Prophet.

Core Idea
The Prophet's reports about the Hour are true because he is truthful and the events are possible.

This passage from the creed affirms that everything the Prophet (peace be upon him) informed us about the signs of the Hour is true. It provides a list of major signs, including the Dajjal, the Beast, and the rising of the sun from the west, and supports them with a hadith from Hudhayfah that enumerates ten portents. Understanding this teaches us to believe in the unseen events that will precede the Day of Judgment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the author's concise style and the inclusion of a hadith.
2
Identify the ten signs
From the hadith of Hudhayfah, list the ten major signs of the Hour as mentioned by the Prophet. This helps you remember and believe in them.
The signs include the smoke, Dajjal, beast, sun rising from west, descent of Jesus, Gog and Magog, three sinkings, and a fire.
3
Understand the reasoning
Why are these signs true? The author gives two reasons: they are possible (mumkin) events, and they were reported by the truthful Prophet (al-sadiq). Reflect on how this reasoning strengthens faith in the unseen.
This logical reasoning is a hallmark of Sunni creedal works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما أخبر به النبي - عليه السلام - من أشراط الساعة أى علاماتها . من خروج الدجال ودابة الأرض ويأجوج ومأجوج ونزول عيسى - عليه السلام - من السماء وطلوع الشمس من مغربها ، فهو حق لأنها أمور ممكنة، أخبر بها الصادق قال حذيفة بن أسيد الغفارى: اطلع رسول الله علينا ونحن نتذاكر. فقال : « ما تذاكرون ؟ » قلنا نذكر الساعة . قال : « إنها لن تقوم حتى تروا قبلها عشر آيات » فذكر الدخان والدجال والدابة وطلوع الشمس من مغربها ونزول عيسى ابن مريم ويأجوج ومأجوج وثلاثة خسوف : خسف بالمشرق وخسف بالمغرب، وخسف بجزيرة العرب. وآخر ذلك نار تخرج من اليمن تطرد الناس إلى محشرهم . والأحاديث الصحاح في هذه الأشراط كثيرة جدا. فقد رويت أحاديث وآثار فى تفاصيلها وكيفياتها تطلب من كتب التفسير والسير والتواريخ .
And what the Prophet (peace be upon him) informed of the portents of the Hour, i.e., its signs, such as the emergence of the Dajjal, the Beast of the Earth, Gog and Magog, the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him) from heaven, and the rising of the sun from its west – it is true because they are possible matters, reported by the truthful one. Hudhayfah ibn Usayd al-Ghifari said: The Messenger of Allah looked upon us while we were conversing and said: 'What are you discussing?' We said: We are mentioning the Hour. He said: 'It will not be established until you see before it ten signs.' Then he mentioned the smoke, the Dajjal, the beast, the rising of the sun from its west, the descent of Jesus son of Mary, Gog and Magog, and three sinkings: a sinking in the east, a sinking in the west, and a sinking in the Arabian Peninsula, and the last of that is a fire that will issue from Yemen driving the people to their place of assembly. And the authentic hadiths concerning these portents are very numerous. Indeed, hadiths and reports have been narrated concerning their details and modalities; they are sought from books of exegesis, biographies, and histories.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a confirmation of the eschatological signs of the Hour. It begins by stating that everything the Prophet informed about the signs (ashrat al-sa'ah) is true. The author provides a list of specific signs: the Dajjal, the Beast, Gog and Magog, the descent of Jesus, and the sun rising from the west. The reason given for their truth is that they are possible (mumkin) events, and they were reported by one who is truthful (al-sadiq, i.e., the Prophet). Then a hadith from Hudhayfah is cited, in which the Prophet enumerates ten major signs, including the smoke, three sinkings, and a fire. The passage concludes that authentic hadiths on this topic are abundant, and their details are found in tafsir, sirah, and historical works. The author does not discuss the theological implications of these signs beyond affirming their truth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think the signs of the Hour are metaphorical or impossible.
Correction: The passage states they are possible (mumkin) events reported by the truthful Prophet, so they are real and will occur.

Checkpoint

A) They are mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The signs of the Hour are real and true because they are possible events and reported by the truthful Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) was absolutely truthful about these future events. Do you live with the same certainty that the signs are real? If not, what is holding you back from full conviction, and what will you do about it today?
?
Imagine you wake up tomorrow and see the sun rising from the west. Would your life have been lived in preparation for that moment? What specific habit or attitude do you need to change to be ready?
?
The signs are possible matters in the power of Allah. Do you truly submit your mind to the possibility of these events, or do you secretly doubt because they seem extraordinary? What would change if you believed with complete certainty?
